202 of 594 DOCUMENTS



McGhee v. Ark. State Bd. of Collection Agencies


No. 08-164


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


375 Ark. 52; 289 S.W.3d 18; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 745



November 6, 2008, Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. 2003-4837, HON. BARRY A. SIMS, JUDGE, REVERSED AND REMANDED.
McGhee v. Ark. State Bd. of Collection Agencies, 368 Ark. 60, 243 S.W.3d 278, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 568 (Ark., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order from the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which, in their declaratory judgment action against appellees, the Arkansas State Board of Collection Agencies and its board members, held that the Arkansas Check-Cashers Act, Ark. Code Ann. §§ 23-52-101- 23-52-117 (2000 & Supp. 2007), was constitutional. The Arkansas Financial Services Association was permitted to intervene in the matter.


OVERVIEW: Appellants brought an action against appellees, alleging that all transactions under the Act involved interest rates that violated the usury provision of Ark. Const. art. 19, § 13. Appellants sought a declaratory judgment that the Act was unconstitutional. The trial court denied appellants' request for a declaratory judgment and found that the Act was constitutional. On appeal, the court found that declaratory relief was proper in the case under Ark. Code Ann. § 16-111-104 (2006). A justiciable controversy was present between appellants and the Board as to the implementation, application, and effect of the Act. Further, the court found that the Act clearly authorized usurious interest rates. Sample contracts contained in the record reflected annual percentage rates (APRs) ranging from 168.20 percent to 558.71 percent. Such rates of interest were clearly and unmistakably usurious and in violation of Ark. Const. art. 19, § 13(a), (b). The Act's provisions concerning the business of check-cashing and the business of deferred-presentment options were so intertwined that severance was inappropriate. The court declared the entirety of the Act unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.


 

203 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Anglin v. Johnson Reg'l Med. Ctr.


No. 08-453


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


375 Ark. 10; 289 S.W.3d 28; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 704



November 6, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE JOHNSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV2006-119, HON. DENNIS CHARLES SUTTERFIELD, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the husband and special administrator of a deceased patient's estate, challenged a judgment of the Johnson County Circuit Court (Arkansas) granting summary judgment, under Ark. R. Civ. P. 56, in favor of appellee medical center on the grounds of charitable immunity, in the husband's wrongful death suit against the medical center.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that the medical center was entitled to both governmental and charitable immunity. The court found that the medical center's charter limited it to charitable or elemosynary purposes, that the charter contained a not-for-profit limitation, and that the medical center provided services free of charge to those unable to pay. The issues regarding the medical center's profit and its practice of filing suit to collect unpaid medical bills were not matters of disputed fact, but rather they were differing legal interpretations of undisputed facts. The existence of profit was not determinative of charitable status. Because there were no disputed facts, the trial court correctly determined, as a matter of law and under Ark. R. Civ. P. 56, that the medical center was a charity entitled to immunity. The husband was not unconstitutionally denied his right to a jury trial, under Ark. Const. art. 2, § 7, because no factual issues existed in the case. The court also held that the husband was not entitled to relate-back to his first amended complaint in an attempt to name the medical center's liability insurance carrier as a defendant because the complaint was a nullity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

204 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Benton County Stone, Inc. v. Benton County Planning Bd.


No. 08-291


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 519; 288 S.W.3d 653; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 760



October 30, 2008, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF BENTON COUNTY, ARKANSAS, NO. CV-06-126-3, HONORABLE JAY T. FINCH, CIRCUIT JUDGE.
Duffield v. Benton County Stone Co., 369 Ark. 314, 254 S.W.3d 726, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 673 (Ark., 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of an order from the Benton County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which upheld the denial of an application for a permit to build a rock quarry by appellee, an appeal review board of a county planning board.


OVERVIEW: The owner sought a permit to build a rock quarry. The planning board granted its approval. However, a group of landowners appealed the decision to the county appeal review board. The review board reversed the planning board's decision, finding that the proposed development was not compatible with surrounding land uses. The trial court upheld the decision of the review board. On appeal, the owner argued that the planning board's ordinance concerning large scale plan requirements, Benton County, Ark., Ordinance § 2(B)(4), was void for vagueness. The ordinance required that a proposed development be consistent and compatible with existing development and the environment. The court found that "compatible" had a plain and ordinary meaning. The three clauses that followed the "compatibility" requirement were to be considered as factors that guided the exercise of the review board's discretion. Their presence did not render the mandatory clause unconstitutionally void. The record was replete with evidence that the county considered the compatibility of the owner's proposed quarry in the context of the ordinance's discretionary restraints.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

205 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Johnson Custom Homes


No. 07-1101


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 457; 288 S.W.3d 607; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 558



October 23, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE ARKANSAS WORKERS' COMPENSATION COMMISSION. F407233.
Williams v. Johnson Custom Homes, 100 Ark. App. 60, 264 S.W.3d 569, 2007 Ark. App. LEXIS 678 (2007)



DISPOSITION: WORKERS' COMPENSATION COMMISSION REVERSED AND REMANDED; COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of an order from the Arkansas Court of Appeals, which upheld an order from the Arkansas Workers' Compensation Commission denying his claim for workers' compensation benefits from appellees, a home builder, an insurer, and an Ohio company.


OVERVIEW: The employee was hired as a crew leader by the home builder. The employee received paychecks from various companies. In early 2004, the employee's paychecks came from the Ohio company. The employee was injured on the job in April 2004. He received biweekly temporary total disability benefits for approximately 17 to 18 weeks from the Ohio Bureau of Workers' Compensation. He initiated a claim for benefits in Arkansas in July 2004. The Commission denied the claim, finding that he was estopped by the election-of-remedies doctrine. The court of appeals upheld the decision. On review, the court held that the factual issue of whether the employee knowingly initiated a claim for benefits in Ohio and knowingly received benefits from Ohio, did not amount to an election of remedies that precluded the possibility of receiving benefits under Arkansas workers' compensation laws. Further, an agreement signed by the employee to select the State of Ohio as the state of exclusive remedy was void and unenforceable under both the Arkansas Workers' Compensation Law, Ark. Code Ann. § 11-9-108 (2002), and the Arkansas Insurance Code, Ark. Code Ann. § 23-92-409(c)(4)(A) (2004).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

206 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. McGraw


No. 08-372


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 483; 288 S.W.3d 623; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 553



October 23, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Mercy Health Sys. of Northwest Ark. v. McGraw, 2013 Ark. App. 61, 2013 Ark. App. LEXIS 57 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE BENTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV-2004-1775-4, HON. JOHN R. SCOTT, JUDGE.
McGraw v. Jones, 367 Ark. 138, 238 S.W.3d 15, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 407 (Ark., 2006)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice case, plaintiffs, a patient and his wife, appealed a judgment of the Benton County Circuit Court (Arkansas) in favor of defendant doctor, arguing that, because the case had been remanded for a trial on the issue of damages only, the circuit court erred in permitting the doctor to introduce evidence on the issue of proximate causation.


OVERVIEW: The patient and his wife filed a medical malpractice case, and a default judgment was rendered against the doctor, who challenged the entry of a judgment against her in the amount of $500,000. While the court affirmed entry of the default judgment, it vacated the damages award and remanded the case for a trial on that issue. At trial, judgment was rendered in favor of the doctor. In reviewing the appeal of the patient and his wife, the court ruled that the circuit court abused its discretion in permitting the doctor to introduce evidence regarding proximate causation because causation was an element of liability, not of damages. The doctor was found liable for medical malpractice by the entry of the default judgment against her. She was entitled to a hearing to determine the amount of damages resulting from her malpractice, but she was not entitled to challenge her liability during the hearing on damages. While the doctor had the right to cross-examine the patient's witnesses, to introduce evidence in mitigation of damages, and to question on appeal the sufficiency of the evidence, she could not be permitted to introduce evidence to defeat the patient's cause of action.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new hearing to determine the amount of damages.

Burchette v. Sex Offender Screening & Risk Assessment Comm.


No. 07-408


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 467; 288 S.W.3d 614; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 551



October 23, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Burchette v. Sex Offender Screening & Risk Assessment Comm., 2008 Ark. LEXIS 772 (Ark., Dec. 4, 2008)
Rehearing denied by Burchette v. Sex Offender Screening & Risk Assessment Comm., 2008 Ark. LEXIS 773 (Ark., Dec. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV 06-4008, HON. ALICE GRAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant alleged offender challenged a decision from the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which, after a remand, affirmed a Level 3 sex offender assessment and rejected the offender's due process arguments relating to appellee Sex Offender Assessment Committee (SOAC).


OVERVIEW: The offender entered guilty pleas to one count of sexual assault in the fourth degree and two counts of sexual indecency with a child. Thereafter, an assessment was conducted by the Sex Offender Screening and Risk Assessment program (SOSRA). The offender was later notified that he was a Level 3 offender. The SOAC upheld this assessment. The offender sought judicial review, the case was remanded, and the Level 3 assessment was again upheld. This appeal followed. In affirming, the supreme court noted that the offender was not entitled to a hearing under the Arkansas Sex Offender Registration Act of 1997, Ark. Code Ann. §§ 12-12-901 to 12-12-920 (2003 & Supp. 2007). He contended that he had a constitutional due process right to receive such. In rejecting this argument, the supreme court noted that the offender had a meaningful opportunity to be heard under the facts of this case because of the procedure, which included a face-to-face SOSRA interview and the SOAC review. Therefore, the offender's procedural due-process rights under either the Arkansas or United States Constitutions were not violated by denying him a second face-to-face interview before SOAC.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Wal-Mart Stores, Inc. v. D.A.N. Joint Venture III, L.P.


No. 08-434


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 489; 288 S.W.3d 627; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 552



October 23, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 20, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE BENTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV06-1500-5, HONORABLE XOLLIE DUNCAN, CIRCUIT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of an order from the Benton County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which entered a writ of garnishment against it in favor of appellee company and denied its motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: A Florida court granted the company a judgment against an employee. The company filed the foreign judgment with the trial court, which issued a writ of garnishment upon the employer. The employer failed to file an answer. The company requested that the trial court order the employer to appear and answer the allegations and interrogatories served with the writ of garnishment. The trial court entered a writ of garnishment against the employer in the amount of $ 5,947, which was the amount it owed at the time of service of the writ, plus the amount of nonexempt wages earned through the date of judgment. The trial court denied the employer's motion for reconsideration. On appeal, the court found that the company properly registered a valid foreign judgment in the trial court as provided by Ark. Code Ann. § 16-66-602 (2005), and the trial court had jurisdiction to issue a writ of garnishment upon the employer. However, Ark. Code Ann. § 16-110-407 (2006) specifically limited a defaulting garnishee's liability to the amount of nonexempt wages held at the time of service of the writ of garnishment, plus attorney fees and other expenses appropriate under the facts and circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the trial court's order entering a writ of garnishment against the employer for the amount of nonexempt wages earned through the date of judgment. The court affirmed the remainder of the trial court's judgment.

 

209 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Bond v. State


No. CR08-224


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 332; 288 S.W.3d 206; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 533



October 2, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MILLER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR2006-609-2, HON. JAMES SCOTT HUDSON, JR., JUDGE.
Bond v. State, 373 Ark. 257, 283 S.W.3d 186, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 253 (Ark., 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Miller County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which convicted him of rape, rape as an accomplice, and permitting the abuse of a minor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape, rape as an accomplice, and permitting the abuse of a minor. The victim was his daughter. He was sentenced to 20 years in prison for the rape, 10 years in prison for being an accomplice, and 10 years in prison for the abuse of a minor. The sentences were to run consecutively. On appeal, he claimed that the trial court erred in excluding evidence of the victim's prior conduct under the rape-shield statute, Ark. Code Ann. § 16-42-101(b) (1999). Defendant had sought to introduce evidence involving an allegation made by the victim that her stepfather had molested her. The court found that the trial court did not clearly err in determining that the evidence of the victim's prior recantation was only slightly relevant, if at all, to the victim's credibility and that such evidence was more prejudicial than probative. The victim's prior allegation against her stepfather was not false because the victim's mother had discovered sexually explicit photographs of the victim taken by her stepfather. The trial court did not err in refusing to give defendant's proffered jury instruction regarding eligibility to transfer to community punishment supervision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

210 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Clark v. State


No. CR07-1276


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 292; 287 S.W.3d 567; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 501



September 25, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE LINCOLN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. LCR-2006-49-5-2, HON. ROBERT HOLDEN WYATT, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Lincoln County Circuit Court (Arkansas) that convicted her of two counts of sexual assault in the third degree, arguing that the trial court erred in denying her motion to suppress because her statement was not voluntarily given and erred in declining to recognize her due process right to have the entire interrogation recorded.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a psychologist with the Arkansas Department of Corrections until she engaged in sexual intercourse with an inmate. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's suppression motion. Although defendant claimed that her confession was the involuntary because it was the product of false promises, the detective denied promising defendant that she would not go to jail or that her license as a psychologist would not be affected, and it was for the trial judge to determine which witness was more credible. Because defendant was educated and intelligent, was not unfamiliar with the criminal justice system, and admittedly waived her Miranda rights and agreed to speak with the detective, the court concluded that defendant's confession was voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently given. The court declined to recognize a constitutional right under Ark. Const. art. 2, § 8, to have all phases of a police interrogation recorded. Even if such a right were recognized, however, any error would be harmless in light of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt, including the testimony of a corrections officer who witnessed the sexual contact.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

211 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Hampton v. State


No. CR 07-1263


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2008 Ark. LEXIS 444



September 18, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE: NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hampton v. State, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 684 (Ark., Dec. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF PULASKI COUNTY, CR 2003-634, HON. CHRIS PIAZZA, JUDGE.
Hampton v. State, 2005 Ark. App. LEXIS 161 (Ark. Ct. App., Feb. 23, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Pulaski County (Arkansas), which denied his Ark. R. Crim. P. 37.1 motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape and sentenced to 300 months in prison. His codefendant was acquitted. Defendant's conviction was upheld on direct appeal. Defendant filed a motion for postconviction relief under Rule 37.1. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, defendant complained that his due process rights were denied to him as shown solely by the inconsistent verdicts. The court concluded that the verdict in the codefendant's trial had no constitutional implications vis-a-vis the verdict in defendant's trial. The inconsistent verdicts did not demonstrate a constitutional error that rendered the judgment in defendant's case a complete nullity. Such a determination precluded defendant from raising the issue of unconstitutional inconsistent verdicts for the first time in a postconviction motion. There was no fundamental unfairness in accepting the jury's verdict in defendant's case, even if it was inconsistent with another verdict, and defendant failed to demonstrate otherwise.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

212 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Warren Wholesale Co. v. McLane Co.


No. 07-1034


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 171; 286 S.W.3d 709; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 459



September 11, 2008, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected, October 30, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV 03-6278; HON. COLLINS KILGORE, JUDGE.
McLane Southern, Inc. v. Davis, 366 Ark. 164, 233 S.W.3d 674, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 303 (Ark., 2006)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Arkansas companies licensed to sell wholesale cigarettes in Arkansas, sought review of an order from the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which declared ultra vires and unconstitutional certain portions of a cost and minimum price rule in a declaratory judgment action brought by appellees, out-of-state companies licensed to sell wholesale cigarettes in Arkansas. Appellees moved to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellees filed a complaint against the Arkansas Tobacco Control Board and its director for a declaratory judgment to determine the validity of § 15 of the Rules and Regulations of the Board. Appellants were allowed to intervene in the action. The trial court declared certain portions of § 15 ultra vires of the Arkansas Unfair Cigarette Sales Act and unconstitutional. While the appeal was pending, the Board ultimately promulgated a completely new version of § 15 and repealed the version of § 15 that was challenged in the declaratory judgment action. On appeal, the court found that when the Board repealed the version of § 15 that was the subject of the challenge, the appeal of the trial court's ruling on that same § 15 was rendered moot. Any construing of statutes that was required in the case had to be done in the context of the challenged regulation. Because the challenged regulation no longer existed, the court was void of a context in which to construe the statute, and the appeal was moot.


OUTCOME: The court granted appellees' motion to dismiss the appeal. The case was remanded for entry of a decree stating that the grounds upon which the trial court relied for entering the declaratory judgment and injunction became moot by the repeal of the challenged § 15.

 

213 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Ark. Dep't of Human Servs. v. A.B.


No. 07-897


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 193; 286 S.W.3d 712; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 466



September 11, 2008, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE BENTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV-05-914-4, HON. JOHN SCOTT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: ARKANSAS DEPARTMENT OF HUMAN SERVICES AFFIRMED; CIRCUIT COURT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Benton County Circuit Court, Arkansas, reversed an administrative law judge's (ALJ) decision that appellee minor had to remain listed on the Arkansas Child Maltreatment Central Registry. Appellant, Arkansas Department of Human Services (DHS), appealed.


OVERVIEW: The DHS argued that the minor's due-process right to confront and cross-examine adverse witnesses was not violated and that the ALJ's finding of child maltreatment was supported by substantial evidence. The supreme court found that the minor had shown nothing but the potential for prejudice. When compared to the government's interest in presenting its case without traumatizing child victims, DHS was not and should not have been required to call the victim to testify. The minor was afforded the opportunity to confront and cross-examine adverse witnesses but waived his right by failing to present their testimony. He could not argue that his due-process rights were violated. Under Ark. Code Ann. § 12-12-503 of the Arkansas Child Maltreatment Act, all that was required was proof that the minor engaged in actual or attempted sexual intercourse, deviate sexual activity, or sexual contact by forcible compulsion with the victim. There was evidence that the minor engaged in both deviate sexual activity and sexual contact by forcible compulsion with the victim. DHS offered a reasonable explanation for its decision not to present the victim's testimony at the administrative hearing.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was reversed, and the decision of the Arkansas Department of Human Services was reinstated.

 

214 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Municipality of Helena-West Helena v. Weaver


No. 08-176


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 109; 286 S.W.3d 132; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 423



June 26, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 20, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE PHILLIPS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV-2007-239. HON. L.T. SIMES, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a municipality and its mayor (city), sought review of the issuance of a writ of mandamus by the Phillips County Circuit Court (Arkansas) ordering the city to pay retirement benefits to appellee former mayor.


OVERVIEW: The former mayor contended that he was entitled to retirement benefits pursuant to West Helena, Ark., Ordinance 4B (2005). The city claimed that Ordinance 4B was invalid because it contradicted Ark. Code Ann. § 24-12-123 (Supp. 2007) and that pursuant to § 24-12-123 the former mayor was not yet entitled to retirement benefits. The court found that pursuant to Ark. Const. art. 12, § 4 no municipal corporation was authorized to pass any laws contrary to the general laws of the State of Arkansas. In addition, the court determined that city ordinances that were in conflict with Arkansas statutes were void under the Arkansas Constitution. Section 24-12-123(a)(3) controlled the manner in which a mayor's previous years of service as a former elected official or employee of the city could be added to his or her years of service as a mayor for retirement benefit purposes. Ordinance 4B provided that a mayor could apply all years of previous service toward his retirement benefits. It was in direct conflict with § 24-12-123. The court concluded the Ordinance 4B could not override the requirements of § 24-12-123. Accordingly, the former mayor was not currently entitled to retirement benefits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the issuance of the writ and dismissed the action.

 

215 of 594 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rowe


No. 07-1330


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 19; 285 S.W.3d 614; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 415



June 19, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 26, 2008.
Post-conviction relief denied at Rowe v. Hobbs, 2012 Ark. 244, 2012 Ark. LEXIS 265 (Ark., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR2004-790, CR2005-2786, HON. WILLARD PROCTOR, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT OF CERTIORARI GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review, or in the alternative a writ of certiorari, of an order of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) declaring Act 1782 (2001) (Act) unconstitutional upon a motion of appellee parolee, who contended that the Act unconstitutionally repealed the sunset clause of Ark. Code Ann. § 16-93-611 (2006) requiring persons convicted of certain offenses to serve 70 percent of their sentence prior to parole eligibility.


OVERVIEW: At a sentencing hearing of the parolee, who pleaded guilty to several controlled substances charges, the circuit court made an oral ruling on a collateral motion regarding parole eligibility, declaring the Act unconstitutional. A written order was entered almost a year later and held that the seventy percent rule would not apply to the parolee. Although the State's brief presented an important issue to the correct and uniform administration of the criminal law and upon which the court could hear an appeal pursuant to Ark. R. App. P. Crim. 3, the State's direct appeal was not timely under Ark. R. App. P. Crim. 2(e) (2008) because the notice of appeal was not filed within thirty days of the written order. However, the court had the discretion to treat an appeal from an order, judgment, or decree lacking in judicial support as if it were brought up on petition for writ of certiorari. The court held that the circuit court did not have authority to rule upon the parolee's motion. The ruling as to Act 1782 was not included in the parolee's judgment or commitment order, and Ark. R. Civ. P. 60(a) (2008), allowing a circuit court to modify a judgment, did not apply to criminal proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for a writ of certiorari.

 

216 of 594 DOCUMENTS



GMC v. Bryant


No. 07-437


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


374 Ark. 38; 285 S.W.3d 634; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 413



June 19, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by GMC v. Bryant, 173 L. Ed. 2d 107, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 498 (U.S., Jan. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE MILLER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV-2005-051-2, HON. JAMES SCOTT HUDSON, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought an interlocutory review of an order of the Miller County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which granted appellee pickup truck owner's request for class certification under Ark. R. Civ. P. 23. The owner filed an action alleging that the corporation sold around 4 million pickup trucks and sport utility vehicles with defectively designed parking brakes.


OVERVIEW: The corporation challenged the circuit court's findings as to predominance, superiority, and the class definition. The court found that whether or not the class vehicles contained a defectively designed parking-brake system and whether or not the corporation concealed that defect were predominating questions. The fact that various states' laws could be required in determining certain issues, such as damages or restitution, did not defeat predominance. The court held that the circuit court was not required to engage in a choice of law analysis prior to certifying the class. With regard to the issue of predominance, the court determined that the proposed class of around 4 million members made it at least likely that without a class action numerous meritorious claims could go unaddressed. In addition, the uniform relief sought was relatively small if sought on an individual basis, and thus, it was not economically feasible for members of the class to pursue the corporation on an individual basis. Finally, the class definition was sufficiently precise because the class was identifiable from objective criteria, specifically, ownership of the specified vehicles so specifically equipped.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order granting class certification.

218 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Gray v. Mitchell


No. 07-858


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


373 Ark. 560; 285 S.W.3d 222; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 380



May 29, 2008, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 25, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV2007-7476, HON. TIMOTHY J. FOX, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; MOTION TO DISMISS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pulaski County Circuit Court, Arkansas, granted summary judgment to appellees, as members of the Board of Education of the Little Rock School District, the Board of Education of the Little Rock School District of Pulaski County, Arkansas, and the Little Rock School District of Pulaski County, Arkansas (Board), on appellant taxpayers' claim that paying severance pay to the terminated superintendent was illegal. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers argued that the circuit court erred in finding that they had the burden of introducing evidence to establish the existence of a material question of fact. The supreme court found that the Board met its burden of showing there was no genuine issue of material fact. The superintendent's contract was properly before the court as an exhibit to the taxpayers' complaint. Absent a showing of a genuine issue of material fact, the question of whether payment of severance pay as part of the termination of the superintendent pursuant to the employment contract fell under the constitutional rubric of maintenance and operation of the public schools could be decided as a matter of law. Exactly what expenditures should be made to benefit a school district was a matter for the Board to determine, Ark. Const. art. 14, § 3. The taxpayer's attempts to characterize the payment to the superintendent as private and one solely for his benefit had to fail. While the specific payment plan involving the superintendent may not be capable of repetition, the issue of whether severance pay in superintendent employment contracts was constitutional was one of substantial public interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

219 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. McDaniel


No. 08-404


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2008 Ark. LEXIS 337



May 15, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE: NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Johnson v. McDaniel, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 5631 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
CIRCUIT COURT OF PULASKI COUNTY, CV 2007-6939, HON. JAMES M. MOODY, JUDGE.
Johnson v. State, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 214 (Ark., Mar. 23, 2006)



DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR RULE ON CLERK TREATED AS MOTION FOR BELATED APPEAL AND DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state inmate filed a pro se motion for rule on clerk, seeking to proceed with an appeal an order of the Circuit Court of Pulaski County (Arkansas) that denied his petition for declaratory judgment. The inmate had claimed that the aggravated robbery statute under which he had been convicted was not a complete statute and violated Ark. Const. art. 5, § 23.


OVERVIEW: The motion was treated as a motion for belated appeal pursuant to Ark. R. App. P. Crim. 2(e) because the notice of appeal was untimely filed in the trial court. The inmate's reasons for failing to perfect the appeal were not considered as he could not have prevailed on appeal. Specifically, the declaratory judgment action was properly dismissed as the inmate had cited no legal foundation for his claim and thus, he had not demonstrated that a justiciable controversy existed. Moreover, he misconstrued the language, purpose, and application of Ark. Const. art. 5, § 23, as it did not prohibit the legislative drafting technique of making a cross-reference to other statutes governing related matters. It was also apparent that the actual purpose of bringing the declaratory judgment action was an attempt to overturn his criminal convictions. A declaratory judgment action was not a substitute for an ordinary appeal.


OUTCOME: The motion for rule on clerk was treated as a motion for a belated appeal and was denied.

Benton County v. City of Bentonville


No. 07-394


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


373 Ark. 356; 284 S.W.3d 52; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 312



May 8, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE: THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Benton County v. City of Bentonville, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 420 (Ark., June 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE BENTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV99-197-1, HON. TOMMY J. KEITH, JUDGE.
City of Siloam Springs v. Benton County, 350 Ark. 152, 85 S.W.3d 504, 2002 Ark. LEXIS 470 (Ark., 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order from the Benton County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which awarded summary judgment to appellee cities in an action challenging the constitutionality of 1963 Ark. Acts 219.


OVERVIEW: The county brought an action against the cities, claiming that 1963 Ark. Acts 219, which directed the county collector to apportion to the cities 90 percent of the road funds collected within the corporate limits of those cities, was unconstitutional under Ark. Const. amend. 14. The trial court awarded summary judgment to the cities. On appeal, the court explained that it had to presume that 1963 Ark. Acts 219 was related to a legitimate governmental interest when enacted. The presumption was not rebutted by the county. No proof was offered to show that in 1963, Act 219 was not rationally related to achieving any legitimate objective of state government under any reasonably conceivable state of facts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


 

221 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Stine v. State


No. CR 07-1300


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2008 Ark. LEXIS 255



April 17, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE: NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Stine v. State, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 345 (Ark., May 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
CIRCUIT COURT OF SEBASTIAN COUNTY, FORT SMITH DISTRICT, CR 2002-304, HON. JAMES O. COX, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: MOTION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed in the Circuit Court of Sebastian County, Fort Smith District, Arkansas, a motion that complained of various constitutional violations related to sentences he received in 2002 and 2003. The trial court denied the motion and defendant, proceeding pro se, appealed the order. The State moved to dismiss the appeal for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Other than general arguments as to the constitutionality of the statutes cited by defendant in the motion, defendant raised no valid argument or authority to review the constitutional claims that he presented. Furthermore, he had no direct or collateral remedy with which to pursue his claims. The motion filed in the trial court could not have been acted upon as a direct appeal from the judgment since defendant pled guilty, and there was no apparent basis for a direct appeal from the plea, Ark. R. App. P. Crim. 1. Other than a petition under Ark. R. Crim. P. 37.1, there were no collateral remedies for defendant to pursue, and defendant's motion failed to raise grounds cognizable under an available postconviction procedure. Moreover, the pro se motion was filed more than five years after entry of the judgment, which was well outside the time limitations imposed in Ark. R. Crim. P. 37.2(c). Furthermore, Ark. R. Crim. P. 37.1 required that an defendant be incarcerated when seeking a remedy under the rule, and he was not. Since there was no basis for jurisdiction over the matter by the supreme court, the State's motion to dismiss had merit.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss the appeal for lack of jurisdiction was granted.

 

222 of 594 DOCUMENTS



Jones v. Flowers


No. 07-409


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


373 Ark. 213; 283 S.W.3d 551; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 267



April 17, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 25, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF PULASKI COUNTY, No. CV 2003-8565, HONORABLE TIMOTHY D. FOX, CIRCUIT JUDGE.
Jones v. Flowers, 547 U.S. 220, 126 S. Ct. 1708, 164 L. Ed. 2d 415, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3451 (2006)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Pulaski County, Arkansas, entered an order denying appellant taxpayer's request for an award of attorney fees against appellee Commissioner of State Lands, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988(b). The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer's due process rights were violated because the State failed to take additional steps to notify the taxpayer of a tax sale after an initial notice was returned undelivered. The taxpayer asserted that, as the prevailing party, he was entitled to recovery of attorney's fees at each stage of the litigation. The circuit court denied the request because it found that the first mention of 42 U.S.C.S § 1983 was in the status report. The taxpayer argued that an action did not have to be specifically pled under § 1983 for entitlement to attorney's fees under § 1988(b). The State asserted that under Ark. R. Civ. P. 54(e), the taxpayer forfeited his entitlement to attorney's fees because he failed to file the motion within 14 days of the supreme court's mandate. The supreme court noted that only until a final judgment that denied the Commissioner's request to reopen the question of liability, ordered that the taxpayer be given his house back, denied the taxpayer requested attorney's fees, and ordered the clerk to close the case was a motion for attorney's fees appropriate. Substance prevailed over form when a party failed to specifically plead an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying attorney fees was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Shoemate v. State


No. CR 08-01


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2008 Ark. LEXIS 190



March 20, 2008, Opinion Delivered

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
CIRCUIT COURT OF FULTON COUNTY, CR 96-45, HON. TIMOTHY M. WEAVER, JUDGE.
Shoemate v. State, 332 Ark. 435, 965 S.W.2d 779, 1998 Ark. LEXIS 193 (Ark., 1998)



DISPOSITION: MOTION TO SUPPLEMENT THE RECORD GRANTED; APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Fulton County, Arkansas, denying his petition for writ of habeas corpus under 2001 Ark. Acts 1780, codified as Ark. Code Ann. §§ 16-112-201--16-112-208 (2006). The petitioner filed a motion to supplement the record.


OVERVIEW: In 1997, a jury found the petitioner guilty of rape and sentenced him to 240 months' imprisonment in the Arkansas Department of Correction. The reviewing court denied the petitioner's motion for belated appeal. In 2006, the petitioner, through counsel, filed the instant appeal. The reviewing court held that there was no error in denying relief. A review of the petition revealed that it was defective in that it failed to rebut the statutory presumption against timeliness and did not comply with the procedural requirements of Ark. Code Ann. § 16-112-202(7). The petitioner failed to show that identity was an issue during the investigation or prosecution of the offense. The petitioner also argued that the record failed to contain a number of pertinent documents. The reviewing court found that the tendered supplement included an amendment to the petition in the trial court and other pleadings not contained in the original record before the reviewing court. Although not explicitly, the order did appear to consider the petition, the amendment, and the other pleadings, and those documents were therefore essential to any review of the order denying the petition.


OUTCOME: The motion to supplement the record was granted, and the appeal was dismissed.

 

224 of 594 DOCUMENTS


City of Fort Smith v. McCutchen


No. 07-864


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


372 Ark. 541; 279 S.W.3d 78; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 140



March 6, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 26, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SEBASTIAN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, FORT SMITH DISTRICT, NO. CIV-2005-612, HON. STEPHEN MERRILL TABOR, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sebastian County Circuit Court, Fort Smith District, Arkansas, granted appellee property owner a variance from a setback requirement contained in appellant city's ordinances. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the city's constitutionality argument was properly before it. The city argued that Ark. Code Ann. § 14-56-425 (1998) was unconstitutional because it permitted a de novo trial on appeal of a legislative determination made by a city Board of Zoning Adjustment (BZA). The supreme court found that under the statute, a BZA was an administrative agency and, despite the city's argument that the city's BZA made a legislative determination, a BZA did not have the power to legislate. Not only did a BZA not have the power to legislate, it was clear that the city's BZA was acting in an adjudicatory or quasi-judicial manner when it denied the owner's variance request because it related to the enforcement of an already-established ordinance. Ark. Code Ann. § 14-56-425 was not a violation of the separation-of-powers doctrine and was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Strong v. State


No. CR06-1346


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


372 Ark. 404; 277 S.W.3d 159; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 112



February 21, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at Strong v. State, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 627 (Ark., Nov. 13, 2008)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Dismissed by, Motion denied by, As moot Strong v. State, 2010 Ark. 181, 372 S.W.3d 758, 2010 Ark. LEXIS 211 (Ark., 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Strong v. Hobbs, 2013 Ark. 376, 2013 Ark. LEXIS 451 (Ark., 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE GREENE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR-2006-71, HON. CINDY THYER, JUDGE.
Strong v. State, 2007 Ark. LEXIS 466 (Ark., Sept. 13, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; MOTION TO WITHDRAW GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Greene County Circuit Court (Arkansas) of two counts of rape and was sentenced to serve two consecutive life sentences. Defendant appealed and his attorney file a no-merit brief and a motion to withdraw.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion for directed verdict because the evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions. The supreme court disagreed. The victim's testimony that she was fifteen years of age at the time of the two charged rapes, that she grew up in defendant's home and considered him her father, and that defendant engaged in sexual intercourse with her was sufficient to support the rape convictions. Moreover, the victim's testimony was corroborated by other reliable evidence. The forensic DNA analyst's testimony that the semen found on the sock and the underwear matched the DNA sample provided by defendant, along with the nurse practitioner's testimony that the victim's injuries were consistent with sexual abuse, provided proof beyond the victim's testimony. Other witnesses testified as to defendant's opportunities to engage in sexual intercourse with the victim. Clearly, the evidence supporting defendant's convictions was substantial. The victim's uncorroborated testimony would have been sufficient, and the testimony of the nurse practitioner as to the victim's injuries further supported the jury's determination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Counsel's motion to withdraw was granted.

Post-conviction relief denied at Jefferson v. State, 2017 Ark. 293, 2017 Ark. LEXIS 255 (Ark., Oct. 26, 2017)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Jefferson v. Arkansas, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 182566 (E.D. Ark., Nov. 3, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE ST. FRANCIS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR2005-513, HON. HARVEY LEE YATES, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the St. Francis County Circuit Court (Arkansas) convicting him of capital murder in violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 5-10-101(a)(1) (Supp. 2005), aggravated robbery, theft of property, and fleeing in violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 5-54-125(a), (d)(2) (Repl. 2005) in connection with the robbery of a convenience store and the death of a state trooper.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion for a directed verdict on the capital murder charge because: (1) but for defendant's aggravated robbery, speeding, and fleeing from the police, the trooper would not have been in the roadway attempting to retrieve stop sticks and would not have been struck by another trooper's vehicle; (2) the State presented sufficient evidence that defendant acted under circumstances manifesting an extreme indifference to the value of human life, as it showed that defendant robbed the victim with a gun, fled with his accomplice and the loot in a stolen car on a busy interstate, and initiated a high-speed chase while being pursued by several law enforcement officers with their lights and sirens blaring, thereby engaging in life-threatening activity; and (3) the phrase "under circumstances manifesting extreme indifference to the value of human life" was not void for vagueness, as the cases interpreting the phrase provided fair warning that it involved a life-threatening activity. The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion for a mistrial based on the prosecutor's allegedly improper remarks.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Ark. Bd. of Collection Agencies v. McGhee


No. 07-129


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


372 Ark. 136; 271 S.W.3d 512; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 43



January 17, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 29, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM PULASKI CIRCUIT COURT.
Old Republic Sur. Co. v. McGhee, 360 Ark. 562, 203 S.W.3d 94, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 87 (Ark., 2005)



DISPOSITION: ADMINISTRATIVE DECISION REVERSED AND REMANDED; CIRCUIT COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee customer sought relief in appellant Arkansas Board of Collection Agencies against appellant surety in the form of release of a bond to satisfy a judgment that the customer had previously won against a payday lender. The board denied relief. The Pulaski Circuit Court (Arkansas) reversed the board's order. The board and the surety appealed.


OVERVIEW: According to the court, the question presented was whether the lender violated the laws of Arkansas so as to invoke the terms of the surety's bond. The surety and the board argued that liability was limited to violations of the Check-Cashers Act, Ark. Code Ann. §§ 23-52-101 to 23-52-117 (2007) and the board's rules and regulations, which were not yet adopted when the bond was issued in 1999. However, the court noted that the bond's language protected against loss or damage suffered by any person resulting from the lender's violation of the "applicable laws of the State [of] Arkansas," including Arkansas' usury laws, such as Ark. Const. art. 19, § 13(a). The surety argued that it was entitled to rely on a Check-Cashers Act provision, Ark. Code Ann. § 23-52-104(b) (2000)--under which check-casher fees were not interest--before that provision was declared unconstitutional in 2001, but the court held that it was incumbent upon the surety to know and abide by the clear public policy of Arkansas regardless of one legislative act (the Check-Casher Act) that ran counter to that policy. By the surety's failure to do so, it violated the laws of Arkansas and became liable under the bond.


OUTCOME: The board's decision was reversed and remanded; the circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

Oldham v. Morgan


No. 07-315


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


372 Ark. 159; 271 S.W.3d 507; 2008 Ark. LEXIS 42



January 17, 2008, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 31, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM CRAIGHEAD COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. DR-2004-0693, HON. PAMELA BENITA HONEYCUTT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged an order of the Craighead County Circuit Court (Arkansas) granting appellee maternal grandparents visitation with their granddaughter under Ark. Code. Ann. § 9-13-103 (Supp. 2005).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the circuit court abused its discretion by granting the grandparents visitation with their granddaughter because the grandparents failed to establish that court-ordered visitation was in the granddaughter's best interest and failed to rebut the statutory presumption of § 9-13-103 that the father's decision was in the granddaughter's best interest, as they did not prove that a loss of the relationship between them and the granddaughter would likely harm her. There was no evidence presented at trial that the relationship between the grandparents and their granddaughter had been lost or would be lost, as the grandmother testified that she had seen her granddaughter seven times from November 17, 2006 and January 29, 2007 and that the father was very willing to work with the grandparents and let them see their granddaughter as much as they wanted. The fact that the grandparents only filed the petition to ensure that they would continue to see their granddaughter in the future rendered their petition premature.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed.

 

229 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Douthitt v. State


No. CR 07-527


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2007 Ark. LEXIS 680



December 13, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE: NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
CIRCUIT COURT OF INDEPENDENCE COUNTY, CR 95-58, HON. JOHN DAN KEMP, JUDGE.
Douthitt v. State, 326 Ark. 794, 935 S.W.2d 241, 1996 Ark. LEXIS 662 (Ark., 1996)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED; MOTION MOOT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant's 174-year sentence for felony rape, incest and violation of a minor were affirmed. The Circuit Court of Independence County, Arkansas denied his writ of habeas corpus based upon new scientific evidence under Ark. Code Ann. §§ 16-112-201 to 16-112-208 (2006), which was affirmed on appeal. Appellant filed pro se a second petition to vacate and/or set aside judgment, which was also denied. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, the supreme court determined that it need not consider the motion as it was apparent that appellant could not prevail in his appeal if it were permitted to go forward. In his previous petition, appellant claimed that the evidence used to convict him was obtained as a result of an unconstitutional search and seizure. In the instant petition, he sought to use scientific testing to prove that the search conducted by the police was initiated prior to authorization of the search by the victim and was unconstitutional. Because appellant had previously raised the issue of an unconstitutional search and seizure in his prior petition and made the same argument in the instant petition, the trial court did not err in denying a successive petition for similar relief. Moreover, this argument presented a basis for summary denial of the petition. Claims pertaining to the admissibility of evidence were not within the purview of a proceeding under Ark. Code Ann. §§ 16-112-201 to 16-112-208 (2006). Also, appellant's evidentiary argument did not involve actual scientific testing of specific evidence that was introduced at trial to secure his conviction.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

230 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Solis v. State


No. 07-701


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


371 Ark. 590; 269 S.W.3d 352; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 656



December 6, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 29, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE BENTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CIV-2006-2-154-2, HON. DAVID S. CLINGER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged a decision from the Benton County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which granted a default judgment in favor of appellee State in a civil forfeiture case.


OVERVIEW: The owner was arrested for a drug offense, and his vehicle was seized. He was served with a summons and complaint when forfeiture proceedings were instituted against the vehicle. The owner's answer did not contain a personal verification, and the State's motion for a default judgment was granted. This appeal followed. In affirming, the supreme court held that, under Ark. R. Civ. P. 11(a) (2007), a verification could have been required by rule or statute. In this case, Ark. Code Ann. § 5-64-505(g)(4) (Supp. 2005) had a specific requirement for a verification. Therefore, the answer was void and had no effect. Next, the summons was not deficient under Ark. R. Civ. P. 4(b) merely because it left out the verification requirements. Further, it was proper to name the vehicle in the caption, rather than the owner. The summons was also not defective for later listing the owner as the person to whom the summons was directed. Under Ark. R. Civ. P. 55(c), since the judgment was not void, the owner was required to demonstrate a meritorious defense. Since this standard was not met, the granting of the default judgment was proper. Finally, a constitutional issue was not addressed.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

231 of 594 DOCUMENTS


El Paso Prod. Co. v. Blanchard


No. 06-1107


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


371 Ark. 634; 269 S.W.3d 362; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 658



December 6, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 28, 2008.
Rehearing denied by El Paso Prod. Co. v. Blanchard, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 45 (Ark., Jan. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE COLUMBIA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. E-98-212-5, HON. LARRY CHANDLER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART; AFFIRMED ON CROSS-APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Columbia County Circuit Court, Arkansas, awarded damages to appellee property owner, resulting from seismic operations conducted by appellants, a production company and an energy company. The seismic operations were conducted upon surface lands owned by the property owner. The parties cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner and his mother owned 80 acres of land, which included a one-half interest in the mineral estate underlying the surface property. The family entered into an oil and gas lease with the energy company. The production company argued that the circuit court erred in finding that it trespassed on the property owner's property. Notwithstanding the production company's right to explore as a result of its one-half mineral rights, the production company violated Rule B-42 of the Arkansas Oil and Gas Commission by failing to obtain the property owner's consent. Further, Rule B-42 was constitutional as applied. Next, the appellate court held that the permission to conduct seismic operations was a license and was not an assignment. The payment to the property owner in unjust-enrichment damages was too speculative, particularly in light of the fact that the amount was not substantiated and neither the production company nor the energy company had the intent to drill. Also, because there was no breach of contract, there could be no tortious interference. Moreover, because there was no breach of contract, the trial court should not have awarded compensatory damages.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for a recalculation of actual damages.

 

232 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Hoyle v. State


No. CR 06-1249


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


371 Ark. 495; 268 S.W.3d 313; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 624



November 15, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hoyle v. State, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 12 (Ark., Jan. 10, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hoyle v. State, 2011 Ark. 321, 2011 Ark. LEXIS 432 (Ark., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE POLK COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT; NO. CR 2004-0103; HON. JAMES SCOTT HUDSON JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Polk County Circuit Court (Arkansas) of one count of battery in the first degree and two counts of manslaughter. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his battery conviction. The supreme court disagreed. The evidence showed that defendant acted recklessly under circumstances manifesting extreme indifference to human life. Specifically, the evidence demonstrated that defendant drove a fully loaded commercial vehicle weighing over 82,000 pounds while under the influence of methamphetamine. According to an expert witness, methamphetamine could cause a driver to weave across lanes of traffic, take undue risks, or leave the roadway. Defendant's entire vehicle, with the exception of the right rear axel, crossed into the oncoming-traffic lane, striking the motor home, and ultimately driving through it. Defendant never attempted to brake prior to the accident or to return to the proper lane of traffic. It was apparent based on the evidence in that defendant exhibited reckless conduct that involved a conscious disregard of a perceived risk. Accordingly, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for directed verdict on the first-degree battery charge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

233 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Tryon v. State


No. CR06-801


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


371 Ark. 25; 263 S.W.3d 475; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 515



September 27, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 13, 2008.
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Motion denied by, As moot Tryon v. Hobbs, 2011 Ark. 76, 2011 Ark. LEXIS 62 (Ark., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SEBASTIAN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. G-CR-2004-48, HON. NORMAN WILKINSON, JUDGE.
Tryon v. State, 2007 Ark. LEXIS 216 (Ark., Mar. 22, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Sebastian County Circuit Court (Arkansas) of possession of a controlled substance (methamphetamine) with intent to deliver, possession of drug paraphernalia, and theft by receiving. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction for possession of methamphetamine because he was not in possession of the methamphetamine that was found in the truck on his property. The supreme court disagreed. Officers testified that defendant was the registered owner of the white truck found in his backyard and that no other person was found at defendant's residence or in his yard. A witness testified that he observed a man matching defendant's description driving a white truck. When defendant left the residence, the bed of the truck was empty, but when he returned, the bed of the truck was full. A parole officer testified that she found the coat with methamphetamine in defendant's truck in defendant's backyard. As the State points out, when the truck was searched, it was immediately and exclusively accessible to defendant, and he was in close proximity to the methamphetamine. The only evidence submitted by defendant to refute any ownership or possessory interest in the truck was his own statement that someone else had borrowed his truck. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

234 of 594 DOCUMENTS



Gallas v. Alexander


No. 06-956


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


371 Ark. 106; 263 S.W.3d 494; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 502



September 27, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE GARLAND COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. 2005-l694-II, HON. JOHN LINEBERGER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Garland County Circuit Court, Arkansas, entered an order granting summary judgment to appellee Racing Commission, and appellee franchise holders, and dismissing appellant citizens' complaint, which alleged that 2005 Ark. Acts 1151, permitting the public's authorization of wagering on electronic games of skill at horse and greyhound racing parks, was unconstitutional. The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizens claimed that the Act was invalid in that it unlawfully delegated the legislature's authority to two private entities, franchise holders, to determine whether a county-wide or city-wide election should be held on wagering on electronic games of skill. The challenge was properly before the supreme court. The supreme court could not say that 2005 Ark. Acts 1151 constituted an impermissible delegation of legislative authority. Authority was not unlawfully delegated to the Commission when the legislature directed the Commission, in Ark. Code Ann. § 23-113-201(f)(2)(A)(i), to make a finding as to whether a game and electronic device or machine constituted an electronic game of skill. For their final point on appeal, the citizens argued that Act 1151 was special legislation because it arbitrarily allowed franchise holders to operate electronic gambling machines on their properties while making it a criminal offense for all other persons in the state to operate the same. The supreme court held that there was nothing irrational or arbitrary about the legislature's decision. The citizens failed to meet their burden in showing the Act was clearly unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.


 

235 of 594 DOCUMENTS



Ark. Okla. Gas Corp. v. MacSteel Div. of Quanex


No. 07-148


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


370 Ark. 481; 262 S.W.3d 147; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 472



September 13, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Ark. Okla. Gas Corp. v. MacSteel Div. of Quanex, 2007 Ark. LEXIS 562 (Ark., Oct. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SEBASTIAN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, FORT SMITH DISTRICT. NO. CIV-2005-181-G, HON. NORMAN WILKERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gas utility sued appellees, a steel manufacturer, a county, the county court, and members of the county quorum court, challenging a lease the county entered into with the manufacturer, subject to an easement in land that had been conveyed to the county for public recreation purposes. The Sebastian County Circuit Court, Fort Smith District, Arkansas, rendered a summary judgment against the utility. The utility appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the utility contended the circuit court erred in finding that the county properly entered into the lease and granted the easement. The appellate court disagreed, finding that giving the words their ordinary meaning and usually accepted meaning in common language, Ark. Code Ann. § 14-164-205 (1998) was plain, unambiguous, and provided that any municipality or county could contract or alienate any land or facilities of any and every nature whatever in securing or developing industry. Thus, the grant of the second easement by the county to allow the manufacturer to obtain gas for its industrial operations was permitted under the plain meaning of this statute. As the utility offered no evidence that the county had become a stockholder in the manufacturer, or any evidence that the county had appropriated money, or loaned its credit to the manufacturer, there was no merit to the utility's argument that Ark. Const. art. XII, § 5 was violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

The Circuit Court of Grant County, Arkansas, entered a judgment reflecting the jury's verdict finding the stranger to be 100 percent at fault. The driver appealed.

Mosley v. State


No. CR 06-694


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2007 Ark. LEXIS 348



June 7, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT


PRIOR HISTORY: PRO SE APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF CRITTENDEN COUNTY, CR 98-774, CR 2005-334, HON. RALPH EDWIN WILSON, JR., JUDGE.
Mosley v. State, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 478 (Ark., Oct. 5, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 1998 and 2006, defendant pleaded guilty to Arkansas drug charges and received suspended sentences. In 2006, defendant entered a plea of guilty to revocation of the first suspended sentence and received a prison sentence. Defendant petitioned for postconviction relief pursuant to Ark. R. Crim. P. 37.1. The Circuit Court of Crittenden County (Arkansas) denied the petition without a hearing, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant maintained that the trial court was prohibited from entering a suspended imposition of sentence in his cases, as the controlling statutes mandated incarceration. Defendant's allegations of ineffective assistance of counsel lacked merit because they failed to provide supporting facts and amounted to mere conclusory statements. Defendant's allegations of prosecutorial misconduct also had no merit because they could have been raised at trial or argued on direct appeal. In addition, the trial court had not been required to hold an evidentiary hearing on the Rule 37.1 petition because the order denying the petition was sufficient to indicate that the trial court had made its findings from the record, and that the record had supported the denial.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

238 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Weiss


No. 07-204


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


370 Ark. 205; 258 S.W.3d 351; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 359



June 7, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 8, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV2005-9251, HON. WILLARD PROCTOR, JR., JUDGE.
Wilson v. Weiss, 368 Ark. 300, 245 S.W.3d 144, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 633 (Ark., Dec. 14, 2006)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED ON DIRECT APPEAL; AFFIRMED ON CROSS-APPEAL. MOTION TO DISMISS APPEAL DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant alleged an illegal exaction premised because certain acts of the general assembly violated Ark. Const. art. 5, § 29 by not including a "distinct purpose" or, alternatively, constituted special and local legislation in violation of Ark. Const. amend. XIV. The Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) found the acts constitutional. Appellant appealed. Appellees, city officials, cities, a county, museums, and clubs (entities) cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, a county filed a motion to dismiss relating to a $ 50,000 appropriation to the county library under 2005 Ark. Acts 932 on grounds of mootness. The Supreme Court of Arkansas held that 2007 Ark. Acts 1290 did not go into effect until July 1, 2007, and, thus, 2005 Ark. Acts 932 was not rendered ineffective until that same date. The result was that a decision regarding the constitutionality of Act 932 handed down prior to July 1, 2007, would not be moot. Indeed, were the supreme court to affirm the decision of the circuit court relative to the county library appropriation prior to July 1, 2007, that money would be available to the library irrespective of 2007 Ark. Acts 1290. The supreme court also held that the acts were unconstitutional in that they failed to state a distinct purpose as required by Ark. Const. art. 5, § 29. The stated purpose in each act was either to provide "state assistance" or "state aid." Those stated purposes did not comply with the requirement of art. 5, § 29, and the supreme court's precedent. The mere statement that the challenged acts will be used for "state assistance" or "state aid" did not explain "how" the funds would be used.


OUTCOME: The orders of the circuit court relating to the acts were reversed. The case was remanded. The judgment of the trial court on the cross-appeal was affirmed. The motion to dismiss the appeal was denied.

Thomas v. State


No. CR 06-439


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


370 Ark. 70; 257 S.W.3d 92; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 310



May 17, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

 [***1] THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 8, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Thomas v. State, 2007 Ark. LEXIS 397 (Ark., June 21, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Thomas v. Arkansas, 552 U.S. 1025, 128 S. Ct. 620, 169 L. Ed. 2d 399, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12155 (2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at Thomas v. State, 2013 Ark. 238, 2013 Ark. LEXIS 272 (Ark., 2013)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part Thomas v. Kelley, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 50059 (W.D. Ark., Mar. 31, 2017)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Sevier County Circuit Court (Arkansas) of two counts of capital murder and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion for a continuance. The supreme court disagreed. Defendant filed motions for a continuance offering the following justifications, inter alia, his court-appointed lead counsel had just completed a capital murder trial which lasted six days, and had another death penalty trial set to begin just twenty-three days prior to defendant's trial, and a witness was unavailable for trial. However, the trial date had been established eight months in advance, and there was no objection by defendant at that time concerning the trial date. Defendant did not provide any evidence that he did not receive effective assistance of counsel or that he was not adequately represented. There was no evidence that the trial testimony of the witness would differ from his testimony given in a pretrial hearing. It was also not shown that the witness would have been available to testify had the continuance been granted. Further, defendant did not prove that the lack of a continuance kept him from being able to present evidence of there being no rape or attempted rape at the scene of the crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Fayetteville v. Washington County


No. 06-602


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


369 Ark. 455; 255 S.W.3d 844; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 271



April 26, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:

THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 8, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE WASHINGTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV-05-559-2, HON. KIM M. SMITH, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART REVERSED AND REMANDED ON CROSS-APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellee County Assessor certified rates and property values for purposes of tax-increment financing, appellant City filed a declaratory judgment and mandatory injunction against appellees, the County, a school district, a public library, et al., seeking redistribution of the tax-increment revenues. The Washington County Circuit Court, Arkansas, concluded that the rates and property values were correct and denied relief. The City appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the City raised several issues challenging the trial court's ruling that the Assessor was correct in its allocation of millage rates. The supreme court agreed that the Assessor was incorrect to allocate more mills to the school district for purposes of the tax-increment financing (TIF) formula than were passed by the voters, which would violate Ark. Const. art. XVI, § 11. However, the supreme court disagreed with the City's argument that Ark. Const. amend. 78 repealed the uniform rate of 25 mills to be used for maintenance and operation of the schools as provided under Ark. Const. amend. 74 as the voters were never put on notice that redevelopment projects would be funded with a portion of the uniform rate of 25 mills that had previously been designated solely for the maintenance and operation of the public school. If the authors of the amendment had meant for it to repeal a particular section of the constitution, they would have said so, but did not. Furthermore, an invincible repugnancy between the amendments did not exist so as to cause a repeal by implication. As such, the trial court properly concluded that Ark. Const. amend. 78 did not alter Ark. Const. amend. 74.


OUTCOME: The Assessor's certification was modified to the correct millage rate; the trial court's finding that the proceeds of one mill from the tax for libraries was properly included in the Assessor's certification was reversed; otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

McMickle v. Griffin

SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS

As Corrected November 8, 2007.
Reaffirmed, Supplemental opinion at, Rehearing denied by McMickle v. Griffin, 2007 Ark. LEXIS 314 (Ark., May 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF PHILLIPS COUNTY, NO. CIV-01-149 AND CIV-03-373; HON. L.T. SIMES AND HON. HARVEY YATES, JUDGES.
