CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death suit brought by appellate administratrix of a decedent's estate, the Circuit Court of Phillips County, Arkansas, entered a judgment following a jury verdict in favor of appellee tractor driver and appellee tractor owner. The parties cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was killed when he hit a tractor on a highway. The tractor driver was an employee of the tractor owner. The administratrix contended that the circuit court erred in refusing to instruct the jury to consider certain statutory violations as some evidence of negligence. The supreme court concluded that the administratrix was entitled to an instruction based on Ark. Code Ann. § 27-35-210 (1955). As far as any inconsistency with Ark. Code Ann. § 27-35-102 was concerned, § 27-35-210 was the controlling statute because it was the later-enacted statute. As to the tractor owner's duty of care to the decedent, the administratrix pointed to, among other things, the tractor driver's deposition testimony that he worked for the tractor owner, and the tractor owner was his boss. The trial court erred in not allowing evidence that showed agency or employment. The trial court did not err in denying a motion for directed verdict for the tractor owner. Another issue was whether an amendment to the wrongful-death statute to allow damages for loss of life was procedural or remedial legislation. The supreme court concluded that 2001 Ark. Acts 1516 was meant to be applied retroactively.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed on the cross-appeal. The supreme court reversed the judgment, and it remanded the matter.

Parker v. BancorpSouth Bank


No. 06-1171


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


369 Ark. 300; 253 S.W.3d 918; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 228



March 22, 2007, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Rehearing denied by Parker v. BancorpSouth Bank, 2007 Ark. LEXIS 433 (Ark., May 3, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Union County Circuit Court, No. Cv-2004-0332-4, Carol Crafton Anthony, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee bank brought suit against appellant debtor, alleging that the debtor had borrowed money from the bank, and the bank alleged the debtor defaulted. The Union County Circuit Court, Arkansas, entered a judgment in favor of the bank, finding that the Arkansas Statutory Foreclosure Act was not unconstitutional. The debtor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The debtor allegedly borrowed money to finance the purchase of a home. A promissory note was executed to evidence the indebtedness. On appeal, the debtor's sole point on appeal was that the circuit court erred when it ruled that the Statutory Foreclosure Act, Ark. Code Ann. §§ 18-50-101 to 18-50-117 (2003), did not violate either the Arkansas or United States Constitution. In essence, the borrower alleged that the act violated procedural due process because the notice requirement failed to give an individual notice of what to do in the event he or she wishes to contest the propriety of a foreclosure. The supreme court disagreed. The supreme court concluded that there was no state action present here. State action did not take place merely because the Arkansas General Assembly passed the act. There were also no state officials involved. The debtor further argued that the statutory foreclosure provisions violate separation of powers, but the debtor failed to raise the argument to the circuit court, and she failed to obtain a ruling on the argument. The supreme court was precluded from addressing the merits of the argument.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Weiss v. Maples


No. 06-742


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


369 Ark. 282; 253 S.W.3d 907; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 227



March 22, 2007, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Pulaski County Circuit Court, No. Cv 04-3685, Mary Spencer Mcgowan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxpayer, on behalf of himself and all taxpayers similarly situated, filed an illegal-exaction lawsuit, claiming that the Emergency Income Tax Rule 2003-4, adopted by appellant Arkansas Department of Finance and Administration (DFA) was unconstitutional. The Pulaski County Circuit Court, Arkansas, agreed with the taxpayer. The circuit court ordered a refund to those taxpayers who were improperly taxed in 2003 and 2004.


OVERVIEW: For the years 2003 and 2004, the taxpayer was bound by the Emergency Rule, requiring that annuity income from employment-related retirement plans be taxed in accordance with I.R.C. § 72. The taxpayer alleged that the Emergency Rule violated the separation-of-powers doctrine and was unconstitutional. Ark. Code Ann. § 26-51-404(b)(24) (Supp. 2003) provided that annuity income from employment-related retirement plans should be taxed in accordance with Ark. Code Ann. § 26-51-307. The supreme court had previously determined that Ark. Code Ann. § 26-51-307(c) (Supp. 2003) was unconstitutional; hence, the Emergency Rule was enacted, pertaining to recipients of public or private retirement plan benefits. Prior case law clearly held that there was nothing to indicate that the Arkansas General Assembly intended that § 72 be applied to recovery of after-tax contributions in employment-related retirement plans. Further, the General Assembly made it clear that § 72 of the Internal Revenue Code should not apply to annuity income received from these retirement plans. The Emergency Rule was outside the scope of the director's rule-making authority as set forth in Ark. Code Ann. § 19-1-208.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

 

244 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Summerville v. Thrower


No. 06-501


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


369 Ark. 231; 253 S.W.3d 415; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 215



March 15, 2007, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Pulaski County, Arkansas, No. Cv 2005-9641, Chris Piazza, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Pulaski County (Arkansas), which dismissed her medical malpractice case against appellee health care providers.


OVERVIEW: The patient contended that the providers failed to properly diagnose her with a tubal pregnancy after she underwent a tubal ligation. She filed a medical malpractice action, but it was dismissed based on a failure to comply with Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-209(b)(3)(A) (2006). This appeal followed. In reversing, the supreme court held that § 16-114-209(b)(3)(A) directly conflicted with Ark. R. Civ. P. 3. This case was similar to the one decided in Weidrick, where it was determined that a 60-day notice prior to the filing of a medical malpractice action was superceded by Ark. R. Civ. P. 3. Here, the mandatory requirement for an affidavit 30 days after filing a complaint was an added encumbrance for filing a complaint that did not essentially differ from the notice requirement struck down in Weidrick. The automatic dismissal of the case if the affidavit was not filed made this portion of the statute procedural in nature. Since the rules of pleading, practice, and procedures for the Arkansas courts was within the domain of the supreme court, the affidavit requirement ran afoul of Ark. Const. amend. 80, § 3. The supreme court noted that the balance of Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-209 was valid.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Davis v. State


No. 06-825


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2007 Ark. LEXIS 182



March 8, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIRCUIT COURT OF LINCOLN COUNTY, LCV 2006-27, HON. ROBERT HOLDEN WYATT, JR., JUDGE.
Davis v. State, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 571 (Ark., Nov. 16, 2006)



DISPOSITION: MOTION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a state inmate, file a pro se petition for writ of habeas corpus. The Lincoln County Circuit Court, Arkansas, denied the petition. The inmate appealed. The appeal was dismissed. The inmate then filed a pro se motion for reconsideration of that decision, which was denied. Then, for a second time, the inmate brought a pro se motion for reconsideration of the decision to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate resurrected the arguments he made in his previous motion for reconsideration. He argued that Ark. Code Ann. § 16-112-103 (1987), was impermissibly vague and unconstitutional. He asserted that the court was precluded from interpreting the statute under Ark. Const. art. IV, and was required to overturn all prior cases interpreting the statute. The court rejected the inmate's assertion that, by requiring a habeas petitioner to plead either the facial invalidity or the lack of jurisdiction and to make a showing, by affidavit or other evidence, of probable cause to believe he was illegally detained, the court's previous cases added requirements beyond those provided in the statute itself. The court also declined to strike down § 16-112-103 as unconstitutionally vague and thereby eliminate a well-established legal remedy. The statute clearly stated its requirements. The inmate's petition did not state claims that supported issuance of a writ of habeas corpus. The inmate stated no reason for the court to revisit its original decision. Therefore, once again, his motion for reconsideration was denied.


OUTCOME: The inmate's motion for reconsideration of the decision to dismiss his appeal was denied.

McKinney v. Bishop


No. 06-1033


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


369 Ark. 191; 252 S.W.3d 123; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 190



March 8, 2007, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal From The Crawford County Circuit Court, No. Cv 2005-328, Michael Medlock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED WITHOUT PREJUDICE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Crawford County Circuit Court, Arkansas, dismissed appellant estate administrator's complaint against appellees, doctors, hospital, and John Does 1-10, alleging survival and wrongful-death claims based on ordinary negligence, medical malpractice, and the violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 12-12-507. The administrator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that there was neither a final order as to John Does 1-10, nor was there an Ark. R. Civ. P. 54(b) certification. Accordingly, the administrator's claims against John Does 1-10 were still pending. Because there was not a final order as to these defendants nor a Rule 54(b) certification, the supreme court did not have jurisdiction to hear the case and the appeal was dismissed without prejudice so that the circuit court may enter an order as to the remaining defendants.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed without prejudice.

 

247 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Childers v. Payne


No. 06-691


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


369 Ark. 201; 252 S.W.3d 129; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 192



March 8, 2007, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Pulaski County Circuit Court, No. Cv 05-118. Alice Sprinkle Gray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a decision from the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which dismissed his malpractice complaint against appellee chiropractor for failure to comply with Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-209 (2006). The chiropractor filed a cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: After a second malpractice case was filed, the chiropractor moved for a dismissal, arguing that a letter attached to the complaint did not comply with Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-209. A later affidavit was filed, the trial court determined that a portion of the statute was unconstitutional, and it gave the patient 15 days to file a supplemental affidavit. This was not filed, and the case was dismissed. An appeal followed. In affirming, the supreme court determined that the patient failed to submit a proper expert affidavit within 30 days of his second complaint. However, an affidavit from the expert that was filed more than 30 days later was not considered because it was too vague. Both the letter and the affidavit failed to describe the expert's familiarity with the applicable standard of care or how the injury was a proximate cause of the failure to perform within that standard. The patient could not argue for reversal when he declined to file a proper affidavit after more time was given. Finally, the patient lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of a portion of the statute since that was not applied to him.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed, and the cross-appeal was moot.

 

248 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Huckabee


No. 06-620


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


369 Ark. 42; 250 S.W.3d 241; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 118



February 15, 2007, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Pulaski County Circuit Court, No. Cv 2003-7036, Williard Proctor, Jr., Judge.
Jones v. Huckabee, 363 Ark. 239, 213 S.W.3d 11, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 474 (Ark., Sept. 15, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant arrestee challenged a decision from the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, the Arkansas Crime Information Center (ACIC), its director, and a governor, in an action alleging a violation of civil rights.


OVERVIEW: After dismissal of two separate sets of criminal charges, the arrestee obtained an expungement under Ark. Code Ann. § 16-90-906 (2006). The arrestee later filed an action contending that the ACIC failed to destroy the records and properly restrict access to them. The circuit court granted summary judgment, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the supreme court noted that the records in this case had been electronically segregated; therefore, they were only available to criminal justice agencies for criminal justice purposes under Ark. Code Ann. § 12-12-1008 (2003). There was no merit in the allegation that the ACIC violated any civil rights when it refused to destroy the records because this was not required under Ark. Code Ann. § 16-90-901(a)(1), (2) (2006). Next, the doctrine of respondeat superior was not a basis for liability under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 based on an allegation of misuse of the arrest records. This rationale also applied to the Arkansas Civil Rights Act, Ark. Code Ann. §§ 16-123-101 to 16-123-108. Finally, since the trial court did not make a specific ruling on the constitutionality of the ACIC enabling statutes, the issue was not addressed on appeal.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Dep't of Health & Human Servs. v. R.C.


No. 06-858


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 660; 249 S.W.3d 797; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 102



February 8, 2007, Delivered


NOTICE:

 [***1] THE LEXIS PAGINATION OF THIS DOCUMENT IS SUBJECT TO CHANGE PENDING RELEASE OF THE FINAL PUBLISHED VERSION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by R. C. v. Ar Dep't of H&Hs, 128 S. Ct. 359, 169 L. Ed. 2d 58, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 9600 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV 05-154, HON. RAYMOND C. KILGORE, JR., JUDGE.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Health and Human Services (DHHS) challenged an order of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) directing that appellee foster mother's name be removed from the child-maltreatment registry.


OVERVIEW: After finding that the foster mother had abused her foster child by spanking her with a switch, an administrative law judge (ALJ) ordered that the mother's name remain on the child maltreatment central registry. On appeal of the circuit court's order reversing the ALJ's decision, the court that there was substantial evidence supporting the ALJ's finding that the mother caused a nonaccidental physical injury to the child because: (1) the child had bruising on the back of her thighs from the back of her knees to the bottom of her buttocks; (2) there were at least eight to ten bruises, which were evidence by several straight lines, some of which were near the child's vaginal area; (3) there was testimony that the bruises were at least 24 hours old; (4) two of the other children being fostered by the mother told an investigator that she used a switch when administering punishment; and (5) the mother herself stated during the investigation that she had used a switch to swat the child upon finding her in the bathroom with feces on her and spread about the bathroom. None of the exceptions to a finding of abuse under Ark. Code Ann. § 12-12-503(2)(C) were present.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed. The ALJ's decision was affirmed.

Simes v. Ark. Judicial Discipline & Disability Comm'n


No. 06-725


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 577; 247 S.W.3d 876; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 63



January 25, 2007, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected June 19, 2007.
Related proceeding at Judicial Discipline & Disability Comm'n v. Simes, 2009 Ark. 296, 308 S.W.3d 613, 2009 Ark. LEXIS 279 (Ark., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Weaver v. City of West Helena, 367 Ark. 159, 238 S.W.3d 74, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 425 (Ark., 2006)



DISPOSITION: PETITION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judge petitioned the Arkansas Supreme Court to grant a writ of certiorari to respondent Arkansas Judicial Discipline and Disability Commission (Judicial Commission) quashing a letter of admonishment and declaring it invalid.


OVERVIEW: The judge argued that the Judicial Commission did not meet its burden of showing a compelling state interest for enactment of Ark. Code Jud. Conduct Canon 5C(2) sufficient to justify infringement of protected speech under the First Amendment. The supreme court found that the case was factually distinguishable from an Eighth Circuit decision and did not view that decision as decisive. The supreme court did find that Arkansas had a compelling interest in impartiality, as a lack of bias for or against either party involved in a proceeding, where the direct solicitation of money by a judge was at issue. The open-mindedness of judges as a sufficient compelling state interest. Avoiding the appearance of impropriety was also a compelling state interest. Canon 5 was narrowly tailored to meet the State's interest of impartiality and avoiding the appearance of impropriety. Canon 5C(2) provided that candidates may establish campaign committees to conduct fundraising on their behalf. The Judicial Commission's determination that an admonition was appropriate was not clearly erroneous based on evidence of conduct that was, or might be, or might become cause for discipline.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

251 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Ellis v. Reynolds


No. 06-1119


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 572; 247 S.W.3d 845; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 64



January 25, 2007, Opinion Delivered


DISPOSITION:  [***1] DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner personal representative filed an application for a writ of prohibition relating to respondent circuit court's referral of an estate matter to mediation under Ark. Code Ann. § 16-7-202(b) (Supp. 2005).


OVERVIEW: The representative and the decedent's husband had a dispute regarding the ownership of the decedent's property. The circuit court ordered the parties to mediate the issues. The representative's motion to dispense with mediation was denied. This writ application followed. In denying the petition, the supreme court determined that the granting of such a writ was only appropriate if the circuit court was wholly without jurisdiction and there was no adequate remedy. The circuit court's jurisdiction included all matters previously cognizable by circuit, chancery, probate, and juvenile courts, pursuant to Ark. Const. amend. 80, § 6(A). As such, the circuit court had jurisdiction over the representative's motions stemming from the administration of the estate. Moreover, the interpretation or constitutionality of a statute was an issue that could have been determined by a circuit court and then appealed. As such, an extraordinary writ was not required in this case.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

252 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Griffen v. Ark. Judicial Discipline & Disability Comm'n


No. 06-1392


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 557; 247 S.W.3d 816; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 65



January 25, 2007, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Griffen v. Ark. Judicial Discipline & Disability Comm'n, 368 Ark. 443, 2007 Ark. LEXIS 29 (Ark., Jan. 12, 2007)



DISPOSITION: PETITION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judge filed a petition for writ of mandamus to compel respondent Arkansas Judicial Discipline and Disability Commission (Judicial Commission) to admit the public and news media to his formal probable-cause meeting. The executive director of the Judicial Commission refused the judge's request that the meeting be open to the public.


OVERVIEW: The judge raised several legal justifications in support of his petition to compel the opening of the probable-cause meeting: (1) violation of the Arkansas Freedom of Information Act, (2) violation of procedural due process, (3) violation of the First Amendment, and (4) waiver of all confidentiality. The judge requested that his probable-cause meeting be open to the public and news media. The supreme court noted that the Judicial Commission could not give it a specific reason for closing the formal probable-cause meeting. Ark. Const. amend. 66(c) contemplated a hearing before disciplining a judge by reprimand or censure. Where a public admonishment or other required adjustment of the judge's conduct may be the result and where a judge has waived confidentiality without any countervailing reason to close the formal meeting presented by the Judicial Commission, the formal probable-cause meeting had to be open. Matters concerning disciplinary procedure that required immediate attention, such as closing a meeting that may result in a public sanction, were appropriately brought to the supreme court by a petition for writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted.

 

253 of 594 DOCUMENTS


C.C.B. v. Ark. HHS


No. 06-554


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 540; 247 S.W.3d 870; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 68



January 25, 2007, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, SIXTH DIVISION; NO. CV 2005-5344; HON. TIMOTHY DAVIS FOX, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Sixth Division, Arkansas, which affirmed his placement on the child maltreatment central registry maintained by appellee Arkansas Department of Health and Human Services (DHHS).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was placed on the registry for having a sexual encounter with a 13-year-old. The decision of the DHHS was upheld in an administrative hearing and in a circuit court. This appeal followed. In affirming, the supreme court determined that the fact that the administrative law judge and the prosecutor came from the same agency did not amount to a violate of due process under the Fourteenth Amendment and Ark. Const. art. 2, § 8. The combination of investigative and adjudicative functions did not, without more, constitute a due process violation. Appellant did not prove that the process was invalid based simply on the statutory scheme and the procedures in place in this case. Moreover, the supreme court rejected the argument that the standard of evidence should have been changed to a clear and convincing standard. Appellant did not show that he would have prevailed had the standard been higher; moreover, he failed to show that he was denied a specific employment opportunity due to his placement on the registry. Finally, the failure to sustain a hearsay objection and the refusal to consider a defense under Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-102 (2003) was not arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

254 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Ark. Dep't of Corr. v. Bailey


No. 06-674


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 518; 247 S.W.3d 851; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 62



January 25, 2007, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF PULASKI COUNTY, ARKANSAS, NO. CV 2004-7304, HONORABLE WILLARD PROCTOR, CIRCUIT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CIRCUIT COURT REVERSED; SEX OFFENDER ASSESSMENT COMMITTEE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Pulaski County, Arkansas, found that the Sex Offender Registration Act (Act), Ark. Code Ann. § 12-12-901 et seq. (2003 & Supp. 2005), violated federal and state constitutional guarantees of procedural due process, as applied to defendant. It reversed the Sex Offender Assessment Committee's decision to assess defendant as a Level 3 offender. The Department of Correction (DOC) appealed.


OVERVIEW: The DOC argued that the Act comported with the requirements of due process. The supreme court concluded that defendant was wrong when he protested that the fact of his conduct had never been established; by entering a plea of not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect, he acceded to the allegation that he engaged in the conduct charged. Because he availed himself of the procedure afforded under Ark. Code Ann. § 5-2-313, defendant's due process rights were not violated. Regardless of the reason one was required to register as a sex offender, the procedures afforded by the Act were the same. Those procedures comported with procedural due-process requirements. The assessment requirement for one who was acquitted of a sex offense by reason of mental disease or defect was rationally related to the State's high and legitimate interest in protecting society from repeat sex offenders.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was reversed; the decision of the Sex Offender Assessment Committee was affirmed.

 

255 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. Norris


No. 06-372


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2007 Ark. LEXIS 34



January 18, 2007, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: PRO SE APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF LINCOLN COUNTY, LCV 2005-120, HON. ROBERT HOLDEN WYATT, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in the Circuit Court of Lincoln County (Arkansas), seeking relief on a judgment for convictions on charges of murder in the second degree, fleeing, aggravated assault, and felon in possession of firearms. The lower court denied the petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate essentially challenged the circuit court's findings that he failed to state grounds to support issuance of the writ. The argument that the consecutive sentences were illegal was rejected as the decision to impose consecutive or concurrent sentences rested solely within the province of the trial judge. Thus, there was no Blakely violation. The assertion that the sentence imposed on the murder charge exceeded the presumptive sentence was not cognizable in a habeas petition as consideration of the inmate's allegations of a Blakely violation would have required an examination of the plea proceedings or more of the record than appeared before the appellate court. Thus, consideration of the issue was not suitable for a habeas proceeding. In essence, because the factual basis for the inmate's plea was not indicated on the record, the circuit court could not have determined the issue without inquiry beyond that appropriate to a habeas corpus proceeding. Since the inmate failed to state cognizable claims, he failed to show any basis for a finding that a writ of habeas corpus should have issued.


OUTCOME: The denial of the habeas petition was affirmed.

Sowders v. St. Joseph's Mercy Health Ctr.


No. 06-414


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 466; 247 S.W.3d 514; 2007 Ark. LEXIS 44



January 18, 2007, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE HOT SPRING COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV2002-225-2, HON. PHILLIP H. SHIRRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, claimant, challenged the order of the Hot Springs County Circuit Court, Arkansas, granting summary judgment in favor of appellees, hospital and health system, in the claimant's suit alleging negligence in prematurely discharging her after a procedure, and failing to safely and properly transport her.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was injured after undergoing an outpatient procedure at the hospital, and the injury allegedly occurred when hospital employees transported the claimant by wheelchair to a waiting car. The hospital was a member of the health system's pooled comprehensive liability program. The circuit court found that the hospital, as a charitable facility, was not subject to suit, and that the pool agreement did not constitute liability insurance for purposes of the direct-action statute, Ark. Code Ann. § 23-79-210 (2004). The appellate court ruled that the claimant could not bring suit against or collect a judgment from the hospital. Under the charitable-immunity doctrine, the claimant could bring suit against the hospital's liability insurer or employees, but could not bring suit against the charitable organization. Also, there was not the right to sue the health system under the direct-action statute because the program did not meet the statutory definition of insurance, and because the health system did not meet the statutory definition of an insurer under the Arkansas Insurance Code, as it was not in the business of entering into contracts of insurance.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Wilson v. Weiss


06-740


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 300; 245 S.W.3d 144; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 633



December 14, 2006, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Subsequent appeal at Wilson v. Weiss, 370 Ark. 205, 258 S.W.3d 351, 2007 Ark. LEXIS 359 (Ark., June 7, 2007)
Related proceeding at Wilson v. Walther, 2017 Ark. 270, 2017 Ark. LEXIS 244 (Ark., Oct. 5, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; Willard Proctor, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: DISMISSED WITHOUT PREJUDICE IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen sued appellees, state officials, a city, counties and various organizations, alleging that multiple acts passed in the 2005 general session constituted as special and local legislation in violation of Ark. Const. amend. 14 and Ark. Const. art. 5, § 29. The Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) found that some of the acts were constitutional and others were unconstitutional. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen filed his complaint and the circuit court initially issued a temporary restraining order against the state defendants to prevent them from disbursement of the funds connected to the contested appropriations. The citizen then amended his complaint and added three defendants. These defendants were never served with process. The supreme court found that the three new defendants added to the complaint were never dismissed. As such, under Ark. R. Civ. P. 54(b) no final order had been entered. With regard to the appeal of the revocation of the restraining order against the city, that was subject to an interlocutory appeal and thus was properly before the court. The act that applied to the city constituted as special and local legislation because the reasons put forth to justify the appropriation to the city for infrastructure, sewer and streets could be advanced by multiple cities and communities throughout the state and no reason rationally related to a legitimate state purpose had been provided for singling out the city for special treatment. Therefore, the act that pertained to the city was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed in part with regard to the claims against the new defendants who were not officially dismissed from the action. The judgment was reversed with regard to the act that pertained to the city and the action was remanded with regard to those claims.

Great Lakes Chem. Corp. v. Bruner


06-73


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 74; 243 S.W.3d 285; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 564; 171 Oil & Gas Rep. 514



November 16, 2006, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Union Circuit Court, No. Cv04-0443-4; Carol Crafton Anthony, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Arkansas Oil & Gas Commission, affirmed on direct appeal; affirmed on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Union County, Arkansas, affirmed an order of appellee Arkansas Oil and Gas Commission (Commission) ordering appellant corporation to return to the accounting procedures agreed to in the operating agreement and approved by the Commission in its 1996 order. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation argued that the contract dispute between it and cross-appellant company was more appropriately decided by the circuit court. The supreme court found that the operating agreement was reviewed and approved by the Commission and the West Brine Unit Order specifically stated that the Commission retained jurisdiction over the parties. Reading the Brine Production Act (Act), Ark. Code Ann. § 15-76-301 et seq. (1994), with the Administrative Procedures Act (APA), Ark. Code Ann. § 25-15-212(g) (2002), it appeared that the correct procedure for the circuit court to follow was to limit its review to the record and allow the parties to introduce evidence only for the purpose of showing the Commission's order was invalid or unreasonable. The Act did not allow a de novo review of the Commission's order but permitted additional evidence relating to procedural irregularities before the Commission. There was substantial evidence that the corporation violated the Commission's order. The final order allowed the corporation to charge the company for its proportionate use of the disposal pipeline system for the transportation of brine to the disposal well.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed on direct appeal and on cross-appeal.

McGhee v. Ark. State Bd. of Collection Agencies


06-381


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 60; 243 S.W.3d 278; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 568



November 16, 2006, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by McGhee v. Ark. State Bd. of Collection Agencies, 375 Ark. 52, 289 S.W.3d 18, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 745 (Ark., Nov. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Seventh Division; No. Cv-2003-4837; Barry A. Sims, Judge
McGhee v. Ark. State Bd. of Collection Agencies, 360 Ark. 363, 201 S.W.3d 375, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 39 (Ark., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pulaski County Circuit Court, Seventh Division, Arkansas, granted judgment in favor of appellees, Arkansas State Board of Collection Agencies and its members (Board), in finding that no public funds were used by the Board in licensing and regulating companies operating under the Check-Cashiers Act (Act), Ark. Code Ann. §§ 23-52-101 to -117, and in finding the Act constitutional. Appellant class members appealed.


OVERVIEW: The members argued that the trial court erred in determining that there was no illegal-exaction claim based on a misuse of public funds. The supreme court found that the Board established its entitlement to summary judgment through the affidavits of the Board's Executive Director. The director averred that the Board did not receive any revenue from state treasuries, had not used any public funds to finance its operations, and the funds used by the Board were not generated from tax dollars. The members failed to refute that evidence. In the absence of a valid illegal-exaction claim, it was proper for the trial court to dismiss the members' claim for declaratory judgment holding the Act unconstitutional because they were required to preserve such a claim in the first appeal. The members were not required to first seek a declaration regarding the constitutionality of the Act before the Board. The members properly sought a declaration in circuit court that the Act was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the circuit court where the members properly sought a declaration in circuit court that the Act was unconstitutional; the judgment was affirmed as to all other issues.

Carter v. Georgia-Pacific Resins, Inc.


05-1250


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


368 Ark. 19; 242 S.W.3d 616; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 582



November 9, 2006, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal From The Ashley County Circuit Court, No. Cv2001-110-1, Samuel Pope, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, employees and family members, appealed a decision of the Ashley County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which dismissed plaintiffs' claims against defendant employer related to alleged exposure to asbestos at the workplace. The circuit court found that the claims were barred by the exclusive remedy provision of the Workers' Compensation Act (WCA), specifically Ark. Code Ann. § 11-9-105.


OVERVIEW: The employer contended that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction to determine the applicability of the WCA. On review, the court agreed that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction to determine whether the employees' injuries were covered under the WCA. The court held that the determination was exclusively within the jurisdiction of the Workers' Compensation Commission. Even though the case raised a constitutional issue and the Commission might not have authority to declare statutes unconstitutional, the issues had to be raised first at the Commission level because such issues required an exhaustive analysis that was best accomplished by an adversary proceeding, which could only be done at the administrative hearing level. The court further found that the facts presented were not so one-sided so as to demonstrate that the WCA did not apply as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court and dismissed the instant appeal, with leave for the parties to pursue a determination before the Commission.

Talbert v. State


CR 05-1279


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


367 Ark. 262; 239 S.W.3d 504; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 446



September 21, 2006, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court, No. Cr 04-4563, John W. Langston, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) convicting him of two counts of third-degree sexual assault in violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-126(a)(1)(B) (Repl. 2006) and sentencing him to two terms of 20 years in prison, to run consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a minister, was convicted for sexually assaulting two victims, who attended and worked for defendant's church. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because the testimony of the victims did not indicate a consensual relationship: (1) both victims testified that they looked up to defendant as a minister and trusted him; (2) one victim testified that she was afraid of what might happen to her if she did not comply with sexual requests; (3) the victim testified that she was not attracted to defendant; (4) and the second victim testified that she told defendant that because he was a minister, sex was not right. The court rejected defendant's constitutional challenges to Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-126(a)(1)(B) (Repl. 2006). The court further held that there was sufficient evidence that the crime against one victim occurred in 2002, and therefore was within the three-year statute of limitations of Ark. Code Ann. § 5-1-109(b)(2) (Repl. 2006) as she testified that the assault happened while she was working for the church during the summer of 2002.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

263 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Jester v. State


CR 05-1231


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


367 Ark. 249; 239 S.W.3d 484; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 448



September 21, 2006, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Hot Spring County Circuit Court, No. CR 2003-326-1, Chris E. Williams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hot Spring County Circuit Court (Arkansas) of first-degree criminal mischief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The supreme court disagreed. The facts revealed that defendant informed the property owner that there were a large number of pine beetles on the property and that he was losing a lot of trees. According to defendant, the owner told him to "go ahead and do what you think needs to be done. Treat it like your own." After that conversation, defendant used a bulldozer to make roads throughout the property and then began to harvest the trees. While the property was on the market, a certified forester inspected the land and discovered that a very large percentage of the property had been recently logged. An investigator examined the property and determined that the entire 300 acres had been cut over. In addition, the owner found a handwritten "no trespassing" sign placed on the property -- on the reverse was a sign for defendant's timber company. Defendant admitted cutting the timber. The jury was not obligated to believe that defendant was acting under -- what he believed was -- the owner's consent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

McGraw v. Jones


No. 06-00048


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


367 Ark. 138; 238 S.W.3d 15; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 407



June 29, 2006, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at, Summary judgment granted by State Volunteer Mut. Ins. Co. v. McGraw, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29519 (W.D. Ark., Apr. 20, 2007)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Jones v. McGraw, 374 Ark. 483, 288 S.W.3d 623, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 553 (Ark., Oct. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE BENTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. NO. CV 2004-1774-4. HON. JOHN RUSSELL SCOTT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician challenged a decision from the Benton County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which entered a default judgment in a medical malpractice case and awarded damages to appellees, a patient and his wife.


OVERVIEW: The patient and his wife filed a medical malpractice case against the physician based on a pulmonary embolism. The physician gave the documents to her office staff, but they never reached an in-house attorney. A default judgment was entered, and damages were awarded. Thereafter, the physician sought to have the default judgment set aside. The trial court denied the request, and the physician sought review. In partially affirming, the appellate court determined that the physician's failure to file an answer was not the result of excusable neglect under Ark. R. Civ. P. 55(c) (2005). She did nothing to ensure that a defense was being mounted on her behalf. The fact that a meritorious defense existed did not mean that the default judgment was set aside, unless one of the grounds under Rule 55(c) was shown. Also, nothing in Rule 55 required the trial court to provide notice to the physician regarding the hearing on damages. Because notice and an opportunity for a hearing had been provided, due process was not violated. However, there was insufficient evidence to support the $500,000 damage award because the testimony was largely speculative.


OUTCOME: The damages awarded were reversed, and the case was remanded for a new hearing on that issue. The rest of the decision was affirmed.

Howard v. State


No. CR 05-699


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


367 Ark. 18; 238 S.W.3d 24; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 417



June 29, 2006, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected February 27, 2007.
Habeas corpus proceeding at Howard v. Norris, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 18771 (E.D. Ark., Mar. 2, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Little River Circuit Court,, No. CR97-105; Charles A. Yeargan, Judge.
Howard v. State, 366 Ark. 453, 236 S.W.3d 508, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 325 (Ark., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Little River County, Arkansas, denying his petition for postconviction relief under Ark. R. Crim. P. 37.5, which sought relief from his convictions of two counts of capital murder and one count of attempted murder, and his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected the inmate's claims that the State knowingly introduced false testimony in order to bolster its theory of the case and that the information charging him with capital murder was defective on the ground that it failed to enumerate any of the four aggravating circumstances upon which the State relied to obtain the death penalty because the claims could have been raised on direct appeal but were not, and could not be raised for the first time in a Rule 37 petition. The inmate's claims pertaining to a juror's alleged untruthfulness during voir dire concerning his feelings about the death penalty were not cognizable in his postconviction proceeding. The inmate waived any error that may have arisen from the sheriff's acting as a witness in his case and as the bailiff because he failed to raise the issue on direct appeal and because the State and defense counsel agreed for the sheriff to remain in the courtroom in exchange for the defense team to be able to keep its investigators in the courtroom as well. The court also rejected the inmate's numerous claims of ineffective assistance of trial counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the inmate's petition for postconviction relief was affirmed.

Dep't of Human Servs. v. Howard


05814


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


367 Ark. 55; 238 S.W.3d 1; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 418



June 29, 2006, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected February 27, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; No. CV 99-9881; Timothy Davis Fox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on direct appeal; cross-appeal moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Arkansas Department of Human Services and the Child Agency Review Board, sought review of a decision of the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Sixth Division (Arkansas), which ruled that § 200.3.2 of the Minimum Licensing Standards for Child Welfare Agencies (Regulation 200.3.2) violated the separation of powers doctrine and was unconstitutional. Appellants filed a cross-appeal with additional constitutional challenges.


OVERVIEW: Regulation 200.3.2 disqualified individuals from becoming foster parents if any adult member of that individuals' household was a homosexual. The circuit court ruled that the regulation violated the separation of powers doctrine. The court determined initially that appellees had standing to bring the lawsuit. Appellees were within the class of persons affected by the regulation and each appellees' attempt to become a foster parent would have been futile. Appellees were not required to exhaust administrative remedies because they could challenge the validity of Regulation 200.3.2 pursuant to Ark. Code Ann. § 25-15-207(2002) with a declaratory judgment action. The court found that Regulation 200.3.2 did nothing to promote the health, safety, or welfare of foster children as required by regulations promulgated pursuant to Ark. Code Ann. 9-28-405(2002). Rather Regulation 200.3.2 improperly excluded a set of individuals from becoming foster parents based upon the Board's morality and bias. The General Assembly did not delegate the legislative power to the Board to address issues of morality, and Regulation 200.3.2 thus violated the separation-of-powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

 

267 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Burton v. State


CR 05-494


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


367 Ark. 109; 238 S.W.3d 111; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 421



June 29, 2006, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Rehearing denied by Burton v. State, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 457 (Ark., Sept. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arkansas County Circuit Court, Southern District. No. Cr-2002-63. Hon. David G. Henry, Circuit Judge.
Burton v. State, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 77 (Ark., Jan. 19, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from Arkansas Circuit Court; David G. Henry, Judge; reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Arkansas County Circuit Court, Southern District (Arkansas) of two counts of aggravated assault, one count of criminal mischief, and one count of being a felon in possession of a firearm. After his request for postconviction relief was denied, the petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued, inter alia, that counsel was ineffective in failing to request a severance of the felon-in-possession charge. The supreme court agreed. The circuit court did not hold a hearing on the petition for post-conviction relief. Consequently, the record provided no insight as to why counsel failed to file a motion for severance. Without such evidence in the record, it could not be presumed that counsel's failure to request severance of the felon-in-possession charge fell within the category of a tactical decision. An examination of the record revealed that the evidence of guilt was less than "overwhelming." A witness testified on behalf of the petitioner, stating that the gun found at the residence was her gun and that a friend had shown her how to shoot the gun earlier that day. She further testified that she did not see the petitioner with a gun. The complainant testified repeatedly that she was drunk at the time of the incident and so could not be sure of any of the details. Most notably, her testimony was even inconsistent regarding whether or not she actually heard a gunshot. Both complainants testified that it was not uncommon to hear gunshots in the area.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Moses v. Hanna's Candle Co.


No. 05-1105


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


366 Ark. 233; 234 S.W.3d 872; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 266



May 4, 2006, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court of Washington County, Arkansas, CV 03-1711-1, Mary Ann Gunn, Circuit Judge.
Moses v. Hanna's Candle Co., 353 Ark. 101, 110 S.W.3d 725, 2003 Ark. LEXIS 220 (Ark., 2003)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual filed a products liability action against defendants, company and its owner, for injuries she sustained while working as temporary employee for the company. The Circuit Court of Washington County, Arkansas, granted summary judgment in favor of defendants. The individual appealed.


OVERVIEW: The individual was working as a temporary employee for the company when she sustained a severe work-related injury that caused the amputation of all of her fingers on her right hand and part of the hand itself. The employee obtained a workers' compensation settlement wherein the temporary agency who placed her with the company agreed to pay all authorized reasonable and necessary medical expenses arising out of the individual's injury. The agency also agreed to pay the individual's attorney's fees and an additional $ 44,225 to settle her claim. The individual filed the present action in the district court and alleged that the company and its owner were liable as "designer, manufacturer, component part supplier, and/or seller" of the machine that caused the individual's injury. The appellate court reversed the grant of summary judgment as it held that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to consider the issue under Ark. Code Ann. § 11-9-105(a) (Supp. 1995). The appellate court held that the Arkansas Workers' Compensation Commission had exclusive, original jurisdiction to determine whether the company was an employer and immune from suit under the Workers' Compensation Act.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court direct the court to remand this case to the Arkansas Workers' Compensation Commission.

 

270 of 594 DOCUMENTS


McLane Southern, Inc. v. Davis


05-990


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


366 Ark. 164; 233 S.W.3d 674; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 303; 2006-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P75,242



April 13, 2006, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Warren Wholesale Co. v. McLane Co., 2008 Ark. LEXIS 459 (Ark., Sept. 11, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; NO. CV 2003-7958, James Maxwell Moody, Jr., JUDGE.
McLane Co. v. Davis, 353 Ark. 539, 110 S.W.3d 251, 2003 Ark. LEXIS 329 (Ark., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cigarette wholesaler sued appellee Arkansas Tobacco Control Board, contending that amendments made to the Arkansas Unfair Cigarette Sales Act, Ark. Code. Ann. § 4-75-701 et seq. (2005), by Act No. 627, Ark. Acts 2003, rendered the Act unconstitutional under the due process provisions of Ark. Const. art. 2, § 8 and the Fourteenth Amendment. The Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) dismissed the complaint; the wholesaler appealed.


OVERVIEW: An amendment to Ark. Code Ann. § 4-75-702(1) and (5)(B) altered the cost to wholesalers by increasing the presumed "cost of doing business" from two and three-fourths' percent to four percent of the basic cost of the cigarettes to a wholesaler. The wholesaler argued that this change made the statutory presumption of predatory intent arising from below-cost sales under Ark. Code Ann. § 4-75-708(e) arbitrary and capricious and therefore unconstitutional. The high court held that the Act, as amended, afforded the wholesaler due process. There was a rational basis for the amendment of the presumed cost of doing business, as the legislature could have found that changed market conditions supported an increase in the cost of doing business. The amendment to Ark. Code Ann. § 4-75-702(5)(B) merely clarified where and what type of proof a wholesaler had to file in order to make a below-cost sale of cigarettes. The anti-rebate provisions in Ark. Code Ann. § 4-75-708(e) had a rational basis and were thus constitutional; because rebates made it more difficult to enforce and administer the Act, the legislature may have decided to prohibit them.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ark. Wildlife Fed'n v. Ark. Soil & Water Conservation Comm'n


05-1009


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


366 Ark. 50; 233 S.W.3d 615; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 222



April 6, 2006, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; No. CV 04-1726, Willard Proctor, Jr., Judge.
 [***1] 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, nonprofit corporations, an association, and individuals, challenged an order from the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which denied their motion for summary judgment and awarded summary judgment to appellees, the Arkansas Soil and Water Conservation Commission (ASWCC) and an irrigation water distribution district, in a suit challenging the ASWCC's authority to enter into a project with the United States Department of the Army.


OVERVIEW: Appellants brought an action against appellees, challenging the authority of the ASWCC to enter into a project cooperation agreement with the Department of the Army. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the ASWCC and denied appellants' cross-motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that appellants had standing to raise the issue of the exclusiveness of the AGFC's authority under Ark. Const. amend. 35, even in the absence of the AGFC as a party. Further, by virtue of Amendment 35, the AGFC did not have the power to prevent the destruction, manipulation, or alteration of natural resources, including streams and rivers, when such changes to those resources would allegedly have a collateral impact on wildlife or wildlife resources. The trial court correctly found that the responsibilities of the ASWCC under the project did not constitute the type of management or control of the wildlife resources of the State of Arkansas that was reserved to the AGFC under Amendment 35, § 1, but rather involved a federal project and a navigable river where the role of the ASWCC was principally one of funding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

272 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Crawford County v. Jones


No. 05-680


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


365 Ark. 585; 232 S.W.3d 433; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 204



March 16, 2006, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Crawford County Circuit Court; No. CV-2001-29; Gary Cottrell, Judge.
Crawford County v. Jones, 91 Ark. App. 161, 209 S.W.3d 381, 2005 Ark. App. LEXIS 431 (Ark. Ct. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED ON DIRECT APPEAL; AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART ON CROSS-APPEAL; COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED. MOTION FOR IMPOSITION OF ATTORNEY FEES AND COSTS; GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee employee was fired as an assessor with appellant county and filed suit for breach of contract, wrongful termination, violation of the Arkansas Whistle-Blower Act (Act), Ark. Code Ann. §§ 21-1-601-609 (2003), and outrage. A quorum court held that she should be reinstated, but she was terminated. The employee filed suit and the trial court granted the county's motion for a directed verdict on all but the claim for breach of contract.


OVERVIEW: The jury found in favor of the employee and awarded damages. The Arkansas Court of Appeals affirmed the breach of contract verdict and affirmed the order of the trial court directing a verdict on the outrage claim and denying the motion for attorney's fees. It reversed the order directing a verdict on the claim under the Whistle-Blower Act. On cross-appeal the employee argued that the trial court erred in granting the motion for a directed verdict on her claim under the Act. Pursuant to Ark. Code Ann. § 21-1-604(c), the employee had to establish that she suffered an adverse action because she engaged or intended to engage in an activity protected under the Act. The issue was whether the employee's actions of reporting the alleged misdeeds to quorum court members constituted reporting to the "appropriate authorities." Because the quorum court was vested with the legislative power of the county and under Ark. Code Ann. § 21-1-602(2)(A)(ii) reporting could be made to a member of a governing body, the evidence submitted by the employee regarding her reporting of the alleged misdeeds to quorum court members created a question of fact that should have been resolved by the jury.


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of the county's motion for directed verdict regarding the Whistle-Blower Act was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial on the employee's claim under the Act. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects. The court of appeals was affirmed. The employee's motion for imposition of attorney fees and costs was granted.

Escobedo v. Nickita


No. 05-315


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


365 Ark. 548; 231 S.W.3d 601; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 178



March 9, 2006, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected December 4, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Washington County Circuit Court, No. PR-04-608-5, Michael H. Mashburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an adoption case, the Washington County Circuit Court, Arkansas, granted the petition for adoption filed by appellee adoptive parents, and found that neither notice to nor consent from appellant, the putative father, was required. The circuit court's order also dismissed the putative father's petition for paternity. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The putative father and the child's mother had a brief romantic relationship. He did not know that the encounter had resulted in pregnancy. Two weeks before the birth, on November 19, 2004, the adoptive parents filed a petition for adoption and alleged that the father was unknown. The mother relinquished her parental rights and consented to the adoption of the baby. On December 14, 2004, the putative father was served with a summons, petition for adoption, notice of hearing, and notice of deposition. The requirements of due process were satisfied. A DNA test showed that he was the child's biological father, but he did not timely register with the putative-father registry. His consent to the adoption was not required by Ark. Code Ann. § 9-9-206(a)(2) (Repl. 2002). He had not "otherwise legitimated" the child pursuant to Ark. Code Ann. § 9-9-206(a)(2). He did not have an established relationship with his child at the time the petition for adoption was filed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Daniels v. Dennis


05-1351


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


365 Ark. 338; 229 S.W.3d 880; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 132



February 23, 2006, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Sixth Division; Timothy Davis Fox, Judge. No. CV2005-10794.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee judge filed a complaint for declaratory judgment against appellant, the Secretary of State for the State of Arkansas, asserting that Ark. Code Ann. § 16-13-104 (Supp. 2005) was unconstitutional. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The Pulaski County Circuit Court, Arkansas, granted summary judgment, and it found the statute to be unconstitutional, void, and of no effect. The Secretary appealed.


OVERVIEW: The judge was appointed to the position of circuit court judge. Subsequent to her appointment, the act became effective. To support her motion for summary judgment, the judge filed an affidavit indicating that had she known that she would be ineligible to run for another circuit judge position, she would not have accepted the appointment. The Secretary argued that the act was constitutional, in that it was a valid exercise of the General Assembly's authority over the creation and regulation of judicial districts and divisions to deny the advantages of incumbency to judges who were not elected. Nevertheless, the supreme court determined that the Secretary's reliance on Ark. Const. amend. 29 was unavailing. Contrary to the Secretary's argument, it was not apparent that the purpose behind the amendment was to deny the advantages of incumbency to an appointed judge. Amendment 29 prevented a person from succeeding himself or herself in the specific position to which he or she was appointed.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

Helena Daily World v. Simes


05-146


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


365 Ark. 305; 229 S.W.3d 1; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 145; 34 Media L. Rep. 1329



February 16, 2006, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected September 29, 2006.
Related proceeding at Weaver v. Simes, 365 Ark. 289, 229 S.W.3d 15, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 147 (Ark., Feb. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PHILLIPS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, HON. L.T. SIMES II, JUDGE.
Helena Daily World v. Simes, 363 Ark. 197, 211 S.W.3d 542, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 454 (Ark., July 1, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Petition for Certiorari granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner newspaper sought a writ of certiorari directing respondent, a judge with the Phillips County Circuit Court (Arkansas), to dissolve an injunction that prevented the newspaper from reporting testimony given in a case involving a dispute between a mayor and a city council.


OVERVIEW: The newspaper sought a writ of certiorari directing the judge to dissolve an injunction that prevented it from reporting testimony given in open court during a pretrial hearing in a case involving a dispute between a mayor and a city council. In the case, the mayor had testified that the judge had initiated an improper ex parte conversation with him. The court agreed that the restraining order was too broad and was an unconstitutional prior restraint on the press. The proceeding concerned an issue of great public interest and concern. Although the court was sensitive to the concerns raised by the judge, it found that they were insufficient to counterbalance the public interest in the knowledge of what had transpired at judicial proceedings that were open to the public. The reasons for the restraining order advanced by the judge were insufficient to justify its breadth or to justify the suppression of the testimony given by the mayor. Once the mayor gave his testimony in open court, the judge could not undo what had been done by attempting to suppress the testimony after the fact. Therefore, the restraining order constituted a plain, manifest, clear, and gross abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of certiorari and directed the judge to modify his order in accordance with the court's opinion.

 

276 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Graham v. State


CR 05-1018


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


365 Ark. 274; 229 S.W.3d 30; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 140



February 16, 2006, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Appeal from the Circuit Court of Pulaski County; No. CR 04-5071, John Langston, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of permitting child abuse after the Circuit Court of Pulaski County, Arkansas, denied her motion to dismiss. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence at trial proved that defendant was the victim's mother, there was physical evidence of the abuse, and the victim's aunt testified that defendant knew her husband was abusing her son. Thus, the appellate court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to dismiss as there was sufficient evidence to support a conviction in violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 5-27-221 (Supp. 2003). The appellate court also noted that the trial court was free to find the aunt's testimony more credible than defendant. Finally, defendant's claim that § 5-27-221 was unconstitutionally vague was rejected because the conduct proscribed by the statute was a "failure to take action to prevent abuse." If abuse was occurring, and defendant was aware of that abuse, she was criminally liable if she did nothing to prevent further abuse. In this case, there was evidence that defendant was aware of the abuse; there was also evidence that the abuse continued to occur after defendant acknowledged her awareness of it, including testimony that defendant permitted the abuse to continue because she "needed a babysitter." This evidence indicated that defendant failed to act to prevent the abuse.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

White v. Ark. Capital Corp.


NO. 05-337


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


365 Ark. 200; 226 S.W.3d 825; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 61



February 2, 2006, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected November 17, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski County Circuit Court, No. EOT 99-2366, Vann Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a judgment of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) that dismissed his suit against appellees, the Economic Development of Arkansas Fund Commission, and grant recipient businesses. The taxpayer challenged the constitutionality of two appropriation bills, 1997 Ark. Acts 413 and 672, and alleged that all appropriations made under the bills constituted illegal exactions in violation of Ark. Const. art. V, § 29.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer claimed that because the Acts were unconstitutional, the appropriations or grants made by the Economic Development Commission were misappropriations of public funds. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees on the ground that appellees acted in good faith by relying on legislative acts that were presumed to be valid. On appeal, the taxpayer claimed illegal-exaction claims were not subject to defenses of good faith. The court adopted the reasoning of other jurisdictions that had adopted the rule that penalties should not be imposed on private parties for acts done in accordance with a law valid at the time the acts were performed but later held to be unconstitutional. The court held that statutes were presumed to be constitutional, and should not punish state officials or citizens for doing likewise. The court noted that in the five-year span between the filing of the lawsuit and the trial court's order, the Commission had been abolished and all monies appropriated through the Commission were spent. Thus, neither injunctive relief nor restitution were proper remedies and the taxpayer's claims were moot and the trial court did not err in so ruling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

278 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Austin v. Centerpoint Energy ARKLA


05-72


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


365 Ark. 138; 226 S.W.3d 814; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 83



February 2, 2006, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski County Circuit Court; No. CV 04-5228, James M. Moody, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a decision ruling that appellee public service commission lacked the authority to establish a policy regarding low-income assistance, appellant customer filed a class action suit for an illegal exaction against the commission and appellee gas utilities, alleging she paid a surcharge pursuant to the policy. The Circuit Court of Pulaski County, Arkansas, granted the commission's and the utilities' motions to dismiss. The customer appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the customer contended, inter alia, that the trial court erred in finding that the commission had jurisdiction to resolve her claims. The supreme court disagreed, finding first that it had already decided in a prior decision the constitutionality and legality of the commission's action and that the relief the customer was seeking was a refund for the amount of the surcharge she paid. Further, the surcharge was collected by the utilities, not the commission, and the commission had primary jurisdiction to mandate monetary refunds under Ark. Code Ann. § 23-3-119(d) (2002). The customer's labeling of her claim as a tort did not automatically deprive the commission of authority to hear the complaint. And, contrary to the customer's assertion, the surcharges were not a tax; they were a mechanism by which the utilities could recover some of the bad debt incurred as a result of the implementation of the policy. As such, the customer did not have a valid illegal exaction claim. The supreme court's conclusion in the prior decision that the surcharge was unlawful did not make it any less of a rate while it was being charged and collected by the utilities.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

279 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Henry v. Buchanan


05-533


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


364 Ark. 485; 221 S.W.3d 346; 2006 Ark. LEXIS 5



January 5, 2006, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected December 6, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Washington Circuit Court; Mark Lindsay, Judge.No. PR-2003-370.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandparents appealed the denial by the Washington County Circuit Court, Arkansas, of their motion to vacate the adoption by appellee wife of appellee husband's daughter. Appellants were the maternal grandparents of the husband's daughter.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents claimed that the trial court erred in denying their motion to vacate the wife's adoption of their granddaughter because they were not given notice of the adoption proceedings. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling as there was no statutory authority for the grandparents to vacate the adoption. The state supreme court noted that essentially there were only two circumstances where grandparents were entitled to notice of adoption proceedings: (1) statutorily, where the grandparent was the parent of a deceased child whose child was to be adopted; and (2) where the grandparent, despite the status of his or her child, had stood in loco parentis to the grandchild at some point. Neither situation applied here as the grandparents' daughter, the child's biological mother, was still alive and had consented to the adoption.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

280 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee


No. 01-836


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2005 Ark. LEXIS 773



December 15, 2005, Decided


NOTICE: NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 368 Ark. 231, 243 S.W.3d 919, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 601 (Ark., Nov. 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Trial Court: Pulaski, Pulaski Chancery, Second Division. Trial Judge: Raymond C. Kilgore Jr. Trial Court Number: 92-5318.
Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 364 Ark. 398, 220 S.W.3d 645, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 776 (Ark., Dec. 15, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Arkansas Supreme Court charged the Special Masters to examine and evaluate action by the General Assembly and administrative action taken by the Department of Education to aid the court in determining whether there was compliance with its prior opinion.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court offered no conclusion on the precise definition of an adequate education as it deemed that to be a matter better left to the General Assembly and the State Department of Education. The supreme court determined that an adequate education had to be provided to all school children on a substantially equal basis with regard to curricula, facilities, and equipment. The supreme court disagreed that early-childhood education was a program that it could mandate to be funded at a certain level. If an adequate curriculum, adequate facilities, and adequate equipment could not be afforded to the school children in the smaller school districts due to a lack of sufficient economic resources, more efficient measures to afford that adequacy was inevitable. Neither the Masters nor the supreme court could gauge and assess the steps to be undertaken to mandate adequate and substantially equal facilities and equipment. The General Assembly did not fail to address the issue of teacher pay. Additional work needed to be done as to other deficiencies.


OUTCOME: The supreme court released jurisdiction of the case and issued the mandate.

 

281 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee


01-836


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


364 Ark. 398; 220 S.W.3d 645; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 776



December 15, 2005, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Supplemental opinion at Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 773 (Ark., Dec. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 364 Ark. 57, 216 S.W.3d 129, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 649 (Ark., Oct. 27, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Motion for Action upon the Special Masters' Report to the Supreme Court of Arkansas granted in part, denied in part.

Motion to Strike State's Brief denied.

Motion to Take Judicial Notice denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor school districts made a motion for action upon the Special Masters' Report after moving the Arkansas Supreme Court to recall its mandate, reappoint masters, and order the State defendants to show cause why they should not be held in civil contempt for failure to comply with the court's previous orders which were granted on June 9, 2005.


OVERVIEW: The districts moved to strike defendants' post-Masters' Report brief, specifically seeking to strike the State's arguments regarding justiciability and the separation of powers. The second motion filed asked the supreme court to take judicial notice of certain items filed in federal district court relating to the Pulaski County desegregation case. The supreme court rejected the State's argument and found that its refusal to review school funding under Ark. Const. art. 14, § 1 would be a complete abrogation of its judicial responsibility and would serve a severe disservice to the people of Arkansas. It viewed the governor and senators and representatives as dedicated public servants who were striving to meet the educational goals of the state. The supreme court agreed with the Masters' finding that the General Assembly did not comply with 2003 Ark. Acts 57. In connection with facilities funding, appropriations for the construction and repair for safe, dry, and healthy facilities were grossly underfunded and, thus, inadequate. The mandate was stayed until December 1, 2006, to allow the necessary time to correct the constitutional deficiencies.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike the State's brief was denied, and the motion to take judicial notice was denied; the issuance of the mandate was stayed to allow the necessary time to correct constitutional deficiencies.

 

282 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Weiss v. Geisbauer


04-1324


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


363 Ark. 508; 215 S.W.3d 628; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 607



October 13, 2005, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected December 6, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Sebastian Circuit Court; James Robert Marschewski, Judge.No. CV-03-1739-6.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sebastian County Circuit Court, Arkansas, granted judgment in favor of appellee business owner by finding that 1997 Ark. Acts 727, § 2, as written, was unconstitutional and concluded that the words "the Mississippi" should be struck from the statute and substituted with the words "a river." Appellant, Director of the Arkansas Department of Finance and Administration, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The director argued that the trial court erred by declaring the classification created by 1997 Ark. Acts 727, § 2, between border cities located on the Mississippi River and border cities that were not, violated the Arkansas and United States Constitution; and the trial court erred by declaring that the term "the Mississippi" should be struck from Ark. Code Ann. § 26-55-211 and that the term "a river" should be substituted in its place. The appellate court found that it could conceive how granting the border city exemption to certain territory within the state, regardless of the date of annexation, might assist certain cities to compete with other cities. However, the classification that limited the application of the Act only to border cities along the Mississippi River, a small portion of the state, was not rationally related to that purpose. The Act was clearly local and special legislation in violation of Ark. Const. amend. 14. Allowing the trial court to broaden the scope of Ark. Code Ann. § 26-55-211 by extending the statute's application from only river border cities on the Mississippi to all river border cities would be an intrusion into the legislative domain.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the finding that the classification in Ark. Code Ann. § 26-55-211 was unconstitutional; the judgment was reversed where the trial court did not have the authority to substitute language within the Act.
