284 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Whorton v. Dixon


04-1031


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


363 Ark. 330; 214 S.W.3d 225; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 516



September 29, 2005, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Saline Circuit Court; No. CIV. 2001-58-3, Grisham A. Phillips, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff patient's medical malpractice suit against defendant physician and defendant hospital, the patient challenged the constitutionality of Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-207(3) (1987). The Saline County Circuit Court, Arkansas, rejected the constitutional challenge. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient alleged negligence in the removal of lymph node masses because he severed a nerve during the process. She further alleged that the hospital was vicariously liable for the physician's negligent conduct. On appeal, the patient contended that § 16-114-207(3) was unconstitutional because it violated the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and the Equal Protection Clause in Ark. Const. art. 2, § 3. She also claimed that the challenged statute was unconstitutional under Ark. Const. amend. XIV. On appeal, the patient argued that strict scrutiny was the appropriate standard of review, but she never made that argument below. As a result, rational-basis review was the test accepted and used by the circuit court in reaching its decision, and the issue was not preserved for appellate review. Applying the rational basis test, the supreme court concluded that the patient had offered no proof that the general assembly acted arbitrarily, or that the legislation was not rationally related to achieving a stated objective. The patient failed to overcome the presumption of constitutionality. The supreme court did not address the patient's separation of powers argument.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

285 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Bowker v. State


CR 04-817


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


363 Ark. 345; 214 S.W.3d 243; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 556



September 29, 2005, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Benton Circuit Court; No. CR02-1158-1, Tom J. Keith, Judge.
 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Benton County Circuit Court (Arkansas) of second-degree sexual assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. There was substantial evidence that defendant made sexual contact with the victim. The victim testified that defendant fondled her breast and digitally penetrated her. Further, defendant admitted that the allegations were true. There was substantial evidence that the victim was under eighteen years of age and that defendant was the victim's temporary caretaker on the night that he made sexual contact with her. Defendant was in a position of trust, as he was a family friend to whom the victim's parents entrusted her, and he was in a position to care for the victim while she spent the night at his house. Both the victim's mother and stepfather testified at trial that they trusted defendant to care for their daughter as they would. Therefore, defendant fulfilled the role of "temporary caretaker." In addition, Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-125 was not void for vagueness because defendant was on notice as to the prohibited conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

286 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Rose v. Ark. State Plant Bd.


04-818


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


363 Ark. 281; 213 S.W.3d 607; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 504



September 22, 2005, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; James M. Moody, Jr., Judge; No. CV-03-9020.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commercial cotton growers challenged a judgment of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) that was entered in favor of appellee State Plant Board in the growers' action asserting that the Board's regulations requiring participation in a boll weevil eradication program, without referendum approval, was not authorized under the Arkansas Boll Weevil Suppression Eradication Act, Ark. Code Ann. §§ 2-16-601 to -617 (1996 and Supp. 2005).


OVERVIEW: The growers claimed that a referendum under Ark. Code Ann. § 2-16-614 was required before any assessment for an eradication program could be levied under Ark. Code Ann. § 2-16-610. The growers also challenged the constitutionality of the Act, claiming that the Board's actions resulted in their being treated differently from cotton growers in other zones that approved their assessments via referendum. The court held that Ark. Code Ann. § 2-16-610(b)(2) specifically authorized the Board to issue regulations requiring the growers to participate in and share the costs of an eradication program and that there was no limiting language in Ark. Code Ann. §§ 2-16-610 or 2-16-614 making the Board's authority dependent upon referendum approval. The court held there was no equal protection violation stemming from the fact that the Act authorized growers who elected to implement an eradication program to later elect to modify or recall that program because the Act created two separate means for eradication, one for the growers and one for the Board, but the Board's power was independent of any action taken by the growers. Thus, all growers were subject to the same authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

287 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. Finck


04-422


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


363 Ark. 183; 211 S.W.3d 532; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 458



July 1, 2005, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Polk Circuit Court; No. DR-2003-0120, Johnny R. Lineberger, Judge.
In re SCD, 358 Ark. 51, 186 S.W.3d 225, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 403 (Ark., June 17, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant birth mother challenged a judgment of the Polk County Circuit Court (Arkansas) that denied her request for certain lying-in expenses in a paternity action, contending that the trial court's order violated Ark. Code Ann. § 9-10-110 (Repl. 2002).


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed an adoption petition filed by the mother and prospective adoptive parents due to a lack of the biological father's consent after the trial court learned that he had legitimated the baby as provided in Ark. Code Ann. § 9-9-206(a)(2). The mother then sought lying-in expenses from the father, which included expenses for counseling, room and board, maternity clothes, schooling expenses, lost income, travel and telephone expenses, and medical expenses paid by the adoptive parents. The trial court denied certain expenses. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that under Ark. Code Ann. § 9-10-110, lying-in expenses included expenses that were directly connected to the birth of the a healthy infant and did not normally include items such as maternity clothes, lost wages, or counseling that were for the benefit of the mother. The court noted that the trial court erred in its interpretation of who could receive payment of lying-in expenses under § 9-10-110, which allowed expenses in favor of the person incurring the expense, if claimed. The court found that the mother failed to prove that she incurred the expenses allegedly paid by the adoptive parents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

288 of 594 DOCUMENTS


State Farm Fire & Cas. Co. v. Andrews


04-1336


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


363 Ark. 67; 210 S.W.3d 896; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 401



June 23, 2005, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected March 14, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Craighead Circuit Court, No. CV 2003-461, Western District; David Burnett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer challenged a decision from the Craighead County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which entered partial summary judgment in favor of appellee insured in a dispute over insurance proceeds after a fire. The insurer also challenged the award of statutory penalties and attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The insured suffered a fire loss on her residence. Shortly thereafter, the property was foreclosed upon by a mortgagee. The insurer paid the proceeds of the insurance policy to the mortgagee. The insured then sought to recover payment under the policy. After her motion for partial summary judgment was granted, the insurer sought review. On appeal, the court determined that the insurer lacked standing to challenge the foreclosure proceeding based on the mortgagee's lack of knowledge of the fire damage. The insurer was not a party to the mortgage or a third-party beneficiary. Because the insurer's only interest was to pay the insurance proceeds to the rightful owner, it had no interest in the foreclosure itself. Other arguments related to the foreclosure were deemed meritless or the insurer failed to cite any authority to support its position. The trial court erred in awarding fees and penalties under Ark. Code Ann. § 23-79-208. The record did not support the argument that the insurer failed to pay. The fact that the amount awarded was within 20 percent of the amount demanded was of no significance because the amount awarded was the exact amount tendered and rejected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the insured, but reversed the statutory damages and attorney's fees.

 

289 of 594 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kelley


CR 04-1300


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


362 Ark. 636; 210 S.W.3d 93; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 390



June 16, 2005, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; No. CR04-327, John W. Langston, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pulaski County Circuit Court, Fourth Division, Arkansas, granted defendant's motion to suppress. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that evidence seized during an inventory pursuant to the impoundment of defendant's car for failure to provide proof of insurance was lawful, and that the circuit court erred in granting defendant's motion to suppress. The State argued that while Ark. Code Ann. § 27-22-104 did not specifically provide for the impoundment of a motor vehicle that lacked proof of valid insurance, it did specifically prohibit it. The appellate court determined that the statute called for the officer to impound only the vehicle's license plate, not the car, in the event the driver was unable to present proof of insurance. Ark. R. Crim. P. 12.6 did not authorize the impoundment of a vehicle, but merely the search after a car had been properly impounded or retained. Without some independent and proper basis for the impoundment itself, the authorization to search pursuant was inapplicable. The statute required the officer to remove and impound the license plate. While both officers testified that defendant's insurance card was expired, other witnesses testified that the car was insured. Neither officer had any record at all of what they discovered in their search of defendant's vehicle.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee


01-836


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


362 Ark. 520; 210 S.W.3d 28; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 356



June 9, 2005, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 6, 2006.
Request granted Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 211 S.W.3d 543, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 461 (Ark., Aug. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

DISPOSITION: Motions to Recall Mandate and Reappoint Masters granted.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant school districts requested that a mandate be recalled in a school-district funding matter.


OVERVIEW: The school districts' core assertions were that the Arkansas General Assembly reneged on its legislative commitments and failed to comply with landmark legislation. The supreme court considered the following issues: (1) the supreme court's jurisdiction to hear the motions; (2) whether the legislature at its 2005 regular session retreated from its prior actions to comply with the supreme court's directives; (3) whether the foundation-funding levels for the next biennium assured a continual level of adequate funding for Arkansas students; and (4) whether the legislature's commitment to facilities funding met the adequacy criterion. The supreme court's determination that Arkansas' public school funding system did not pass constitutional muster dated back 22 years. The supreme court was determined not to waver in its commitment to the goal of an adequate and substantially equal education for all Arkansas students.


OUTCOME: The supreme court recalled its mandate, and it reappointed masters. The masters were directed to furnish the supreme court with a report on or before a set date.

 

291 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Villines v. Harris


04-568


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


362 Ark. 393; 208 S.W.3d 763; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 310



May 19, 2005, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; No. CV 97-8317, John S. Patterson, Judge.
Villines v. Harris, 361 Ark. 111, 204 S.W.3d 520, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 132 (Ark., Mar. 3, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A county court held that appellant county violated the civil rights of county taxpayers under the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. Appellee citizen then asserted a right to damages in the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Arkansas. The circuit court denied the county's motion to dismiss based on a lack of subject-matter jurisdiction and granted the citizen's motion for summary judgment. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen first asserted that the appeal had to be dismissed because the notice of appeal was not filed within 30 days of the circuit court's order allowing for damages. However, the order referred to an attached letter opinion. In that letter opinion, the circuit court stated that damages were yet to be assessed. The Arkansas Supreme Court had on numerous occasions held that for an order to be final, it had to establish the amount of damages. To the extent that Hartwick v. Hill, 73 S.W. 3d 15 (2002), was inconsistent thereon, it was overruled. A subsequent order directing payment of damages was the first order that definitively set out the damages. The county's appeal from that order was timely. However, the county court (any county court), lacked subject-matter jurisdiction over claims of violation of the federal constitution (in the case at bar, deprivation of constitutional rights), and its judgment in that regard was null and void. Jurisdiction of a county court was limited to those subjects set forth in Ark. Const. art. VII, § 28. The citizen was basing her action in circuit court on a void order from the county court. Thus, the circuit court's judgment was also void.


OUTCOME: There was no valid judgment from the county court for the circuit court to enforce regarding the claims of civil rights violations. The judgment of the circuit court is void.

Hester v. State


CR 04-875


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


362 Ark. 373; 208 S.W.3d 747; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 312



May 19, 2005, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; No. CR2002-1339, Timothy Davis Fox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) that convicted him of possession of pseudoephedrine with intent to manufacture methamphetamine, manufacture of a controlled substance, possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, possession of drug paraphernalia with intent to manufacture methamphetamine, and maintaining a drug premises, and that sentenced him to 30 years in prison and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because he was illegally seized during a knock-and-talk procedure by police after he refused consent to search his home and was denied reentry into his home for four hours. The court found that police went to defendant's home to question him about manufacturing methamphetamine based on an informant's tip. Defendant denied consent to search but a guest at the house came out and confirmed that there were drugs and paraphernalia inside. The court held that the informant's tip, coupled with the guest's information, gave police probable cause to believe the house contained evidence of a crime. The officers also reasonably believed that defendant would destroy the evidence if not restrained. Thus, the court held that the limited restraint of defendant for a short time did not violate the Ark. Const. art. 2, § 15 or the Fourth Amendment. The court noted that defendant's home was not searched until a search warrant was obtained and held that defendant's motion to dismiss the possession with intent to manufacture charges was properly denied because they were not lesser-included offenses of the manufacturing offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

293 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Parham


04-929


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


362 Ark. 352; 208 S.W.3d 162; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 300



May 12, 2005, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sebastian Circuit Court; Norman Wilkinson, Judge. No. CV-2004-226 (V)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sebastian County Circuit Court (Arkansas) dismissed a medical negligence claim filed by appellant, the administrator of the estate of the decedent. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss that had been filed by appellee doctors and a medical center claiming that the statute of limitations had run on the suit. The administrator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The administrator argued that the trial court erred in granting the motion to dismiss, and challenged the constitutionality of the statute of limitations under the Medical Malpractice Act, codified at Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-201 et seq., (1987 and Supp. 2003). The issue was whether the cause of action was barred by the medical-malpractice statute of limitations in a wrongful-death action. The cause of action was controlled by the 2-year medical malpractice statute of limitations set forth in Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-203. Under § 16-114-203(a), all actions for medical injury shall be commenced within 2 years after the cause of action accrued. Under § 16-114-203(b), the date of the accrual of the cause of action shall be the date of the wrongful act complained of and no other time. The alleged negligence occurred on January 26, 2001, when the chest x-ray, which allegedly showed an aortic aneurysm, was read by a doctor as "clear." The other doctor's alleged negligence occurred on January 29, 2001, when he noted that there was "no acute disease." The complaint was filed on February 25, 2004, which was 3 years past the date of the alleged misreadings of the deceased's chest x-rays.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Flowers v. State


CR 04-853


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


362 Ark. 193; 208 S.W.3d 113; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 269



May 5, 2005, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 14, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Columbia Circuit Court; Fifth Division; No. CR-2003-66; Larry Chandler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Columbia County Circuit Court, Fifth Division (Arkansas), of capital murder and aggravated robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in failing to suppress his custodial statement because he did not make a knowing and intelligent waiver of his rights nor was his statement voluntarily made. The supreme court disagreed. Defendant verbally indicated that he understood his Miranda rights. He also initialed each of his responses and signed the waiver. An interviewer stated that during the process, defendant appeared to be alert and responsive and did not seem to have any problem understanding his rights as they were explained to him. He also stated that at no time during the interview did he see any indication that defendant suffered from mental retardation, nor did defendant give responses that were not age appropriate. The interviewer further testified that initially defendant denied any involvement in the crime but that he ultimately gave a statement regarding his involvement in the robbery and murder. The interviewer wrote out defendant's statement and then read it to defendant, who signed at the end of the statement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

295 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Ford-Robinson


04-1235


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


362 Ark. 232; 208 S.W.3d 140; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 280



May 5, 2005, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Robinson v. Ford-Robinson, 126 S. Ct. 424, 163 L. Ed. 2d 323, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 7336 (U.S., Oct. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; No. DR2003-2456. Mackie McClellan Pierce, Judge.
Robinson v. Ford-Robinson, 88 Ark. App. 151, 196 S.W.3d 503, 2004 Ark. App. LEXIS 739 (Ark. Ct. App., Oct. 27, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order from the Arkansas Court of Appeals, which upheld a decision awarding appellee stepmother visitation in a divorce action.


OVERVIEW: The father had sole custody of his son, who was less than two years old when the stepmother moved in with them. When the father and stepmother divorced, the father was granted full custody of the child, with limited visitation awarded to the stepmother. It was held that the stepmother had stood in loco parentis to the child since he was 18 months old. The lower court upheld the decision. On review, the court found that the father admitted that he had described the stepmother as the child's mother in both conversations and in writing. He also acknowledged that he had executed powers of attorney for the stepmother so that she could get medical care for the child when he was away in the military. The stepmother was the only mother that the child had ever known, and he did not know she was not his birth mother until first grade. She had served as his mother for six years. She described herself as the child's mother; he called her "mommy." The fact that she told the father that one of the reasons she left was because she was a nanny, rather than a wife or mother, appeared to have had more to do with her impression of her relationship with the father than with the child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court.

State v. Fudge


CR 04-83


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


361 Ark. 412; 206 S.W.3d 850; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 226



April 14, 2005, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by State v. Fudge, 206 S.W.3d 850, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 337 (Ark., 2005)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at, Appeal dismissed by Fudge v. Hobbs, 2012 Ark. 80, 2012 Ark. LEXIS 85 (Ark., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Court, First Division; No. CR-1998-626, Marion Humphrey, Judge.
Fudge v. State, 354 Ark. 148, 120 S.W.3d 600, 2003 Ark. LEXIS 486 (Ark., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on appeal; affirmed on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder in the Pulaski County Circuit Court, First Division (Arkansas), and sentenced to death. Upon reconsidering defendant's motion for relief under Ark. R. Crim. P. 37, the circuit court concluded that defendant's penalty-phase counsel was ineffective for failing to object to evidence of a prior conviction for battery and granted defendant a new sentencing hearing. The State appealed, and defendant cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his counsel's failure to object to the introduction of evidence of a first-degree-battery conviction constituted ineffective assistance of counsel. Three justices argued that counsel's assistance was not ineffective because, the evidence showed, defendant had in fact been convicted of battery. A majority of the court, however, affirmed the grant of a new sentencing hearing. Their opinion was that the State had not argued that counsel was effective, merely that defendant was not prejudiced, and that the court could not reverse on an argument that the State had not made. The court affirmed the circuit court's rejection of defendant's other ineffective assistance claims, finding that his counsel's failure to present allegedly mitigating evidence of defendant's alcoholism and violent family history was strategic.


OUTCOME: A divided court affirmed the circuit court's finding that a new sentencing hearing was warranted based on the admission of a prior battery conviction and affirmed the circuit court's denial of relief on defendant's other claims of ineffective assistance.

Teston v. Ark. State Bd. of Chiropractic Examiners


04-420


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


361 Ark. 300; 206 S.W.3d 796; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 214



April 7, 2005, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 14, 2006.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Teston v. Ark. State Bd. of Chiropractic Exam'rs, 126 S. Ct. 480, 163 L. Ed. 2d 363, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 7669 (U.S., 2005)
Related proceeding at Fryar v. Touchstone Physical Therapy, Inc., 2006 Ark. LEXIS 6 (Ark., Jan. 5, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court, No. CV 03-502, Timothy Davis Fox, Judge.
Teston v. Ark. State Bd. of Chiropractic Examiners, 2004 Ark. App. LEXIS 479 (Ark. Ct. App., June 23, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Arkansas State Board of Chiropractic Examiners fined appellant, a licensed physical therapist, for practicing chiropractic without a license in violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 17-81-303(a)(1) (2002). The Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) affirmed. The therapist sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The therapist was not a licensed chiropractor. Two of his patients testified that he manipulated their spines in a manner similar to that of their chiropractors, causing their spines to "pop." An expert testified that the popping sounds indicated that the therapist manipulated the patients' spines by moving them outside of their normal range of motion; under § 17-81-303(a)(1) of the Arkansas Chiropractic Practices Act, Ark. Code Ann. § 17-81-101 et seq. (2002), only chiropractors could perform "spinal manipulations," as defined in Ark. Code Ann. § 17-81-102(7). The appellate court, noting that the credibility and weight of the evidence was within the Board's discretion, found that the evidence was sufficient to support the Board's decision, and that it made the requisite findings of fact under Ark. Code Ann. § 25-15-210(b)(2) (2002). The therapist's actions did not fall under the Act's "physical therapy exemption," Ark. Code Ann. § 17-81-302(3), as physical therapy was defined in Ark. Code Ann. § 17-93-102(6) as passive movement within the joint's normal range of motion, "excluding spinal manipulation." The therapist's constitutional argument was not preserved for appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Mashburn v. Norris


No. 05-23


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2005 Ark. LEXIS 192



March 31, 2005, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIRCUIT COURT OF LINCOLN COUNTY, LCIV 2004-68-1, HON. BERLIN C. JONES, JUDGE.
Mashburn v. State, 2004 Ark. App. LEXIS 468 (Ark. Ct. App., June 23, 2004)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED; MOTION MOOT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Lincoln County (Arkansas), which denied his application for a writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner sought an extension of time to file his brief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner entered a plea of guilty in 2001 for failure to register as a sex offender. He was sentenced to serve two years' imprisonment, with the imposition of an additional four years' imprisonment suspended. In 2003, the suspended portion of the term of imprisonment was revoked because petitioner had failed to comply with the conditions of the suspended sentence. He was sentenced to serve 36 months' imprisonment. The revocation order was upheld on appeal. In 2004, petitioner filed a pro se petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The petition was denied. On appeal, petitioner sought an extension of time to file his brief. The court determined that it did not need to consider the motion for an extension of time because it was apparent that petitioner could not prevail in the appeal if it was permitted to go forward because he failed to demonstrate a ground for the writ. None of his claims were sufficient to establish that his commitment was invalid on its face or that the trial court was without jurisdiction. Clearly, petitioner failed to meet his burden of showing probable cause that he was illegally detained.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal. The court held that petitioner's motion for an extension of time was moot.

 

300 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Dickson v. Fletcher


04-741


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


361 Ark. 244; 206 S.W.3d 229; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 200



March 31, 2005, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; Ellen B. Brantley, Judge. No. 93-106.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The divorce decree purportedly set forth all of the parties' properties and indebtedness and divided those properties and debts between appellant ex-husband and appellee ex-wife. The wife subsequently filed a motion in which she alleged the husband had committed fraud during their divorce proceeding and asked the Circuit Court of Pulaski County (Arkansas) to divide the disputed stock, which the trial court did. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that, at the time of the divorce, the husband introduced into evidence a statement of net worth which failed to disclose his ownership of the shares of the disputed stock. The husband never denied that his responses to the wife's discovery requests omitted the disputed stock and that he failed to supplement his discovery responses. In addition, the husband neither denied that his statement of net worth at the time of the divorce omitted the disputed stock, nor did he deny that he presented false testimony by stating his statement of worth was complete. Thus, the trial court did not err in ruling that the husband had committed fraud. The supreme court found that the wife's proof of constructive fraud was sufficient to reopen the divorce under Ark. R. Civ. P. 60(c)(4). Additionally, because the supreme court amended Rule 60(c)(4), to supply a new or more appropriate remedy to enforce an existing right and obligation in order to avoid unjust results, the amendment to Rule 60(c)(4) was remedial in nature and appropriately applied retroactively. Thus, the trial court did not err in modifying the divorce decree where the wife only showed intrinsic fraud.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

301 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Old Republic Sur. Co. v. McGhee


04-704


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


360 Ark. 562; 203 S.W.3d 94; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 87



February 10, 2005, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Ark. Bd. of Collection Agencies v. McGhee, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 43 (Ark., Jan. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pope Circuit Court, First Division; John S. Patterson, Judge. No. CV-2003-272.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant surety sought review of an order from the Pope County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which denied its motion to dismiss and granted plaintiff individual's motion for summary judgment in an action for the release of a bond to satisfy a judgment that the individual had previously won against a payday lender.


OVERVIEW: The surety provided a bond for a payday lender. The individual brought an action against the surety seeking release of the bond to satisfy a judgment that she had previously won against the payday lender. The surety moved to dismiss the action, asserting that the trial court lacked jurisdiction because the individual had failed to exhaust her administrative remedies before the Arkansas State Board of Collection Agencies (Board). The individual moved for summary judgment. The trial court denied the surety's motion to dismiss and granted the motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that the trial court lacked jurisdiction over the case because the individual failed to exhaust her administrative remedies. It was not futile to require the individual to exhaust her administrative remedies before proceeding with her claim in court, even though the Board ruled against her on a similar claim. She failed to demonstrate with certainty that the Board's decision would be the same in the current case. By skipping the crucial step before the Board, the individual deprived the agency of the opportunity to correct any mistakes that it might have made in the previous case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

302 of 594 DOCUMENTS


McGhee v. Ark. State Bd. of Collection Agencies


04-199


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


360 Ark. 363; 201 S.W.3d 375; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 39



January 20, 2005, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 2, 2006.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by McGhee v. Ark. State Bd. of Collection Agencies, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 568 (Ark., Nov. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; Barry Sims, Judge. No. 2003-4837.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers filed a suit against appellees, the Arkansas State Board of Collections Agencies and associated individuals, maintaining that all transactions under the Check-Casher's Act (Act), Ark. Code Ann. § 23-52-101 et seq., involved interest rates that violated the usury provisions of Ark. Const. art. 16, § 13. The Pulaski County Circuit Court, Arkansas, granted appellees' motion to dismiss. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers argued that the circuit court not only erred in dismissing the case, but also in determining that it could not rule on the constitutional issue and in failing to grant their partial summary-judgment motion. The appellate court found that the circuit court erred when it found that the claim was barred by an unrelated administrative claim, where only one person filed the administrative complaint and the issues were not the same. The pendency of the administrative process did not prevent the taxpayers from filing a new and separate cause of action for illegal exaction. The taxpayers' allegations that all plaintiffs were Arkansas residents and taxpayers were sufficient to withstand a motion to dismiss for lack of standing. The complaint sufficiently stated a cause of action for illegal exaction. The misapplication of public funds was one avenue for establishing a claim for illegal exaction. Because the taxpayers successfully pled an illegal exaction claim, the doctrine of sovereign immunity was not applicable. All licensed check-cashers in Arkansas would be members of the class and parties to the illegal exaction suit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

303 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Polston v. State


CR 04-651


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


360 Ark. 317; 201 S.W.3d 406; 2005 Ark. LEXIS 36



January 20, 2005, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Independence Circuit Court; NO. CR03-218, John Dan Kemp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Independence County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which ordered defendant to submit to deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) testing after a felony drug conviction.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted, he was ordered to submit to DNA testing under Ark. Code Ann. § 12-12-1109(a) (2003). He contended that this requirement violated his Fourth Amendment rights. In affirming, the court adopted the totality of the circumstances test to determine if the DNA collection statute constituted an unreasonable search and seizure under the Fourth Amendment. The court noted that a felon's expectation of privacy was diminished. Moreover, the intrusion occasioned by a blood test was not significant on defendant's privacy and bodily integrity. In contrast, the State's interest in solving crimes was substantial. As such, the collection and maintenance of DNA samples was reasonable. Since defendant failed to show that the court's treatment of Ark. Const. art. 2, § 15 in relation to searches in the penal context was inconsistent with the Fourth Amendment, no further analysis was required. Finally, the court found that there was no Fourth Amendment violation based on the right of privacy separate from the right to be free of unreasonable searches and seizures.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

304 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Engram v. State


CR 99-928


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


360 Ark. 140; 200 S.W.3d 367; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 788



December 16, 2004, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Engram v. Arkansas, 545 U.S. 1142, 125 S. Ct. 2965, 162 L. Ed. 2d 893, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 5087 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; John B. Plegge, Judge. No. CR 97-2685.
Engram v. State, 341 Ark. 196, 15 S.W.3d 678, 2000 Ark. LEXIS 215 (Ark., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Motion to recall mandate and reopen case denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a motion to recall the mandate and reopen his case after a federal court dismissed his amended habeas corpus petition seeking relief from his capital murder and rape convictions and death sentence therefor. Petitioner claimed that he was mentally retarded and that his execution was barred under the United States Supreme Court's holding that execution of mentally retarded individuals violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OVERVIEW: The holding relied upon by petitioner came out after the mandate was issued, and the federal court in which petitioner filed his habeas petition held that the legal basis for his claim was unavailable to him during the state proceedings. However, the court held that petitioner could have availed himself of Ark Code Ann. § 5-4-618(b) (Repl. 1997), which prohibited execution of mentally retarded defendants, but that he failed to do so. Petitioner never even presented evidence that he was mentally retarded, and a forensic psychologist testified that petitioner's score on an intelligence test did not indicate mental retardation. Thus, there was no merit to petitioner's contention that he could not have made his federal constitutional argument previously. In addition, petitioner's state court remedies with respect to postconviction relief had been exhausted, as he agreed with the assessment that there were no issues appropriate for such relief and the time for filing a petition was long since past. State habeas relief was not a proper avenue for petitioner, as the sentencing court possessed jurisdiction, and the sentence of death was not invalid.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's motion to recall the mandate and reopen his case, and it held that, because petitioner exhausted his right to assert a mental retardation defense in state court, he was left to pursue any such relief in the federal courts.

 

305 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Flowers


04-449


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


359 Ark. 443; 198 S.W.3d 520; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 722



November 18, 2004, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by Jones v. Flowers, 126 S. Ct. 35, 162 L. Ed. 2d 933, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 5416 (U.S., 2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Jones v. Flowers, 126 S. Ct. 1708, 164 L. Ed. 2d 415, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3451 (U.S., Apr. 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; Sixth Division; Timothy Davis Fox, Judge. No. CIV2003-8565.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pulaski County Circuit Court, Sixth Division (Arkansas), entered an order finding that Ark. Code Ann. § 26-37-301 (Repl. 1997) complied with the constitutional requirements of due process and granted appellee tax sale purchaser's and the tax commissioner's motions for summary judgment and denied appellant owners' motion. The purchaser's counterclaim for unlawful detainer was granted. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners argued that the trial court erred in ruling that the State was not required to locate their correct address after the tax-sale notices were returned to the State unclaimed, arguing that the trial court erred in ruling that the State's sale of their property was constitutional under Ark. Code Ann. § 26-37-301. They further argued that due process required the State to conduct a reasonable search of public records in an attempt to ascertain the husband's correct address before selling his property. The purchaser and the commissioner countered that an attempt to provide actual notice was all that was required in order to comply with the requirements of due process. The Supreme Court of Arkansas agreed. There was simply not a requirement in § 26-37-301 that the State had to try to locate the correct address of a delinquent taxpayer when a notice was returned unclaimed. And such action was not required in order to comply with the constitutional dictates of due process. The State attempted to provide the owners with notice, both via certified mail and through publication in the newspaper and complied with the provisions of § 26-37-301. The tax sale was valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

306 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Ark. Hearing Instrument Dispenser Bd. v. Vance


03-1365


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


359 Ark. 325; 197 S.W.3d 495; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 640



November 4, 2004, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Cleburne Circuit Court; No. CV-02-182-4, Timothy M. Weaver, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Circuit Court reversed; Board affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cleburne County Circuit Court, Arkansas, reversed the findings of appellant Arkansas Hearing Instrument Dispenser Board and concluded that there was not substantial evidence to support the Board's findings of violations of two standards of conduct and that the disciplinary procedures violated the rights of appellee dispenser to due process. The Board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court's inquiry was whether there was substantial evidence to supporting the findings. Based upon the testimony of the customer, there was substantial evidence to support the findings of fact that the dispenser, in making a sale to the customer, represented that she had to purchase a hearing instrument on January 12th to receive the discount from the coupon that was valid until January 13th. The customer testified that she continued to experience problems with her instruments, and after three trips to the dispenser's office within one week, she went to a doctor who wrote a letter stating that the hearing instruments were causing ulcers in her left ear. There was not insufficient evidence upon which the Board could base its findings of fact. Ark. Code Ann. § 17-84-101 made it clear that there was ample guidance for the reasonable person in determining whether a course of conduct was ethical or unethical under the statutes. The dispenser did not offer any authority for his proposition that the statute regulated a fundamental right. The statute was given greater leeway in a constitutional challenge for vagueness as it was a statute that regulated business activity.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was reversed; the judgment of the Board was affirmed.

 

307 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Shipley, Inc. v. Long


04-136


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


359 Ark. 208; 195 S.W.3d 911; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 602; 33 Media L. Rep. 1110



October 21, 2004, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment granted by Shipley, Inc. v. Long, 454 F. Supp. 2d 819, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 30101 (E.D. Ark., Nov. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Arkansas Supreme Court's Responses to the Certified Questions from the United States District Court, Eastern District of Arkansas, Western Division, Honorable G. Thomas Eisele, District Judge.
Shipley, Inc. v. Long, 356 Ark. 220, 148 S.W.3d 746, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 98 (Ark., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff booksellers brought suit before the United States District Court, Eastern District of Arkansas, against defendant state prosecuting attorneys. The complaint sought to enjoin the enforcement of, and to declare facially unconstitutional and void, the newly amended portions of Ark. Code Ann. § 5-68-502 (amended 2003). The federal district court certified questions, asking for a statutory interpretation.


OVERVIEW: Ark. Code Ann. § 5-68-502 (amended 2003) required material deemed "harmful to minors" to be obstructed from view and physically segregated. The question put forth by the district court was whether the statute intended to protect all minors from exposure to materials harmful to minors? The supreme court answered in the affirmative. The next question was whether a bookseller or librarian allowed a minor to view any material that was harmful to minors by simply shelving and displaying such material? If material harmful to minors was shelved on a bookshelf, even without some other effort made to draw attention to it, it was displayed within the meaning of the statute. Even if a book only had "harmful" content, but not a "harmful" cover, the bookseller could still be subject to prosecution, if that book were not obstructed from view and physically segregated. The booksellers were allowed to choose the method best suited to their individual establishments; it remained for the federal court to ultimately determine whether the First Amendment rights of booksellers, librarians, and their adult customers were violated.


OUTCOME: The supreme court responded to the certified questions.

Populist Party of Ark. v. Chesterfield


04-994


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


359 Ark. 58; 195 S.W.3d 354; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 811



October 1, 2004, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 7, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; Timothy Davis Fox, Judge, No. CV 2004-9755.
Populist Party of Ark. v. Chesterfield, 358 Ark. 482, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 821 (Ark., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Writ of mandamus vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, political party, presidential candidate, and vice-presidential candidate, appealed the writ of mandate granted by the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Arkansas, in favor of appellee democratic party that removed the Presidential and Vice Presidential candidates' names from the certified list of candidates running for office.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the writ of mandate and held that appellants' petitions to place the Presidential and the Vice Presidential candidate on the state's ballot were insufficient because the individuals who signed the petitions did not state the Presidential and Vice Presidential candidates were "their candidates." Rather, the petitions stated a desire to have "the" particular candidates on the ballot. The state supreme court vacated the writ of mandate and held that nothing in Ark. Code Ann. § 7-8-302(5)(B) (Supp. 2003) required appellants to use a form contained in the 2004 Candidate Information handbook published by the Arkansas Secretary of State's Office. More importantly, there was no requirement that petitioners declared their intention to actually vote for the candidate on the petition. To make such a requirement would cause the provision to be unconstitutional, as it would infringe upon the fundamental civil liberty of the secret ballot. Thus, the Secretary of State's office was ordered to certify the ballots with the names of the Presidential and Vice Presidential candidates.


OUTCOME: The writ of mandamus was vacated.

Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee


01-836


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


359 Ark. 49; 194 S.W.3d 193; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 535



September 30, 2004, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 358 Ark. 137, 189 S.W.3d 1, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 425 (Ark., June 18, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Motions for Attorney's Fees and Costs; denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, attorneys, filed a request for a ruling on a pending motion for attorney fees from appellee, State of Arkansas, for legal work and costs for work done on behalf of appellant, school district, after January 1, 2004.


OVERVIEW: In November 2002, the court awarded $ 3,397,035 in attorneys fees and costs to the attorneys based on the court's previous opinion that the State of Arkansas had waived a sovereign-immunity defense by its actions. On January 1, 2004, the mandate issued in the case stated that the parties each bore their own costs on appeal, and, on January 22, 2004, the court recalled the mandate. In March 2004, the court denied the attorneys' motion for additional costs and attorney fees incurred during certain time frames and refused to clarify what fees and costs might be forthcoming after January 22, 2004. The second mandate was issued on September 9, 2004. Now the attorneys requested fees and costs incurred after January 1, 2004. The court ruled that what occurred after January 1, 2004, was a separate matter, though the docket number remained the same. The court could not say that the State of Arkansas waived its sovereign-immunity defense with respect to any claims for fees and costs incurred post-January 1, 2004.


OUTCOME: The request was denied.

Davis v. Williamson


03-682


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


359 Ark. 33; 194 S.W.3d 197; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 536



September 30, 2004, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 4, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Washington Circuit Court, No. J96-953-3; Stacey A. Zimmerman, Judge.
Davis v. Williamson, 353 Ark. 225, 114 S.W.3d 216, 2003 Ark. LEXIS 256 (Ark., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Washington County Circuit Court (Arkansas) denied appellant mother an award of attorney's fees in her paternity action. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the trial court's order, the court noted that fees could be granted under Ark. Code Ann. § 9-10-109 (Repl. 2002), but that fees were discretionary. It also noted that although the mother argued that disparity in income should require a grant of fees, that reason alone was not a basis for an award of attorney's fees. The court, in evaluating the services of the mother's counsel, stated that beyond complex financial issues, the case presented straight forward legal issues. The mother argued that a showing of bias in the case prior to filing a motion for attorney's fees was relevant to show bias and an abuse of discretion in the decision on the fees. The appellate court considered every allegation of bias she argued. The trial court found the billings were inadequate and some were inflated. Examples of deficiencies were given in the order. The trial court was of the opinion that counsel's billings were unreliable, that too much time was spent on a number of types of items, and that counsel exhibited a lack of expertise. The trial court considered the proper factors in deciding the mother's attorney's fee motion. She failed to show an abuse of discretion by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

311 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Fletcher v. Norris


CR 03-929


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2004 Ark. LEXIS 508



September 23, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY. CV 2002-848-5. HONORABLE FRED D. DAVIS, III, JUDGE.
Fletcher v. Davis, 2003 Ark. LEXIS 372 (Ark., June 19, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed a judgment by the Jefferson County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which denied his petition for a declaratory judgment; the inmate claimed, inter alia, that he was entitled to parole pursuant to Act no. 50, Ark. Acts 1968.


OVERVIEW: After the inmate was convicted of murder and battery, he was twice convicted of escape and other crimes. The state supreme court held that the inmate's parole eligibility was determined by the law in effect at the time the crime was committed. Pursuant to Ark. Stat. Ann. § 43-2807(b)(1) (Supp. 1971), the inmate would become eligible for parole after having served one-third of the time to which his life sentence was commuted to a term of years by executive clemency. Because executive clemency was denied, the inmate was not eligible for parole. Because Act no. 50, Ark. Acts 1968 did not change the inmate's parole eligibility, it was not being unconstitutionally applied as an ex post facto law. Accordingly, the trial court did not error in denying the inmate's petition for declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

312 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Porter v. State


CR 03-1307


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


358 Ark. 403; 191 S.W.3d 531; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 489



September 16, 2004, Opinion delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From The Sebastian County Circuit Court. No. CR-2002-675. J. Michael Fitzhugh, Judge, affirmed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sebastian County Circuit Court (Arkansas) convicted defendant of two counts of aggravated robbery and one count of capital murder. He was sentenced to two life sentences running consecutively for the aggravated-robbery charges and life without parole for the capital-murder charge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence was sufficient to establish defendant caused the victim's death under circumstances manifesting extreme indifference to the value of human life. Defendant admitted pointing a loaded gun at the victim in the course of a robbery. Such conduct by itself constituted a manifestation of extreme indifference. Also, he fired a gun at an unarmed victim from less than three feet away, further indicating extreme indifference. He repeatedly threatened to shoot all three victims throughout the ordeal. He used a gun to shoot the victim at close range and admitted the shooting was intentional. He not only cursed the victim as he died, but threatened the other victims and locked them in a room so he could get away. These actions were sufficient to show premeditation and deliberation. Defendant's own statements provided enough evidence to sustain his conviction for aggravated robbery, as he admitted to having the purpose to commit felony theft, employing and threatening to employ force on his victims, and using a gun during the robbery. There was a presumption that the model instruction was a correct statement of the law, and defendant cited no authority sufficient to overcome it.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Meadows v. State


CR 03-1175


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


358 Ark. 396; 191 S.W.3d 527; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 492



September 16, 2004, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Related proceeding at Meadows v. State, 360 Ark. 5, 199 S.W.3d 634, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 767 (Ark., 2004)

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Carroll Circuit Court; No. CR2002-127(B), Alan D. Epley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Carroll County Circuit Court, Arkansas, convicting and sentencing him for capital murder and arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant told a neighbor that he tried to get his live-in girlfriend out of his trailer home, but that the trailer home exploded and the victim died. An investigator visited the fire scene to discover the remains of a human body. The medical examiner testified that the victim died of smoke inhalation. The jury unanimously found him guilty of arson and capital murder. On appeal, defendant claimed that the circuit court erred in admitting a witness's testimony as to where the fire originated. However, this specific argument was not made to the circuit court as part of defendant's motions for directed verdict. Thus, the matter was not preserved for appellate review. The appellate court could not address defendant's argument that the circuit court erred in convicting him of arson, because it was a lesser-included offense of capital murder. The argument was not sufficiently developed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee


01-836


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


358 Ark. 137; 189 S.W.3d 1; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 464



September 9, 2004, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion granted by Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 362 Ark. 251, 208 S.W.3d 93, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 282 (Ark., May 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 358 Ark. 137, 189 S.W.3d 1, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 425 (Ark., June 18, 2004)

Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee


01-836


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


358 Ark. 137; 189 S.W.3d 1; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 425



June 18, 2004, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 13, 2006.
Motion denied by Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 359 Ark. 49, 194 S.W.3d 193, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 535 (Ark., Aug. 30, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 189 S.W.3d 1, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 464 (Ark., Sept. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 357 Ark. 274, 161 S.W.3d 787, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 251 (Ark., Apr. 29, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Supplemental opinion


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter was before the court for consideration of objections and comments filed by appellants school district and appellees, governor and others, regarding the Masters' report pertaining to what administrative and legislative steps had been taken by the General Assembly and Department of Education to comply with the court's opinion in Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, known as Lakeview IIII.


OVERVIEW: The common theme throughout much of the oral arguments was that if the court did not serve as a "watchdog" agency to assure full compliance with Lake View III, the General Assembly would fully implement what it had already begun to ensure equal education to both poor and wealthy school districts within Arkansas as required by Ark. Const. art. 14, § 1. The court referred the case to Masters to determine what legislative and administrative action had been taken to comply with Lake View III. The Masters filed a summary of an Adequacy Study commissioned by the General Assembly that focused on school finance, teacher compensation, and accountability, and concluded that it was thorough in its approach. The Masters then detailed the significant legislation that had been enacted to implement and fund the recommendations of the Adequacy Study and the rules adopted by the Department of Education to implement the legislation. The court accepted the Masters' report and released its jurisdiction of the case but held that it would exercise the power and authority of the judiciary at any time to achieve the goal of an adequate and substantially equal education for all Arkansas students.


OUTCOME: The court accepted the Masters' report and released jurisdiction of the case.

Perroni v. State


03-878


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


358 Ark. 17; 186 S.W.3d 206; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 393



June 17, 2004, Opinion delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Companion case at Fox v. Perroni, 358 Ark. 251, 188 S.W.3d 881, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 424 (Ark., June 24, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Perroni v. Arkansas, 543 U.S. 1150, 125 S. Ct. 1317, 161 L. Ed. 2d 112, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 1514 (U.S., Feb. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; No. CR00-2498, Timothy Davis Fox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of an order from the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Sixth Division (Arkansas), which found him in criminal contempt. The court imposed fines and sanctions.


OVERVIEW: The attorney agreed to represent a client in a tax fraud case. The attorney later sought a continuance of the trial on the ground that he had another trial scheduled on the same date. Instead of appearing at the hearing on the continuance motion, the attorney sent an associate. The trial judge denied the motion. The trial judge denied the attorney's motion to withdraw as counsel. On the day of trial, the client appeared in court without counsel. The trial judge found the attorney in criminal contempt for willfully disobeying the scheduling order by not appearing with the client at trial. On appeal, the court found that the attorney failed to demonstrate bias on the part of the trial judge. The court further found that the attorney had numerous opportunities to address the scheduling conflict, but chose not to do so. The attorney waited until the last minute to address the situation. The trial judge was justified in finding the attorney in contempt. The court found no merit to the attorney's contention that the trial court failed to accord him his constitutional protections. He was not entitled to a jury trial, and the trial court did not err in denying his request for one.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

317 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Weiss v. Chavers


03-805


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 607; 184 S.W.3d 437; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 363



June 3, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; No. E-94-6630, Vann Smith, Judge.  [***1]  .
Fisher v. Chavers, 351 Ark. 318, 92 S.W.3d 30, 2002 Ark. LEXIS 630 (Ark., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an illegal-exaction action, appellant state finance department director challenged a judgment of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which granted partial summary judgment for appellee taxpayers holding that they had involuntarily paid taxes and that Ark. Code Ann. § 26-51-301 (Supp. 1993) was unconstitutional, in that it violated the Equal Protection Clause and the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, who lived in Louisiana and paid taxes in Arkansas, filed an illegal-exaction suit seeking a refund of taxes and asserting that Ark. Code Ann. § 26-51-301 (Supp. 1993) was unconstitutional in that it permitted individuals who were full-time Arkansas residents to use a reduced tax table in calculating income taxes. The trial court found that § 26-51-301 was unconstitutional and that the taxpayers were entitled to a refund, as they had paid the taxes involuntarily. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in finding that the taxpayers' payments had been coerced and in failing to apply the voluntary-payment rule. The court noted that, under the rule, taxes paid voluntarily could not be recovered in an illegal-exaction suit and that taxes paid before the suit began were considered voluntary unless coerced. The court concluded that the taxpayers' payments were not coerced, because there was no evidence of the director's actual or threatened exercise of power in an attempt to collect the taxes, and the taxpayers had other reasonable means of relief. The court declined to address the constitutionality of § 26-51-301 (Supp. 1993), as it had been repealed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment that held the taxpayers were entitled to a refund of contested taxes paid, because the trial court erred in finding that the payments had been coerced. The court also reversed the trial court judgment that directed the taxpayers' attorney fees be paid from a common fund because there was to be no recovery, thus there was no common fund.

 

318 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Gwin v. Daniels


03-997


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 623; 184 S.W.3d 28; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 366



June 3, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Little River Circuit Court; No. DR03-50, Ted C. Capeheart, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Little River County Circuit Court, Arkansas, granted visitation rights to appellees, the great-grandparents of appellant mother's daughter. The mother appealed, asserting that the trial court's award violated her liberty interest under the due process clause and that the Arkansas Great-Grandparents Visitation Act, 2003 Ark. Acts 652, was unconstitutional. The mother also asserted there was a lack of competent evidence to support the award.


OVERVIEW: With respect to the Arkansas Great-Grandparents Visitation Act, 2003 Ark. Acts 652, the relevant provision at issue was Ark. Code Ann. § 9-13-103 (Supp. 2003). However, the mother neither presented the trial court with the issue of the constitutionality of the statute, nor did she obtain a ruling on the issue. Therefore, the Arkansas Supreme Court declined to review the constitutionality of the grandparents visitation law. Secondly, the mother argued that, because no expert testimony was provided on the issue of harm to her daughter caused by denial of visitation, there was a lack of competent evidence. However, the mother cited no authority on that issue; therefore, this supreme court would not consider it on appeal. Finally, the mother argued that the trial court's decision on visitation was in error, because the great-grandparents failed to meet the burden of proof of showing by a preponderance of the evidence that loss of the relationship would harm the child. However, the cases the mother cited purportedly in support of the latter argument were not on point and were not convincing authority. Thus, the supreme court would not consider that issue on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

319 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Green v. City of Jacksonville


03-563


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 517; 182 S.W.3d 124; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 346



May 27, 2004, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 13, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM PULASKI CIRCUIT COURT, NO. IJ 2001-2650, HON. ALICE SPRINKLE GRAY, JUDGE.
Green v. City of Jacksonville, 82 Ark. App. 39, 110 S.W.3d 323, 2003 Ark. App. LEXIS 344 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Court of Appeals reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee City of Jacksonville's petition for review of an appellate court (Arkansas) decision was granted. The appellate court decision reversed a circuit court order granting summary judgment in favor of the City and against appellants, a developer and his development company, in appellants' lawsuit seeking a declaration that an action by the City Council regarding a sidewalk ordinance was void.


OVERVIEW: The City's planning commission approved a preliminary plat for a subdivision development, and appellants commenced construction. The City then enacted a sidewalk ordinance, requiring sidewalks in all subdivisions. Appellants' development did not include sidewalks. The planning commission stipulated that it would not require appellants to include sidewalks as they were not practicable. The City Council disagreed with the stipulation and approved the final plat subject to appellants' constructing sidewalks. More than three months elapsed before appellants filed their declaratory judgment action against the City. Both sides filed motions for summary judgment. Appellants argued that the City Council acted ultra vires. The City argued that appellants' appeal was untimely under Ark. Code Ann. § 14-56-425. The circuit court agreed, as did the Arkansas Supreme Court. Prior case law precedent established that appellants were required to appeal the City Council's action within 30 days of the conditional plat approval. Having failed to do so, the circuit court properly granted summary judgment for lack of subject-matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals' decision was reversed.

 

320 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Hathcock v. State


CR 03-1089


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 563; 182 S.W.3d 152; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 350



May 27, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court, No. CR2001-2388, Willard Proctor, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Fifth Division, (Arkansas) of incest. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by failing to admit evidence of the victim's prior sexual conduct. The supreme court disagreed. The trial court's ruling did not impede the defense; it merely prevented questioning the victim with regard to her admission that she had sex with another person subsequent to the crime by defendant. The State contended that it was not necessary for defendant to expose the victim's subsequent sexual history in order to demonstrate her lack of credibility with regard to the claims she had made against defendant. The trial court excluded evidence of the prior sexual conduct, but it allowed defendant to argue that the victim was fabricating the allegations because she thought that defendant was too strict with her. Given the obvious potential that the evidence could be used to inflame the jury, the trial court conducted the appropriate balancing test and concluded that the prejudicial nature of the evidence outweighed its probative value.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

321 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Barclay v. Waters


03-369


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 386; 182 S.W.3d 91; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 324



May 20, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court, NO. OT 98-2100, Alice Sprinkle Gray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed on direct appeal; dismissed on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxpayers filed a class action against appellant, the state department of finance and administration director, a city judge, and cities, challenging a use tax imposed by 1987 Ark. Acts 31. The Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) denied appellants' motion to dismiss the suit, finding that a prior judgment that the tax was valid had been rendered null and void by a subsequently decided case. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: In a prior case, taxpayers successfully challenged a compensating use tax imposed by the county based on voter approval of a sales tax. The state legislature later enacted 1987 Ark. Acts 31, which imposed a use tax at the same rate. Taxpayers then unsuccessfully challenged 1987 Ark. Acts 31. The taxpayers filed the instant suit challenging the tax again based on a subsequently decided case involving a sales tax. On appeal, the court held that the trial court should have granted appellants' motion to dismiss the instant challenge. The court held that the recently decided case addressed only ballot title issues and, therefore, had no effect on the previous challenge to 1987 Ark. Acts 31, which was not decided based on ballot title issues. Therefore, the prior decision finding 1987 Ark. Acts 31 valid was res judicata. None of the constitutional arguments addressed in the prior case were successful on appeal; hence, they could not be readjudicated. The same claims were raised in the instant action. Also, the prior suit was also brought by taxpayers, and its judgment bound all taxpayers. The fact that the collection period for the tax was different in the two suits was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and dismissed appellees' cross-appeal.

 

322 of 594 DOCUMENTS


JurisDictionUSA, Inc. v. Loislaw.com, Inc.


03-1154


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 403; 183 S.W.3d 560; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 329



May 20, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Crawford Circuit Court, NO. CIV-2002-115, Michael Medlock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant software user filed a notice of removal of a suit brought by appellee software designer. On September 30, 2002, the designer filed a motion for default judgment pursuant to Ark. R. Civ. P. 55(f). On October 4, 2002, the user filed a response to the motion for default judgment. The Crawford County Circuit Court (Arkansas) entered a default judgment following the order of remand from the federal court. The user appealed.


OVERVIEW: The user contended that the trial court abused its discretion in granting the default judgment, because, under the amended version of Ark. R. Civ. P. 55(f), the designer was not entitled to entry of default judgment when an answer had been filed in federal court and the amended version of rule 55(f) should have been applied retroactively. The issue was whether the amended version of rule 55(f) should have been applied retroactively. In the instant case, the designer's right to request a default judgment was not enlarged or extinguished by the amendment to rule 55(f). The amendment to the rule merely outlined a new procedure that had to be followed before a party could obtain a default judgment after a case had been removed to federal court and then remanded back to the circuit court. Under either version of the rule, a plaintiff could request a default judgment. The change to the rule merely modified the standard by which default could be determined. Thus, the Supreme Court of Arkansas held that rule 55(f) was procedural and remedial and amended rule 55(f) should have been applied retroactively, because the user filed its answer in federal court on April 5, 2002.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Cambiano v. Ark. State Bd. of Law Exam'rs


03-1341


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 336; 167 S.W.3d 649; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 283



May 6, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Cambiano v. Ligon, 345 Ark. 124, 44 S.W.3d 719, 2001 Ark. LEXIS 341 (Ark., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former attorney was disbarred in 2000. The attorney filed an original action against appellee Arkansas State Board of Law Examiners, challenging the Board's decision denying his application to be readmitted to the bar under Ark. Sup. Ct. Prof. Conduct P. § 24.


OVERVIEW: The attorney's disbarment in 2000 was based on conduct from 1992 for which he had pleaded guilty to a felony charge relating to causing a bank to file a false currency-transaction report. The disbarment had been affirmed on appeal. In 2003, the attorney applied for readmission to the bar. In the instant action, the attorney challenged the Board's denial of that application without a hearing. The court affirmed. The court rejected the attorney's claim that applying Ark. Sup. Ct. Prof. Conduct P. § 24 to him violated his due process rights. The court noted that admission to the bar was a privilege, not a right. Also, the court held that the five-year waiting period was not an enlargement of a punishment in violation of Ark. Const. art. 2, § 8 and U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10, as disbarment proceedings were neither criminal nor civil, the waiting period did not impose an affirmative disability, the attorney cited no authority indicating that a waiting period was a punishment, the waiting period was merely a procedural operation, and the five-year waiting period was not excessive. The court also found no error in failing to credit the attorney for the pre-disbarment period of suspension.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Board.
