Whitlow v. State


CR 03-830


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 290; 166 S.W.3d 45; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 298



May 6, 2004, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 13, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM GREENE CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR 02-44, HON. DAVID N. LASER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his motion to accept a guilty plea was denied, the Greene County Circuit Court (Arkansas) entered judgment on a jury verdict convicting him of two counts of delivery of methamphetamine. After his similar motion on sentencing was likewise denied, defendant was sentenced to 15 years. Defendant appealed from the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court's refusal to accept his guilty plea violated due process rights as well as separation of powers provisions in the U.S. Constitution and at Ark. Const. art. 4, §§ 1 and 2, the separation of powers provisions. On appeal the court found no error. The court noted that defendant had no constitutional right to unilaterally waive a jury trial. Moreover, Ark. R. Crim. P. 31.1 and Ark. Code Ann. § 16-89-108(a) (1987) required the approval of the prosecutor before a trial court could accept defendant's request to plead guilty and waive a jury trial. The court also rejected defendant's claim that Ark. R. Crim. P. 31.1 violated defendant's due process rights because it curtailed his liberty interest and exposed him to a higher sentence. The sentencing grid codified at Ark. Code Ann. §§ 16-90-801 to -804 did not create a liberty interest in protecting defendant from exposure to the higher ranges of sentences. Rather, the purpose of the sentencing scheme was to assist judges who were required to do the sentencing due to guilty pleas or the inability of juries to agree on a sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

325 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Ark. Tobacco Control Bd. v. Sitton


03-414


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 357; 166 S.W.3d 550; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 284; 2004-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P74,425



May 6, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; No. CV02-7042, Christopher Charles Piazza, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Arkansas Tobacco Control Board (ATCB) appealed a decision of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), finding that, in the absence of the ATCB adopting regulations defining the statutory terms "trade discounts" and "rebate," the Unfair Cigarette Sales Act's (UCSA), Ark. Code Ann. § 4-75-701 et seq., prohibition against rebates was void for vagueness as applied to appellee retailer.


OVERVIEW: At issue on appeal was the meaning of the terms "trade discount" and "rebate." As the circuit court noted, neither term was defined in the statute. The ATCB chose to define "rebate" by regulation, but did not define "trade discount." Wholesalers and retailers of tobacco, who were presumably professionals in their fields, professed confusion arising from the defined term and the undefined terms. The Supreme Court of Arkansas agreed that the terms "trade discount" and "rebate" were unclear under the existing UCSA and ATCB regulations as to what an allowed "trade discount" was, as opposed to a prohibited "rebate." The supreme court held that the law was unconstitutionally vague under due process standards, because it did not give a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice of what was prohibited, that was, of whether payments to the retailer were permitted "trade discounts" or prohibited "rebates." The changes in the law in 2003 by the general assembly appeared to have been intended to cure some of the confusion giving rise to the instant appeal. The circuit court did not err in its finding.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Hunt v. Perry


03-1014


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 224; 162 S.W.3d 891; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 278



April 29, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Yell Circuit Court; David H. McCormick, Judge. NO. E-2000-88.
Hunt v. Perry, 355 Ark. 303, 138 S.W.3d 656, 2003 Ark. LEXIS 673 (Ark., Dec. 11, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Yell County Circuit Court (Arkansas) found appellant father in contempt of court for denying appellee grandmother's visitation rights to her grandchildren as was previously ordered by the trial court. The trial court also denied the father's motion to terminate the grandmother's visitation. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the father asserted that the underlying visitation order was unconstitutional and, thus invalid, it was certainly valid at the time it was issued and within the subject-matter jurisdiction of the trial court. Because the father refused to comply with the order that was clearly within the trial court's jurisdiction and because the supreme court would not look behind the order for contempt purposes, the supreme court held that the father had not demonstrated that the trial court's finding of contempt against him was in error. The father alleged that he refused to comply with the trial court's visitation order because his son was being sexually abused by the grandmother. However, the trial court found that the allegations of sexual abuse were unsubstantiated. Thus, the trial court did not err in denying the father's petition to terminate the grandmother's visitation with the grandchildren and in finding him in contempt of the visitation order. Finally, the investigator's supervisor was properly allowed to testify regarding a police report that was made following the father's call to the sexual abuse hotline because her testimony did not run afoul of the hearsay rule.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Woolbright v. State


CR 03-170


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


357 Ark. 63; 160 S.W.3d 315; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 231; 41 A.L.R.6th 643



April 22, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sebastian Circuit Court; J. Michael Fitzhugh, Judge. NO. CR-2002-265 A/B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a case in the Sebastian County Circuit Court (Arkansas) where two separate juries were impaneled, one jury found the first defendant guilty of first-degree murder and sentenced her to a term of life imprisonment; whereas, the other jury found the second defendant guilty of second-degree murder and sentenced him to 40 years' imprisonment. Both defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The first defendant gave two recorded statements in which she admitted to being at the crime scene. In one of those statements, she told the police that she intended to kill the victim but was unable to muster the strength. She also acknowledged handing the murder weapon to the second defendant after he stated that he would kill the victim. Viewed in the light most favorable to the State, the first defendant confessed to either murdering or aiding in the murder of the victim. In addition, the evidence reflected that the victim died as a result of a homicide. Thus, there was sufficient evidence to support the verdict finding the first defendant guilty of first-degree murder. The supreme court condemned the practice of using dual juries and prohibited the use of dual juries in the future; however, because the supreme court could find no prejudice in defendants' case, it declined to reverse defendants' convictions on that point. But, the appellate court found that none of the officers informed the second defendant that he had the right to refuse consent to their entry and subsequent search of his home. Thus, all the evidence that flowed from that search should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the first defendant's conviction and sentence, but reversed and remanded the second defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

328 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Medlin v. Weiss


03-1043


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 588; 158 S.W.3d 140; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 200



April 8, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Polk Circuit Court. Jerry Wayne Looney, Judge. NO. DR-99-11.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother filed a petition in the Polk County Circuit Court, Arkansas, asking for child support from appellee father. The father, and his wife as intervenor, counterclaimed asking that their daughters, the mother and father's child's half-sisters, be allowed to exercise visitation with her. The trial court granted the father relief. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had denied the mother's constitutional challenge and allowed half-sibling visitation concurrent with the father's parental visitation rights with the parties' child. The trial court found that the mother offered no convincing testimony for objecting to such visitation. The mother argued that Ark. Code Ann. § 9-13-102 (Supp. 2002), the sibling visitation statute, was unconstitutional as written and as so applied. The appellate court noted that the liberty right of a parent to raise a child applied to both parents, and neither the state nor the absent parent had the right to intrude upon the decisions a fit parent made while the child in his or her custody, regarding what was in that child's best interest or with whom she could associate. The appellate court held that the father, during those visitation periods, had the right to decide what was in the child's best interest, including visitation between and among his daughters, in his own home, without being physically present. However, the appellate court concluded that the trial court clouded the issue of parental visitation rights by ordering concurrent sibling visitation rights under Ark. Code Ann. § 9-13-102.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court delineating parental visitation rights was affirmed; however, the trial court clouded the issue of parental visitation rights by ordering concurrent sibling visitation rights, which warranted a remand to amend its order.

Sims v. State


CR 03-63


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 507; 157 S.W.3d 530; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 181



April 1, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM CIRCUIT COURT OF MISSISSIPPI, ARKANSAS, NO. CR 2001-240; HONORABLE JOHN FOGLEMAN, CIRCUIT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Mississippi County, Arkansas, denying his motion to suppress evidence seized during a traffic stop.


OVERVIEW: At the suppression hearing, the officer testified when he first saw defendant's vehicle, he believed it was obstructing traffic in the left lane. He observed that the left taillight and brake light of the car was not functioning, which was a violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 27-36-216(a) and (b) (Repl. 2004). The officer wrote up a warning, citing defendant for having a defective brake light. The officer also ran a criminal history check on both defendant and the passenger, which revealed that both men had prior drug arrests. The officer then brought a drug dog to the car. The officer's subsequent search of the car turned up 13 grams of cocaine. The Supreme Court of Arkansas held that defendant was entitled to have the evidence suppressed. The continued detention of defendant after the legitimate purpose of the traffic stop ended was a violation of Ark. R. Crim. P. 3.1.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

330 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


CR 02-1362


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 534; 157 S.W.3d 151; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 183



April 1, 2004, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Johnson v. Arkansas, 543 U.S. 932, 125 S. Ct. 326, 160 L. Ed. 2d 235, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 6810 (2004)
Appeal after remand at Johnson v. State, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 313 (Ark., May 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM SEVIER CIRCUIT COURT. NO. CR-93-54. HON. TED C. CAPEHEART, JUDGE.
Johnson v. State, 342 Ark. 186, 27 S.W.3d 405, 2000 Ark. LEXIS 454 (Ark., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death, and the court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The inmate subsequently sought postconviction DNA testing under Act 1780, Ark. Code Ann. § 16-112-201-207 (Supp. 2003) and asserted claims of ineffective assistance of counsel under Ark. R. Crim. P. 37. The Sevier County Circuit Court, Arkansas, denied those petitions, as well as a motion to supplement. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the denial of DNA testing as to "Caucasian" hairs, reasoning that they were not tested at trial even though testing was available. Also, it was stipulated that the inmate, an African-American, was not the donor; thus, the jury knew there were hairs that belonged to someone else, and it still convicted him. The hairs thus were not materially relevant under Ark. Code Ann. § 16-112-202(c)(1)(B). Testing was also properly denied as to a cigarette butt, because prior retesting had decreased the probability of the saliva being from a different donor from 1 in 250 to 1 in 28 million. The court reversed the denial, however, as to retesting of "Negroid" hairs. The probability that they belonged to another African-American was only 1 in 250, a result that could have included thousands of people. The inmate made 13 other ineffective assistance of counsel claims, none of which met the Strickland test. Finally, the inmate was not entitled to supplement his petition to include an argument that victim impact procedure was inadequate in not requiring the jury to find proof beyond a reasonable doubt. Victim-impact statements were simply evidence, not an element in a statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of the inmate's petition to retest the Negroid hairs and remanded for the circuit court to order DNA retesting. The court affirmed the remainder of the decision.

State v. Brown


CR 03-914


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 460; 156 S.W.3d 722; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 168



March 25, 2004, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As corrected, April 22, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM POPE CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR 2002-483, HON. JOHN S. PATTERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Arkansas sought review of an order from the Pope County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which granted defendants' motions to suppress evidence seized during a warrantless search of their residence.


OVERVIEW: Three drug task force agents approached defendants' residence. They did so because of information received from two anonymous sources that defendants were involved in drug activity and that a child inside the residence had become ill due to drug manufacturing. The agents presented one defendant with a consent-to-search form to sign. As a result of the search, defendants were charged with manufacture of methamphetamine and marijuana and possession of methamphetamine with intent to deliver. The trial court granted defendants' two separate motions to suppress the evidence seized during the search. On appeal, the court held that the failure of the task force agents to advise the defendant who answered the door that she had the right to refuse consent to the search violated both defendants' rights against warrantless intrusions into the home, as guaranteed by Ark. Const. art. II, § 15. The court explained that strong public policy in Arkansas in favor of privacy in one's home warranted its opinion. Accordingly, the court upheld the suppression of all evidence seized in the case that flowed from the unconstitutional search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Omni Holding & Dev. Corp. v. 3D.S.A., Inc.


03-841


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 440; 156 S.W.3d 228; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 178



March 25, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Crittenden Circuit Court, NO. CV 2003-50, Charles David Burnett, Judge..



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant development corporation sought review of the decision of the Crittenden County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which found in favor of appellee corporation and entered an order of civil contempt against the development corporation for refusing to delivery aviation property. The circuit court also found appellant managing officer in criminal contempt.


OVERVIEW: The development corporation appealed from an order finding it to have been in civil contempt for refusing to deliver to the corporation all of the aviation property that it was ordered to deliver by the circuit court. The circuit court further found that the development corporation's managing officer was in criminal contempt for personally directing the development corporation's employees to switch data plates on several planes and for intentionally refusing to deliver certain items in the order of delivery in an assembled manner. On appeal the supreme court modified the judgment, stating that it disagreed with the circuit court that the purging of the managing officer's contempt could rest on the development corporation's payment of $ 75,000 to the corporation. The key to the jail in civil contempt rested in the hands of the contemnor and not a third party. The supreme court affirmed the judgment as modified, stating that because the development corporation and its managing officer failed to turn over to the sheriff assembled planes and related equipment as specified in the order of delivery, they were in contempt of that order.


OUTCOME: The supreme court modified the contempt order to eliminate the development corporation's payment as a condition for the managing officer's release from jail. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

 

333 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Durham v. Marberry


03-874


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 481; 156 S.W.3d 242; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 179



March 25, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sharp Circuit Court. NO. CV-2002-24. Harold S. Erwin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sharp County Circuit Court, Arkansas, granted judgment in favor of appellees, individual and mobile home company, in appellant estate administrators' suit for damages incurred when a mobile home transport vehicle collided with the vehicle driven by the decedent. The administrators appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted partial summary judgment to appellees with regard to claimed "loss of life" damages, finding that at least some period of life between injury and death was a condition for recovery of loss-of-life damages by a decedent's estate. The administrators argued that no period of life between injury and death was required to recovery loss-of-life damages. The appellate court determined that, contrary to appellees' assertion, although damages for "loss of life" and "loss of enjoyment of life" were both hedonic, "loss of life" damages were not the equivalent of those for "loss of enjoyment of life." The legislature allowed for the recovery of loss-of-life damages in the Arkansas survival statute, Ark. Code Ann. § 16-62-101, which made no distinction between "personal injury" and "death" when it spoke of the term "injury." When a person was killed instantaneously, as was the decedent, her injury was her death, which was compensated by loss-of-life damages. While the determination of damages was within the purview of the jury, the issue was not ripe for consideration by the appellate court. Double recovery for damages was also not an issue ripe for review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

334 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Bennett v. Lonoke Bancshares, Inc.


03-258


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 371; 155 S.W.3d 15; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 158



March 11, 2004, Opinion Delievered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Lonoke Circuit Court, NO. CIV2002-46, Lance Hanshaw, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant founders challenged a decision from the Lonoke County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which granted a motion for summary judgment filed by appellee members in an action involving a dispute over cumulative voting in a bank holding company.


OVERVIEW: The bank holding company was formed under the Arkansas Business Corporation Act of 1987, Ark. Code Ann. § 4-27-101 et seq. The founders and the members had a dispute over whether they were required to use cumulative voting for electing directors. As a result, the founders filed a complaint seeking to invalidate the action taken by the members. When the trial court granted the members' motion for summary judgment, the founders sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the trial court did not err by denying a motion for a continuance and a stay under Ark. R. Civ. P. 56(f). There was no indication that the issues before the trial court necessitated any further inquiry into the surrounding facts and circumstances. Further, cumulative voting was not required because it was not mandated by the articles of incorporation. In addition, a bank holding company was not included within Ark. Code Ann. § 23-48-320, which governed cumulative voting. Finally, the court determined that this interpretation of § 23-48-320 was not unconstitutional. Ark. Const. art. 12, § 6 allowed the Arkansas General Assembly to amend, alter, or repeal any law regarding corporations.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

335 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Scamardo v. Jaggers


03-765


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 236; 149 S.W.3d 311; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 125



February 26, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF SEBASTIAN COUNTY, ARKANSAS, NO. CV 2002-1340 I; HONORABLE NORMAN WILKINSON, CIRCUIT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient filed a medical malpractice suit against appellee doctor and a medical center. The complaint also named appellee, the center's insurer. The patient stated a belief that the center might claim immunity from suit for tort under the charitable immunity doctrine. The Circuit Court of Sebastian County (Arkansas) dismissed the insurer, basing its dismissal on the Clayborn decision. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient asked the Supreme Court of Arkansas to overrule Clayborn. Declining to overrule Clayborn, the court stated that it was a 2002 case involving both Ark. Code Ann. § 23-79-210, the direct action statute, and the doctrine of charitable immunity. The supreme court did not agree with the patient's suggestion that, if Clayborn was allowed to stand, unjust results would follow. The patient argued that, if a hospital was "immune from liability," its carrier would not be obligated to pay any damages that may accrue. However, the supreme court held that such an argument appeared to have been premised on a misunderstanding of what the supreme court meant when it used the term "immune from liability." The phrase did not mean that a nonprofit organization could not be found liable; rather, it meant that the prevailing party in a lawsuit against a nonprofit could not execute on the property or assets of the nonprofit in order to satisfy any judgment. However, as was true in the instant case, the losing party's insurer could be bound to pay up to its policy limits any judgment entered against the nonprofit. The supreme court likewise saw no need to limit Clayborn's holding.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

336 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Isom v. State


CR 02-213


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 156; 148 S.W.3d 257; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 111



February 19, 2004, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Isom v. Arkansas, 543 U.S. 865, 125 S. Ct. 204, 160 L. Ed. 2d 110, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 6516 (2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Isom v. State, 2010 Ark. 496, 372 S.W.3d 809, 2010 Ark. LEXIS 599 (Ark., 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at Isom v. State, 2010 Ark. 495, 370 S.W.3d 491, 2010 Ark. LEXIS 600 (Ark., 2010)
Review pending at Isom v. State, 2011 Ark. 149, 2011 Ark. LEXIS 129 (Ark., 2011)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Petition granted by Isom v. State, 2015 Ark. 225, 2015 Ark. LEXIS 357 (Ark., 2015)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Petition denied by Isom v. State, 2015 Ark. 219, 2015 Ark. LEXIS 359 (Ark., 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DREW CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR 2001-52-2, HON. SAMUEL B. POPE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Drew County Circuit Court (Arkansas) of capital murder, residential burglary, attempted capital murder, rape, and aggravated robbery. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his capital murder conviction. The supreme court disagreed. The victim identified defendant as her attacker in the attempted murder and rapes and as the person who was physically abusing the other victim. She further testified that defendant demanded and received money and her ring, using the threat of the broken scissors. Her testimony was sufficient to support a burglary conviction, in that she stated that he pushed his way into the home and proceeded to commit rape and aggravated robbery. And, finally, her in-court identification of defendant, as well as the body hair found in her vagina connecting him to the rape, placed him at the scene where the victim was murdered. While the victim did not specifically see defendant stab the other victim with scissors or beat him, she saw defendant with the scissors standing on the victim's head. She also heard his threats. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant caused the death of the victim in the course of committing several felonies under circumstances manifesting extreme indifference to the value of human life.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Weiss v. McFadden


03-1215


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 123; 148 S.W.3d 248; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 105



February 19, 2004, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Weiss v. McFadden, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 783 (Ark., Dec. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI CIRCUIT COURT, NO. OT99-3939, HON. COLLINS KILGORE, JUDGE.
Weiss v. McFadden, 353 Ark. 868, 120 S.W.3d 545, 2003 Ark. LEXIS 378 (Ark., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An illegal-exaction lawsuit was filed by appellees, a group of taxpayer retirees, against appellant, the Arkansas Department of Finance and Administration (department). This second appeal concerned the refund mechanism fashioned by the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) upon remand. Both the taxpayers and the department proposed refund mechanisms. The trial court opted for the taxpayers' refund. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court's first decision held that (1) after-tax contributions to retirement plans were property not subject to income taxes; and (2) income tax levied against after-tax contributions pursuant to Ark. Code Ann. § 26-51-307 was an ad valorem tax on property in violation of Ark. Const. Amend. 47, and an illegal exaction under Ark. Const. Art. 16, § 13. On appeal, the department asserted the trial court erred in refusing to (1) apply the voluntary-payment rule to any illegally-exacted taxes paid before the 1999 filing of the lawsuit, and (2) apply I.R.C. § 72, which prorated recovery of after-tax contributions on federal tax returns. On cross-appeal, the taxpayers argued the trial court erred in finding that 1991 Ark. Acts 380 did not violate the intergovernmental tax immunity doctrine. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling that 1991 Ark. Acts 380 did not violate the intergovernmental tax immunity doctrine; it affirmed the trial court's refusal to apply I.R.C. § 72 to after-tax contributions in employment-related retirement plans; and it reversed the trial court's ruling that the voluntary-payment rule did not apply to taxes paid on after-tax contributions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part. The judgment that the voluntary-payment rule did not apply to taxes paid on after-tax contributions was reversed and remanded with instructions to fashion a remedy consistent with this opinion.

Greene v. State


CR 02-736


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


356 Ark. 59; 146 S.W.3d 871; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 88



February 12, 2004, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE JOHNSON CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR-91-44, HON. JOHN S. PATTERSON, JUDGE.
Greene v. State, 343 Ark. 526, 37 S.W.3d 579, 2001 Ark. LEXIS 40 (Ark., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of an order of the Johnson County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which denied his petition for postconviction relief. The court had previously affirmed defendant's murder conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner went to the victim's home, tortured him, and ultimately shot him. The postconviction court dismissed the petition without an evidentiary hearing. The court held that the order complied with the mandates of Ark. R. Crim. P. 37. The trial court did not need to hold a hearing, even though it was a death penalty case, because it could be conclusively shown on the record that the allegations had no merit. The court held that the trial court did not clearly err in finding that counsel's decision to use transcripts of prior testimony as mitigating evidence at resentencing was a matter of trial strategy. Counsel could have considered the potential that the State would more vigorously cross-examine the mitigation witnesses, and counsel did attempt to secure live testimony. Given the evidence of guilt, the prisoner could not show that he was prejudiced by counsel's decision not to object to the prosecutor's closing comments, asking the jury to send a message. Although counsel failed to make a First Amendment objection to admission of a T-shirt, the First Amendment did not prohibit the evidentiary use of speech to establish the elements of a crime or to prove motive or intent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling.

Otis v. State


CR 03-334


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


355 Ark. 590; 142 S.W.3d 615; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 27



January 22, 2004, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Otis v. State, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 723 (Ark., Nov. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE ARKANSAS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NORTHERN DISTRICT NO. CR01-137, HON. F. RUSSELL ROGERS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Arkansas County Circuit Court, Northern District (Arkansas), which denied his motion to transfer to juvenile court after he was charged with capital murder. The court also denied his motion to declare Ark. Code Ann. § 9-27-318 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with the offense of capital murder. At the time of the murder, appellant was 14 years old. Appellant filed a motion to have his case transferred to the juvenile court. In addition, appellant filed a pretrial motion in which he argued that Ark. Code Ann. § 9-27-318 was unconstitutional. The trial court entered an order denying appellant's motion to declare § 9-27-318 unconstitutional. The trial court also denied appellant's motion to transfer to juvenile court. On appeal, the court could not say, in light of the evidence presented, that the trial court's denial of the motion to transfer appellant to the juvenile court was clearly erroneous. There was clear and convincing evidence to support the trial court's finding that appellant should be tried as an adult. The offense in question was of a serious and violent nature. The court further found that appellant failed to demonstrate that § 9-27-318 was arbitrary or irrational. Finally, the court found that appellant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the sentencing authorized by § 9-27-318, because there had been no formal adjudication of guilt and he had not been sentenced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Feland v. State


CR 03-706


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


355 Ark. 573; 142 S.W.3d 631; 2004 Ark. LEXIS 29



January 22, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF WASHINGTON COUNTY, ARKANSAS, NO. CR-02-1646-1, HONORABLE WILLIAM A. STOREY, CIRCUIT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Washington County (Arkansas) convicted defendant of driving while intoxicated and violating a city noise ordinance, after denying his motion to suppress. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving his truck in the early morning hours along a city street. A city police officer observed that the vehicle's stereo was plainly audible at a distance of approximately 75 feet; the officer's car windows were rolled up, and defendant's were down. Because the city's noise ordinance prohibited vehicular stereos being plainly audible at a distance of more than 30 feet, the officer initiated a traffic stop. Upon approaching the vehicle, he smelled a very strong odor of alcoholic beverages. He conducted several field sobriety tests, and determined that defendant was intoxicated. On appeal, defendant argued the trial court should have granted his motion to suppress on the grounds that the noise ordinance was unconstitutional, and the police officer who pulled him over should have known of the ordinance's unconstitutionality. The officer had more than a reasonable suspicion to believe that defendant had just committed a violation of the noise ordinance, and because ordinances are presumed to be constitutional, he reasonably relied on the validity of the noise ordinance to stop defendant. The trial court did not err in denying the motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Finagin v. Ark. Dev. Fin. Auth.


02-1197


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


355 Ark. 440; 139 S.W.3d 797; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 684



December 18, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM LAFAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CIV-99-38-2 HON. JAMES HUDSON, JUDGE.
Finagin v. Ark. Dev. Fin. Auth., 353 Ark. 356, 107 S.W.3d 174, 2003 Ark. LEXIS 291 (Ark., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant stockholders challenged a judgment from the Lafayette County Circuit Court (Arkansas) which, following a bench trial, entered a judgment for appellee Arkansas Development Finance Authority (ADFA) in its action to enforce payment under the stockholders' guaranty agreements with the ADFA.


OVERVIEW: The ADFA was established to issue revenue bonds for the development of business and industry in the state. A company received revenue bonds from the ADFA to establish a plant. The funds were secured by personal guaranties from each individual stockholder. When the company defaulted, the ADFA made demand on the stockholders under the personal guaranty agreements. The stockholders did not make payments and suit was brought to enforce the guaranties. Following a bench trial, judgment was entered for the ADFA The stockholders appealed, arguing the legislature did not authorize the ADFA to execute personal guaranties and they should have been released when other obligors were released. The court found that because each stockholder individually signed a guaranty for a stated amount, and because each was individually liable on the separate guaranties, a release of one guarantor did not release all of them. Also, while personal guaranties were not specifically authorized, Ark. Code Ann. § 15-5-413 gave the ADFA authority to make reasonable lending requirements, including personal guaranties. Other issues were not raised below, so the court would not address them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment enforcing the guaranty agreements against the stockholders.

Hunt v. Perry


03-420


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


355 Ark. 303; 138 S.W.3d 656; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 673



December 11, 2003, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Subsequent appeal at Hunt v. Perry, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 278 (Ark., Apr. 29, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hunt v. Perry, 158 L. Ed. 2d 984, 124 S. Ct. 2428, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 3873 (U.S., June 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE YELL CIRCUIT COURT, SOUTHERN DISTRICT; NO. E-00-88; HON. DAVID H. McCORMICK, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed the order of the Yell County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which denied his petition to terminate appellee maternal grandmother's visitation rights with his two children. He argued that the trial court erred in dismissing on summary judgment his challenge to the constitutionality of the Arkansas Grandparent Visitation Act (GPVA), Ark. Code Ann. § 9-13-103 (Repl. 2002), and by failing to find a change in circumstances.


OVERVIEW: The father and his wife (the grandmother's daughter) had two children. After the wife died and the father remarried, he denied the grandmother visitation; she sought visitation rights under Ark. Code Ann. § 9-13-103. The father's claim that the GPVA was unconstitutional was rejected, and the grandmother was granted visitation. The father did not appeal, but later filed this action to terminate visitation, alleging as changes in circumstances: (1) changes in constitutional law as to the GPVA; and (2) changes in his children's behavior since visitation was ordered. The appellate court held that the trial court properly granted the grandmother partial summary judgment on grounds that res judicata barred the father's challenge to the constitutionality of the GPVA, as the same parties and issue had been involved in the prior action. As to changes in the children's behavior, the trial court ruled that it was not possible to determine whether their behavioral problems stemmed from the visitation with the grandmother or the blending of the families of the father and his current wife, and, as this finding was supported by the evidence, it would not be disturbed on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Townsend v. State


CR 02-1130


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


355 Ark. 248; 134 S.W.3d 545; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 647



December 4, 2003, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Motion denied by Townsend v. State, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 110 (Ark., Feb. 17, 2005)
Motion granted by Townsend v. State, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 267 (Ark., May 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE WASHINGTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR-2000-1803, HON. WILLIAM STOREY, JUDGE.
Townsend v. State, 76 Ark. App. 371, 66 S.W.3d 666, 2002 Ark. App. LEXIS 12 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery, being a felon in possession, and a habitual offender; he was sentenced to 40 years' imprisonment. On remand, the State filed an amended information alleging habitual-offender status. At the conclusion of defendant's new trial, he was convicted of aggravated robbery and being a felon in possession; he received a life sentence for aggravated robbery based on his habitual-offender status. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review of defendant's criminal conviction, he argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash the amended felony information filed on remand for a new trial. The new information alleged him to be a habitual-offender. He contended that the new information was an attempt to punish him for exercising his fundamental right to appeal. The Supreme Court of Arkansas disagreed. By the time defendant obtained a new trial, he had been convicted of four counts of rape and one count of aggravated robbery in a separate case. The new convictions were used to amend the felony information. Because it was impossible to proceed on the enhanced-sentencing charge, in defendant's first trial, the State rebutted the presumption of vindictiveness. Accordingly, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to quash the amended felony information.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

344 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Summit Mall Co. v. Lemond


02-1337


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


355 Ark. 190; 132 S.W.3d 725; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 650



December 4, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI CIRCUIT COURT, NO. IJ 2001-2246, HON. MACKIE M. PIERCE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a company, a city, and a mayor and board of directors of the city, challenged a decision of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which ruled in favor of appellee landowners and entered a permanent injunction enjoining the city from issuing a building permit to the company or taking any other action with respect to a particular ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The board passed an ordinance that approved a planned unit development. The company planned to construct a mall on the property, but the landowners sought an injunction. They were successful, but the court reversed. By enacting the ordinance, the board approved the recommended action and amended a prior ordinance, but it rezoned the property and added new conditions to accommodate the rezoning. Thus, the board took legislative action delegated to it under Ark. Code Ann. § 14-56-402 (1998). Because the action was not administrative, the landowners were not required to proceed under Ark. Code Ann. § 14-56-425 and the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction. The court declined to dismiss the matter for lack of standing. The trial court erred in ruling against the company and city on their defense of laches because the landowners could have filed their action sooner. Had they done so, the company would not have bought the subject property. Because the ordinance was new legislation with future ramifications, it was a legislative matter subject to a referendum as provided by Ark. Const. amend. 7. However, whether a referendum election was to be approved was not before the court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

Landers v. Jameson


03-114


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


355 Ark. 163; 132 S.W.3d 741; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 649; 16 A.L.R.6th 851



December 4, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV 99-1411 HON. WILLARD PROCTOR, JUDGE.
Landers v. Jameson, 2002 Ark. App. LEXIS 199 (Ark. Ct. App., Apr. 3, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pawn shop challenged a decision of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which ruled in favor of appellee property owner in his action to recover property and found that Ark. Code Ann. §§ 18-27-202, 18-27-203 (1987) were constitutional. An award of attorney fees in the owner's favor was held in abeyance by the trial court, pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: The owner alleged that his jewelry was stolen and sold to the pawn shop. When the pawn shop refused to return the jewelry after the police department put a hold thereon, the owner filed this action. The trial court ruled in the owner's favor and rejected the pawn shop's claim that Ark. Code Ann. §§ 18-27-202, 18-27-203 (1987) were unconstitutional. The court reversed. The constitutionality of the statutes was not raised until after an appellate court first heard the matter on an earlier appeal. However, the law of the case doctrine was not an alternative reason to affirm the case. The court held that §§ 18-27-202, 18-27-203, as applied to the pawn shop, were unconstitutional. The interest acquired by the pawn shop in the goods constituted a sufficient property interest to warrant due process protection. The joint participation to recover the goods by the police department and the owner amounted to state action. The court concluded that the statutes were unconstitutional in mandating the pawn shop to return property to the owner based merely on his request and affidavit before a judicial determination of ownership had taken place and in assessing fees against the pawn shop.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

Johnson v. Encompass Ins. Co.


03-305


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


355 Ark. 1; 130 S.W.3d 553; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 620



November 20, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE ASHLEY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV01-183-1, HON. SAMUEL B. POPE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insureds challenged a decision of the Ashley County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee insurer and held that Ark. Code Ann. §§ 23-89-305(a), 23-89-306 (2000) were constitutional as applied to the facts.


OVERVIEW: The insureds filed a claim, but the insurer denied coverage and contended that they were no longer insured based on a notice of non-renewal that was mailed to the insureds prior to the accident. The insureds brought this action and alleged that the notice statutes, Ark. Code Ann. §§ 23-89-305(a), 23-89-306 (2000) were unconstitutional as applied to the facts. The trial court ruled in favor of the insurer and the court affirmed on appeal. Because the insureds failed to cite to legal authority on their alleged error concerning the finding that the statutes were constitutional as applied, the court did not consider the argument. Section 23-89-306 provided a measure of protection to an insured by requiring notice. Even if use of the United States Postal Service could have been considered state action, the statute's use of regular, non-certified mail was rationally related to a governmental purpose. The requirement of notification did not rise to the level of state action and no due process violation occurred when the statute was enacted. The insureds had no protected property right in any coverage beyond the lapse date. The doctrine of estoppel did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

347 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Tsann Kuen Enters. Co. v. Campbell


03-391


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


355 Ark. 110; 129 S.W.3d 822; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 621



November 20, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE BENTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CIV2002-1177-5, HON. XOLLIE MARIE BUFFER DUNCAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee land buyers filed a complaint in unlawful detainer against appellant land owner in the Benton County Circuit Court (Arkansas). The owner requested the trial court to find the notice procedures in Ark. Code Ann. § 26-37-101 et seq. (Repl. 1997) unconstitutional. The trial court found for the buyers and denied the owner's request. The trial court entered an order for immediate possession in favor of the buyers. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: After purchasing the subject property, the owner moved its corporate office from Illinois to California. The owner did not provide its new address to the county tax collector. The owner did not pay the taxes on the property for years. The Commissioner of State Lands mailed a notice of delinquent real estate taxes to the owner at its old Illinois address, but the notice was returned to the Commissioner, marked "unclaimed" and "forwarding order expired." Published notice was also made in newspapers. The buyers acquired title to the property by limited warranty deed. The owner conceded that the Commissioner strictly complied with Ark. Code Ann. § 26-37-301 (Repl. 1997); however, it argued that Ark. Code Ann. § 26-37-101 et seq. did not satisfy due process requirements of the United States Constitution and the Arkansas Constitution, in that it failed to provide sufficient notice to nonresident landowners prior to the property being sold at a tax forfeiture sale. On appeal, the court found that § 26-37-301 fulfilled constitutional due process requirements and provided sufficient notice to nonresident landowners prior to their property being sold.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Berry v. City of Fayetteville


CR 03-381


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


354 Ark. 470; 125 S.W.3d 171; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 551



October 16, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE WASHINGTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR02-1953-1, HON. WILLIAM A. STOREY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Washington County Circuit Court (Arkansas), in which appellant submitted a plea of guilty conditioned upon affirmance of the trial court's decision that appellee city had the authority to regulate appellant's racing activities and the trial court's decision that City of Fayetteville, Ark., Ordinance § 4366 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered the conditional plea pursuant to Ark. R. Crim. P. 24.3(b). Ark. R. Crim. P. 24.3(b) was limited to an adverse determination on a pretrial motion to suppress evidence. Neither of the issues upon which appellant sought a Supreme Court of Arkansas ruling involved a motion to suppress evidence. Therefore, his reliance upon Ark. R. Crim. P. 24.3(b) was misplaced. In the absence of compliance with Ark. R. Crim. P. 24.3(b), the supreme court lacked jurisdiction to hear the appeal, even though there had been an attempt at trial to enter a conditional plea.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

349 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


CR 02-1258


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


354 Ark. 226; 118 S.W.3d 542; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 472



September 25, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CLARK COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR2001-23, HON. JOHN ALEXANDER THOMAS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on direct appeal; reversed and remanded for resentencing on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Clark County Circuit Court (Arkansas) convicted defendant of 20 counts of violation of a minor in the first degree, contrary to Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-120 (1997), which was since repealed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions, raising various claims regarding alleged trial and sentencing errors. The State argued on cross-appeal that a no-term sentence imposed and a fine of zero dollars for 15 of the 20 convictions was illegal. The appeals court agreed with the State. First, former Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-120 did not deny defendant equal protection under the law, as the State had an interest in punishing school district employees who facilitated inappropriate relationships with children. Second, evidence that defendant violated a no contact order was properly admitted, because when said order was violated, defendant continued to harm the victim, adding to the injurious consequences of his crime. Third, while defendant was prosecuted for violation of a minor in the first degree and not rape, the commission of both offenses prohibited sexual intercourse or deviate sexual activity. Thus, consecutive sentences were proper. As to the State's cross-appeal, the sentence of no term of imprisonment and no fine was improper, as the sentencing range was five to twenty years' imprisonment, or a fine not to exceed $ 15,000, or both. Thus, resentencing was ordered.


OUTCOME: The judgments of conviction on all counts were affirmed. But, on the cross-appeal, the judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for resentencing on counts six through twenty.

Raymond v. State

Gaines v. State


CR 02-868


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


354 Ark. 89; 118 S.W.3d 102; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 457



September 18, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR2001-1300, HON. JOHN W. LANGSTON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which convicted defendant of rape, in violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-103(a)(4) (1997).


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly engaged in sexual activity with a 13 year old child. He was convicted of rape in violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-103(a)(4) (1997). After his conviction, defendant sought review. He contended that the trial court erred by failing to instruct the jury on a lesser-included offense and by not allowing him to present a mistake-of-age defense. In affirming, the court determined that carnal abuse in the third degree was not a lesser-included offense of § 5-14-103(a)(4). The carnal abuse statute, Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-106(a) (1997), contained elements that were not required by Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-103(a)(4) (1997). Further, defendant was unable to establish that carnal abuse in the third degree differed only from rape by the seriousness of harm to the victim. In addition, the court determined that defendant's due process rights were not violated by the trial court's refusal to allow a mistake-of-age defense. The court noted that it was within the power of the legislature to determine crimes and defenses. Further, there were exceptions to the rule that every crime was required to contain a mens rea element.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

352 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Craig v. Carrigo


01-1408


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


353 Ark. 761; 121 S.W.3d 154; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 377



June 26, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, TWELFTH DIVISION; NO. PAA 98-0639; HON. ALICE S. GRAY, JUDGE.
Craig v. Carrigo, 340 Ark. 624, 12 S.W.3d 229, 2000 Ark. LEXIS 120 (Ark., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a decedent's alleged common law wife and his personal representative, filed motion to determine heirship and legal interest in ancillary probate proceedings. The Pulaski County Circuit Court, Twelfth Division (Arkansas), entered a letter order, determining that the appellees, the decedent's children, were pretermitted heirs of the estate and thus entitled to inherit the real property located in Arkansas. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The decedent lived as married with the alleged common law wife in Alberta, Canada, for less than three years before he died. With a holographic will the common law wife initiated probate proceedings in Canada and ancillary proceedings in Arkansas, where the decedent had real and personal property. The children, not mentioned in the will, contested the same. The trial court determined that the children were pretermitted children entitled to the decedent's Arkansas real property under Ark. Code Ann. § 28-39-107(b) (1987). Applying Arkansas law as to the will pursuant to Ark. Code Ann. § 28-25-105 (1987), the court on appeal held that the trial court properly determined that there was no common law marriage. Alberta statutory law did not recognize common law marriages at the time of decedent's death, and the relationship did not meet the three-year cohabitation requirement under Alberta case law. The fact that national Canadian law recognized the common law marriage was irrelevant. The will failed to mention either of the decedent's children; hence, Ark. Code Ann. § 28-39-407(b) (1987) applied, and the children were entitled to the decedent's real property in Arkansas.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellants' request for review as to the award of attorney's fees and costs and affirmed the letter order in all other respects.

Jackson v. Ivory


02-1022


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


353 Ark. 847; 120 S.W.3d 587; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 379



June 26, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, SECOND DIVISION, NO. CV 00-11030, HON. CHRIS PIAZZA, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed & remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client sued respondents, attorney and her law firm, for professional negligence, respondeat superior, and negligent supervision. The Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) granted summary judgment for the lawyer and law firm. The client appealed.


OVERVIEW: The client had the attorney draft an agreement making arrangements to secure his loans to a business. The agreement was signed; however, since a financing statement was never filed, the lien was not perfected. When the business went bankrupt, the client was a creditor and he sued the attorney who failed to file the financing statement. He sued the lawyer's law firm also, claiming the firm was in privity with the lawyer. On appeal, the client argued that Ark. Code Ann. 16-22-310 (Supp. 1993) did not bar his claim of professional negligence against the lawyer and a material fact remained as to whether he was in privity with the lawyer, and a material fact remained as to whether there was an employer-employee relationship between the lawyer and the firm at the time of the lawyer's alleged negligence. The instant court agreed with the client on those points and reversed and remanded on those issues. The instant court found the client's respondeat superior claims against the firm were not barred by Ark. Code Ann. 16-22-310.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded on the trial court's finding that the client's respondeat superior claims against the firm were barred by statute and on the trial court's finding that there was no material factual dispute as to whether the client was in privity with the lawyer. The judgment was affirmed on all remaining points.

Williams v. Ark. State Bd. of Physical Therapy


02-1117


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


353 Ark. 778; 120 S.W.3d 581; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 396



June 26, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE JEFFERSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CIV-2000-428-3-2, HON. H. A. TAYLOR, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jefferson County Circuit Court, Arkansas, affirmed a decision of appellee, the Arkansas State Board of Physical Therapy, suspending the license of appellant physical therapist for three months and placing him on probation for a period of nine months after the completion of the suspension. The physical therapist appealed, asserting the trial court erred in concluding that the decision of the Board was not arbitrary and capricious.


OVERVIEW: The complaint, written by the husband of the patient, accused the physical therapist of immoral conduct. The physical therapist also argued the Board failed to exclude witnesses from the hearing room, under Ark. R. Evid. 615. However, the appellate court noted that the Arkansas Rules of Evidence were relaxed in administrative proceedings. Finally, there was substantial evidence to support the Board's decision, and, therefore, it was not arbitrary or capricious.

Weiss v. McFadden


02-1231


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


353 Ark. 868; 120 S.W.3d 545; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 378; 30 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2439



June 26, 2003, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by, Motion denied by Weiss v. McFadden, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 105 (Ark., Feb. 19, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, THIRTEENTH DIVISION, NO. OT 99-3939, HON. RAYMOND C. KILGORE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Arkansas Department of Finance and Administration (DFA) challenged a decision of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which granted partial summary judgment in favor of appellee taxpayers and found that the State violated Ark. Const. amend. 47 in connection with taxing benefits paid under a retirement plan pursuant to Ark. Code Ann. § 26-51-307 (Supp. 2001).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers were those who made after-tax contributions to retirement plans. The trial court found that the DFA violated Ark. Const. amend. 47 when it attempted to tax benefits paid under a retirement plan, where the benefit taxed after-tax contributions being returned to the taxpayer. The DFA argued that, under Ark. Code Ann. § 26-51-307 (Supp. 2001), the legislature declared that the return of retirement plan after-tax contributions was income. The court affirmed the partial summary judgment grant in the taxpayer's favor and held that, when after-tax contributions to a retirement plan were returned to a retiree, that return was property, not income. The attempt to levy a value-based tax on the after-tax contributions constituted an illegal exaction, because the DFA was attempting to levy a tax in violation of Ark. Const. amend. 47. Just because a state chose to characterize a tax as an income tax did not make it an income tax. The tax the DFA sought to collect was really an ad valorem tax on property, which was prohibited under the constitution. Thus, the DFA's attempted application of Ark. Code Ann. § 26-51-307 (Supp. 2001) was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

356 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Sidney Moncrief Pontiac, Buick, GMC Co.


02-449


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


353 Ark. 701; 120 S.W.3d 525; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 363



June 19, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT NO. CIV 00-2035 HON. WILLARD PROCTOR, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pulaski County Circuit Court, Arkansas, set aside a default judgment against appellees, car dealership and its successor, in appellant buyer's suit alleging fraud and a breach of contract after the buyer purchased a used car from the dealership that was found to be defective. The buyer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The buyer argued that the circuit court erred in dismissing her amended complaint with prejudice. The appellate court noted that the buyer's summonses were deficient under Ark. R. Civ. P. 4(b). Because the service requirements were strictly construed and compliance with them had to be exact, the complaint was properly dismissed for failure of service of valid process under Ark. R. Civ. P. 12(b). The one-year savings statute merely tolled the general statute of limitations. Ark. R. Civ. P. 41(b) applied to the second dismissal, which was an adjudication on the merits. The buyer's breach of contract claim against the dealership's successor should have been dismissed without prejudice. Her fraud claim was time barred because when she amended the complaint to add the successor, the three-year statute of limitations had expired. The buyer could not use Ark. R. Civ. P. 6(b) to enlarge the time to obtain service when she had not complied with Ark. R. Civ. P. 4(i). A summons that incorrectly identified the defendants and misstated the deadline for responding to the complaint did not comply with the service requirements. The constitutionality of Ark. R. Civ. P. 12(a) was upheld.


OUTCOME: The dismissal with prejudice of the buyer's amended complaint against the dealership, and the buyer's claim against the successor was affirmed; the order was modified to reflect that the buyer's breach of contract claim against the successor was dismissed without prejudice.

McLane Co. v. Davis


02-1057


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


353 Ark. 539; 110 S.W.3d 251; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 329



June 12, 2003, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at McLane S., Inc. v. Davis, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 303 (Ark., Apr. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF PULASKI COUNTY, ARKANSAS, NO. IJ-95-6966, HONORABLE COLLINS KILGORE, CIRCUIT JUDGE.
McLane Southern, Inc. v. Davis, 80 Ark. App. 30, 90 S.W.3d 16, 2002 Ark. App. LEXIS 650 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part for the trial court to enter an order consistent with this court's opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wholesaler sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Pulaski County (Arkansas), which found in favor of appellees, Arkansas Tobacco Control Board (board) and director, in an action involving Arkansas's Unfair Cigarette Sales Act (Act), Ark. Code Ann. §§ 4-75-701 to 713 (Repl. 1996), and the cost of doing business.


OVERVIEW: The legal dispute began in 1995 when the cigarette and other product wholesaler contacted the Department of Finance & Administration, requesting it to repeal Miscellaneous Tax Regulation 1988-2 that it promulgated pursuant to the Act. The director notified the wholesaler that it could commence selling cigarettes at the new minimum price, but the competitors filed an action requesting that the board be prohibited from implementing the new Miscellaneous Tax Regulation 1995-5. The board then rescinded its earlier approval of the wholesaler's new cost of doing business amount of .5 percent. The wholesaler then filed the current action, and the court previously reversed and remanded to determine how and under what authority the board acted when it determined and increased the basic cost of cigarettes to be at four percent. The court reversed in part, stating that the board failed to show that its regulation and actions fell within the Act's provision; thus, the four percent cost of doing business was arbitrary, ultra vires, and unenforceable. The two percent presumptive cost of doing business would then govern, thereby triggering the other valid remaining provisions of the regulation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part, stating that the board failed to show its regulation and actions fell within the Acts provision and remanded; the remainder was affirmed.

359 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Axley v. Hardin


02-1275


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


353 Ark. 529; 110 S.W.3d 766; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 342



June 12, 2003, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Southern College of Naturopathy v. State ex rel. Beebe, 2005 Ark. LEXIS 86 (Ark., Feb. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF SCOTT COUNTY, ARKANSAS, NO. CIV02-15; HONORABLE PAUL DANIELSON, CIRCUIT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a church and its associated college, taught students to perform religious functions, and specifically, "naturopathy," or the functions of natural healing. The church filed a petition for writ of mandamus on the issue of obtaining an exemption from the requirements of appellee, Arkansas Department of Higher Education. The Circuit Court of Scott County, Arkansas, denied the petition. The church appealed.


OVERVIEW: Ark. Code Ann. § 6-61-301 (Repl. 1996) empowered the Department to establish the criteria required for certification and to promulgate rules and regulations regarding degree programs. The church and its college offered two specific degree programs, and generally, degree programs granted by colleges and universities needed to be certified by the State. An exception came under Rule 8 of the Department's "Rules and Regulations for Institutional and Program Certification in Arkansas" (the Rules). Rule 8 provided an exception for certification in certain circumstances where the predominant purposes of the courses and programs were religious. That exception had to be pursued through the Arkansas Higher Education Coordinating Board. The appellate court concluded it was the church's responsibility to pursue the matter to completion through the Arkansas Higher Education Coordinating Board, which was charged with the responsibility of determining the propriety of exemptions. Here, the church could have brought such a declaratory action to determine whether or not Rule 8 should have applied. Thus, the church had an adequate alternative remedy and was not entitled to a writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, denying the writ of mandamus, was affirmed.

Comm. to Establish Sherwood Fire Dep't v. Hillman


02-1165


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


353 Ark. 501; 109 S.W.3d 641; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 322



June 5, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV 2002-10847, HON. CHRIS PIAZZA, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, committee to establish a municipal fire department, appealed a judgment of the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Second Division, Arkansas, in favor of appellee voters, which declared a ballot title and initiative petition unconstitutional. The committee argued that, as it was allowed to intervene, the circuit court should have allowed the committee to participate in the litigation concerning the ballot title and initiative petition.


OVERVIEW: The committee circulated a petition to place an ordinance "to create a fire department" on the city's general election ballot. The voters alleged that the ballot title and the proposed text of the ordinance were patently misleading. The circuit court agreed. The committee was allowed to intervene in the matter, but the circuit court informed the committee that a hearing on the merits could only be set on a date after the election, but that the committee could appeal to the Arkansas Supreme Court. Meanwhile, the commission was enjoined from placing the ballot title on the ballot. While the election was over, the Arkansas Supreme Court chose to address the issue of whether the committee had standing to intervene. The committee argued it had standing as a nonprofit association, pursuant to Ark. Code Ann. § 4-28-507 (Repl. 2001), and that it should have been joined as a necessary party pursuant to Ark. R. Civ. P. 19(a). The appellate court held the committee, which was not joined by a local voter and, further, did not purport to represent local voters, lacked standing to intervene in a case concerning rights that, pursuant to Ark. Const. amend. VII, were reserved to the local voters.

361 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Bank of Eureka Springs v. Evans


02-623


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


353 Ark. 438; 109 S.W.3d 672; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 324



June 5, 2003, Opinion Delievered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CARROLL COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, WESTERN DIVISION NO. 2000-76, HON. KIM SMITH, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee mortgagor obtained a loan from appellant bank to purchase land for a ranch. Later, the mortgagor informed the bank of his intent to file for bankruptcy. The enraged bank filed criminal complaints, alleging the mortgagor disposed of secured assets. The mortgagor was charged with felonies. A jury in the Carroll County Circuit Court, Western Division, Arkansas, held the bank liable for malicious prosecution. The bank appealed.


OVERVIEW: The bank approved a $ 460,000 loan for the mortgagor who had other outstanding loans with the bank. The mortgagor sought to turn undeveloped land into a cattle ranch by cutting the timber. A loan worksheet provided that half the loan could be repaid by timber sales. However, the mortgage provided that the mortgagor "could not cut timber from the encumbered land." When the mortgagor's fortunes collapsed, he considered bankruptcy. The bank then prosecuted through the county attorney, alleging the businessman wrongfully cut timber and illegally disposed of assets. The mortgagor was never convicted of the alleged offenses, but his reputation was badly damaged by the publicity. His construction business was basically destroyed as a result. The appellate court held the bank was not protected by the safe harbor provision of the Annunizo-Wylie Money Laundering Act, 31 U.S.C.S. § 5318(g)(3), an immunity provision. The appellate court held the Act did not give banks blanket immunity for malicious actions. Further, the trial court did not err in denying the bank its directed verdict motions, as there was substantial evidence to support the elements of malicious prosecution.


OUTCOME: The appellate court held the jury's award of $ 100,000 compensatory damages for the businessman, in light of almost $ 40,000 of actual damages, as well as mental anguish stemming from fear of imprisonment, embarrassment before the community, and destruction of his business reputation, was supported by substantial evidence. The award of $ 300,000 in punitive damages was proper under the circumstances. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Anderson v. State


CR 01-1131


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


353 Ark. 384; 108 S.W.3d 592; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 307



May 29, 2003, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Anderson v. Arkansas, 540 U.S. 1050, 124 S. Ct. 832, 157 L. Ed. 2d 699, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 8628 (2003)
Appeal dismissed by, Motion denied by Anderson v. State, 2006 Ark. LEXIS 109 (Ark., Jan. 12, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by Anderson v. Norris, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 10114 (E.D. Ark., Feb. 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] NO. CR-2000-79-2. APPEAL FROM THE CHICOT COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT HON. SAM POPE, JUDGE.
Anderson v. State, 351 Ark. 675, 100 S.W.3d 48, 2003 Ark. LEXIS 88 (Ark., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part. Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Chicot County Circuit Court (Arkansas), convicting him of murdering the victim and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for shooting the victim to death. At trial, defendant claimed that he shot the victim in self-defense during a fight. On appeal, the court held that the prosecutor did not clearly and unequivocally misstate the State's burden of disproving self-defense beyond a reasonable doubt during voir dire, and, therefore, the trial court did not manifestly abuse its discretion by failing to instruct the jury not to consider same. The prosecutor relied on the Arkansas Model Jury Instructions, Criminal, as the basis for his definition and explanation of proof beyond a reasonable doubt, his statements to the jury about conflicting testimony were not technically incorrect, but his statements represented a subtle attempt to shift the burden of proof by equating defendant's burden of proof with the State's burden. The court reversed defendant's death sentence because verdict Form 2 was not signed or filed, and, therefore, the court was unable to say that the jury considered any possible mitigating circumstances, much less that it concluded that beyond a reasonable doubt that the only aggravating circumstance outweighed any mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: Defendant's murder conviction was affirmed, but his death sentence was reversed and the case was remanded for resentencing.

Holloway v. Ark. State Bd. of Architects


02-1096


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


352 Ark. 427; 101 S.W.3d 805; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 164



April 3, 2003, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.
Related proceeding at Holloway v. Ark. State Bd. of Architects, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 15447 (8th Cir. Ark., July 27, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pulaski Circuit Court; David B. Bogard, Judge.
Holloway v. Ark. State Bd. of Architects, 79 Ark. App. 200, 86 S.W.3d 391, 2002 Ark. App. LEXIS 558 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee architect filed a complaint with the Arkansas State Board of Architects, alleging that appellant engineer, as a non-architect, designed and stamped different aspects of a project. The board found that the engineer practiced architecture without a license, and it imposed a fine. The engineer filed an appeal to the trial court and then appealed to the Arkansas Court of Appeals. The board petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The engineer prepared and filed plans for a metal building. The engineer asserted that it was his understanding that his work on the facility was well within the realm of engineering activity. On appeal, the engineer argued that the statutes defining the practice of architecture and the practice of engineering were void for vagueness. The appellate court determined, however, that a person of ordinary intelligence could glean that architects plan and design buildings primarily intended for people to live and work in, and engineers plan and design buildings primarily intended for accommodation of equipment, vehicles, goods, and/or processes. The statutes were not void for vagueness. The engineer also argued that the board failed to make necessary findings of fact. The appellate court disagreed. The board's findings contained relevant sufficient facts so that the appellate court could determine whether the board resolved those issues in conformity with the law. The engineer also argued that the penalty imposed by the board was arbitrary, capricious, and an abuse of discretion. Nevertheless, the imposition of the civil penalty was supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.
