Beulah v. State


CR 02-704


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


352 Ark. 472; 101 S.W.3d 802; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 166



April 3, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF PULASKI COUNTY, NO. CR 99-3726, HONORABLE JOHN B. PLEGGE, JUDGE.
Beulah v. State, 344 Ark. 528, 42 S.W.3d 461, 2001 Ark. LEXIS 269 (Ark., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Pulaski County (Arkansas), which found in favor of appellee State and denied his postconviction petition; he pled guilty to murder in the first degree and battery.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was charged with capital murder in the death of a fetus in its ninth month of gestation and battery of the mother. He was charged under Act 1273 of 1999, the Arkansas Fetal Protection Act, which redefined "person" for purposes of the state's homicide statutes to include a fetus beyond 12 weeks of development. Ark. Code Ann. § 5-1-102(13)(B)(i)(b) (Supp. 1999). He subsequently pled guilty to murder in the first degree and battery. He claimed that he entered into the plea agreement with the condition that he would be permitted to pursue his constitutional challenge under Ark. R. Crim. P. 37. The trial court denied his postconviction petition, and the court affirmed. When a guilty plea was challenged under R. 37, the sole issue was whether the plea was intelligently and voluntarily entered with the advice of competent counsel. Rule 37 did not provide an avenue to raise matters that could have been raised on direct appeal, including constitutional claims, and a constitutional claim was not in itself sufficient to trigger application of R. 37. The inmate's claims were not cognizable under the rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

366 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Carwell Elevator Co. v. Leathers


02-240


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


352 Ark. 381; 101 S.W.3d 211; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 147



March 20, 2003, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. OT 2000-758, HON. COLLINS KILGORE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged a decision from the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which entered judgment in favor of appellees, Arkansas Commissioner of Revenue and a research board, by determining that the taxpayers were unable to recover assessments paid as first-time rice buyers.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers paid an assessment to the research board as first-time rice buyers under Ark. Code Ann. § 2-20-511 (1996). A company filed an action claiming that the assessment was an illegal exaction, in violation of Ark. Const. art. 16, § 13. Subsequently, it was determined that § 2-20-511 constituted an unlawful delegation of legislative authority under Ark. Const. art. 2, § 23. It was not decided whether or not the assessment constituted an illegal exaction. The taxpayers then filed an illegal exaction action, which sought a refund of all assessments paid. After the trial court determined that the taxpayers were not entitled to a refund because the assessments were voluntarily paid, they sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the issues adjudicated in the prior action were not limited to the company that filed the action. The action filed by the company constituted a class action, which was prosecuted on behalf of all affected taxpayers. Moreover, the case was not barred by the doctrine of res judicata, as the taxpayers were not given proper notice of the suit. Finally, the court found that the action was not barred by laches for the same reason.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

Craighead Elec. Coop. Corp. v. Craighead County


02-812


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


352 Ark. 76; 98 S.W.3d 414; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 96



February 20, 2003, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Craighead Circuit Court, No. CIV 99-0650(H), Victor Hill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cooperative challenged a decision of the Craighead County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which granted appellee county summary judgment in connection with the cooperative's action alleging that the county had encroached on easements and rights of way owned or possessed by the cooperative.


OVERVIEW: The cooperative claimed that it incurred significant expenses in moving power lines and poles after the county widens roads that encroached on the cooperative's easements and rights-of-way. The county claimed that it had a right-of-way in the land used to widen the roads based on an earlier court order. The trial court ruled in the county's favor. The court reversed and found that summary judgment was improperly granted. The earlier order did not purport to convey a property interest to the county. Whether the county, the cooperative, or both possessed a right-of-way in the land adjoining the roadway had not been determined below. The trial court was required to determine what rights, if any, both the county and the cooperative possessed in the land in question. If the cooperative had a property interest in the land where the poles and power lines were standing before the roads were widened, then forcing the movement of the poles and lines might have constituted a taking that required compensation, and the common law rule that a utility was to bear the costs of relocation did not apply where the county widened the road, but only when relocation was required by a public necessity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision.

Jones v. Double "D" Props.


02-717


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


352 Ark. 39; 98 S.W.3d 405; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 95



February 20, 2003, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Jones v. Double "D" Props., 357 Ark. 148, 161 S.W.3d 839, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 274 (Ark., 2004)
Related proceeding at, Motion granted by, Dismissed by Jones v. Double "D" Props., 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 49655 (W.D. Ark., Apr. 5, 2005)
Related proceeding at Stilley v. Marschewski, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 49654 (W.D. Ark., May 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Sebastian Circuit Court , No. E-01-710; Mark Hewett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, taxpayer wife and taxpayer husband, challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Sebastian County, Arkansas, which (1) found that appellee Commissioner of State Lands (Arkansas) complied with Ark. Code Ann. § 26-37-301 (1997) in informing both taxpayers about the sale of their property for delinquent taxes to appellee buyer and (2) found that both taxpayers' constitutional arguments were not timely raised.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner sold the land to the buyer after the real estate taxes were not paid. The trial court found that the notice of the sale given by the Commissioner was valid. The court agreed. Ark. Code Ann. § 26-37-301 (1997) required notice by certified mail, and the Commissioner strictly complied with the statute's requirements. The statute did not require that the Commissioner take every step possible to see that the letter arrived. The court agreed with the trial court that the constitutional issues were not properly raised. While the taxpayer wife had filed a motion for a new trial, the constitutional issues raised therein should have been raised earlier. The trial court did not err in dismissing the taxpayer husband's constitutional claim pursuant to Ark. R. Civ. P. 13(a). The taxpayer husband's claims arose out of the same transaction that was the subject of the original matter, and as such the claim was a compulsory counterclaim that should have been brought during the trial of the matter instead of later. Because the issues raised by the taxpayer husband were not timely presented, the dismissal of his claim was also affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Davis v. State


CR 02-534


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


351 Ark. 406; 94 S.W.3d 892; 2003 Ark. LEXIS 2



January 9, 2003, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE UNION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR-2000-242, HON. CAROL CRAFTON ANTHONY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Arkansas Court of Appeals reversed defendant's convictions for possession of drug paraphernalia and possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, holding that the police lacked a reasonable suspicion to believe defendant was engaged in illegal activity. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the court of appeals failed to apply the totality-of-the-circumstances test in concluding that the evidence should be suppressed. For clarification of the standard of review, the appellate court concluded that the standard was that the appellate court conduct a de novo review based on the totality of the circumstances, reviewing findings of historical facts for clear error and determining whether those facts gave rise to reasonable suspicion or probable cause, giving due weight to inferences drawn by the trial court. The appellate court concluded that the police had a reasonable suspicion to make the stop. Defendant and another man were in a high crime area known for drug activity. Defendant exhibited nervous, evasive behavior, which was a pertinent factor in determining reasonable suspicion. The testimony revealed that the officer was concerned about the possibility of drugs and weapons violations. He had seen defendant engage in a hand-to-hand transaction with another man, and he did not know what was in defendant's pocket. As such, the pat-down search was justified under the totality of the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Finney v. Cook


02-475


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


351 Ark. 367; 94 S.W.3d 333; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 639



December 19, 2002, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: HONORABLE VICKI S. COOK, CIRCUIT JUDGE, 18TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT (EAST).



DISPOSITION: Petition for Writ of Prohibition; denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother was in the military, based out-of-state. The children's grandparents had been granted guardianship over the children. The Circuit Court of the 18th Judicial District (East), State of Arkansas, ordered the mother to appear and show cause why she should not be held in contempt. The mother petitioned the instant court for a writ of prohibition, and the circuit court stayed the proceeding pending the instant court's ruling.


OVERVIEW: The mother joined the Army and was stationed in Hawaii. Ultimately, the grandparents were granted guardianship over the children. The grandparents then filed a petition for contempt, alleging that the mother had removed the children. The issue was whether service on a court-appointed attorney for the absent military mother was sufficient service of process in a case of continuing jurisdiction. The mother's argument was that the trial court was without jurisdiction to enter the guardianship order due to a lack of personal jurisdiction, because neither she nor her children lived in Arkansas, and she was not properly served with notice. The State countered that under Ark. Code Ann. § 28-1-112(e) (Supp. 2001), notice could be served upon the party's attorney of record. It was undisputed that service was made on the mother's attorney of record. Thus, the service of notice was in compliance with § 28-1-112(e). There may have been a conflict between the provisions of Ark. R. Civ. P. 5, and Ark. Code Ann. § 28-1-112(e) (Supp. 2001). Ark. R. Civ. P. 5 required service on the party. However, the mother did not brief this issue, and the appellate court held the trial court had jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The mother's writ of prohibition was denied.

Eady v. Lansford


02-695


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


351 Ark. 249; 92 S.W.3d 57; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 631



December 12, 2002, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF SEBASTIAN COUNTY, ARKANSAS, NO. 00-89; HONORABLE J. MICHAEL FITZHUGH, CIRCUIT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Sebastian County (Arkansas), which granted appellee physician's motion for summary judgment in a medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The physician prescribed a certain drug to the patient, who was suffering from sinus problems. The patient was later hospitalized for a severe reaction to the drug. The patient contended that the physician failed to inform him of the possible side effects. He also alleged that the physician failed to obtain his informed consent before prescribing the drug. The physician's motion for summary judgment was accompanied by an expert's affidavit. The patient did not respond to the affidavit. After summary judgment was granted, the patient sought review. In affirming, the court determined that Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-206(b), which set forth the burden of proof in an informed consent case, was constitutional. Specifically, § 16-114-206(b) required a medical expert in every case involving informed consent. The court also held that there was a rational basis for drawing a distinction between informed consent cases and other medical malpractice cases. There was a rational relationship between the burden of proof required and the achievement of a legitimate governmental objective. Finally, the court declined to apply the "common knowledge" exception to informed consent cases.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment granted in favor of the physician was affirmed.

Bell v. Bershears


02-702


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


351 Ark. 260; 92 S.W.3d 32; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 632



December 12, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE GARLAND COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT; NO. CIV 2000-4-I; HON. JOHN HOMER WRIGHT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sued appellee driver in the Circuit Court of Garland County, Arkansas, for personal injuries resulting from a traffic accident. Both parties file postjudgment motions for costs. The trial court granted the driver's motion and denied the claimant's. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The driver offered to settle the case for 13,589, with costs accrued to the date of the offer. The claimant rejected the offer and the case went to trial. The jury returned a verdict for the claimant in the amount of $ 13,200. The claimant sought to recover her costs under Ark. R. Civ. P. 54(d) on the grounds that she was the prevailing party. The driver sought to recover his costs from the date of the offer under Ark. R. Civ. P. 68 on the grounds that the claimant's recovery was less than the offer. The trial court granted the driver's motion but denied on the claimant's on the grounds that the award to the driver precluded an award to the claimant. The appellate court held that the two rules were not mutually exclusive, and both parties could recover costs on the facts in this case. The case was remanded to the trial court to determine the amount of the claimant's costs. The award would, however be limited to costs accrued prior to the offer because those costs, plus the amount of the award, did exceed the offer. The claimant could not include post-offer costs to determine whether the award exceeded the offer.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part.

Williams v. State


CR 02-21


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


351 Ark. 229; 91 S.W.3d 68; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 608



December 5, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF SEBASTIAN COUNTY, ARKANSAS, FORT SMITH DISTRICT, NO. CR 97-359, HONORABLE J. MICHAEL FITZHUGH, CIRCUIT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in Wisconsin of third-degree sexual assault. Defendant was later convicted of breaking or entering and felony theft of property in Arkansas and given suspended sentences. The State subsequently sought to revoke defendant's suspended sentences alleging defendant failed to register as a sex offender. The Sebastian County Circuit Court (Arkansas) revoked defendant's suspended sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that the revocation of his suspended sentence on the basis of the amended version of Ark. Code Ann. § 12-12-905 was an unconstitutional ex post facto application of the law. Defendant also argued that there was insufficient evidence to warrant the revocation of his suspended sentence. The appellate court rejected defendant's arguments. Defendant's ex post facto argument failed because his sentence was imposed in October of 1997, and, the effective date of the amendment was August 1, 1997. Thus, defendant had 30 days after August 1, 1997, in which to register, and he failed to do so. The court also found that because the evidence showed that defendant was convicted of a sex offense and registered as a sex offender in Wisconsin, had lived in Arkansas since 1992, and failed to register as a sex offender in Arkansas in accordance with the requirements in § 12-12-905, the State met its burden of proving that defendant violated a condition of his suspended sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Fegans v. Norris


01-1233


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


351 Ark. 200; 89 S.W.3d 919; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 587



November 21, 2002, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF LEE COUNTY, CIV 2000-54, HONORABLE HARVEY LEE YATES, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a civil rights action against appellees, the director and the assistant director of the Arkansas Department of Correction (ADC), in their official and individual capacities. The alleged causes of action arose out of an administrative directive concerning prisoner cleanliness and grooming. The Lee County Circuit Court, Arkansas, dismissed the action with prejudice for failure to state a claim. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1978, inmates of the ADC filed a class action suit against ADC officials, raising First Amendment challenges to ADC grooming and food policies. The parties entered a mediated settlement agreement. As a result of the agreement, the ADC issued a less restrictive grooming policy. In 1998, the ADC issued a new grooming policy, which set standardized hair length and prohibited beards. Federal courts refused to find the ADC in contempt and, ultimately, terminated the settlement agreement. The inmate entered the ADC in 1991. He claimed his religion required that his beard and hair not be clipped beyond that allowed by the Bible. The inmate alleged he was disciplined following the enactment of the 1998 policy. The supreme court held that because the inmate's request for relief, if granted, would control the action of the ADC, a state agency, and subject it to liability, his claims against the director and the assistant director in their official capacities were constitutionally barred. The director and the assistant director were personally immune from suit because they did not violate clearly established principles of law of which a reasonable person would have knowledge.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the inmate's complaint was modified to be without prejudice. As modified, the order was affirmed.

Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee


01-836


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


351 Ark. 31; 91 S.W.3d 472; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 603



November 21, 2002, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.
Motion denied by Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 351 Ark. 385, 94 S.W.3d 340, 2002 Ark. LEXIS 640 (Ark., 2002)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wilson v. Huckabee, 538 U.S. 1035, 123 S. Ct. 2097, 155 L. Ed. 2d 1066, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 3753 (2003)
Later proceeding at Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 355 Ark. 501, 2004 Ark. LEXIS 569 (Ark., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CHANCERY COURT, NO. 92-5318, HON. RAYMOND COLLINS KILGORE, Chancellor.
Lake View Sch. Dist. No. 25 v. Huckabee, 340 Ark. 481, 10 S.W.3d 892, 2000 Ark. LEXIS 105 (Ark., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; attorney's fees affirmed as modified; stay issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee school district and others (the district) sued appellant State officials (the State) in the Chancery Court of Pulaski County, Arkansas, challenging the constitutionality of the school-funding system (the system). The trial court held that the system violated the Arkansas Constitution. The court awarded over $ 9,000,000 in attorney fees to the district, but denied costs. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that the system violated the education and equality articles of the Arkansas Constitution. The ruling also addressed other specific aspects of the system. The appellate court agreed that the State had not fulfilled its duty to provide an adequate school funding system in violation of Ark. Const. art. 14, § 1. The system also violated Ark. Const. art. 2, §§ 2, 3, and 18, the equality articles, because the system did not ensure equality of funding among school districts on a per student basis, and there was no rational basis for such discrepancies. The constitution did not, however, require the creation of pre-school programs. The appellate court further held that the trial court properly excluded desegregation funds and weighted average daily membership in determining funding equality. The trial court had, however, erred in applying Ark. Code Ann. § 26-80-204(18)(C) (Supp. 2001), regarding excess millage, as the statute violated Ark. Const. amend. 74. A total of approximately $ 3,000,000 in attorney fees and costs were approved. The court stayed its mandate to allow the State time to fashion a system that met constitutional requirements.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order regarding the unconstitutionality of the public school-funding system was affirmed, but some portions of the ruling were reversed. The attorney fee award was modified and costs were granted. The appellate court stayed its mandate until January 1, 2004.

Republican Party of Ark. v. Kilgore


02-1181


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


350 Ark. 540; 98 S.W.3d 798; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 554



November 7, 2002, Opinion Delivered



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Emergency Petition for Writ of Certiorari granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the Republican Party of Arkansas and a member of the county election commission, filed an emergency petition for writ of certiorari in the state supreme court. The stated purpose of the petition for certiorari was to void the emergency order of the judge of the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas) to extend voting hours.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, the Democratic Party of Arkansas and its counsel, prayed for an immediate hearing to extended the voting hours. The circuit court judge granted the motion and extended the voting hours. Counsel for the Republican Party of Arkansas argued that the circuit court judge had no authority to extend voting hours and that to do so was an abuse of discretion. Counsel for the Democratic Party of Arkansas argued that registered voters had a constitutional right to vote and they were being deprived of that right. Members of six of the justices for the state supreme court voted to void the circuit court judge's emergency order. The state supreme court held that the election law, Ark. Code Ann. § 7-5-304 (2000), was clear that the polls opened at 7:30 a.m. on the day of the election and closed at 7:30 p.m. The legislative branch had spoken on that issue, and there was no provision in the Arkansas Election Code authorizing an extension of voting times by the judiciary. Thus, the circuit court judge clearly abused his discretion and exceeded his authority in extending the voting hours to 9:00 p.m. in contravention of state law.


OUTCOME: The petition for writ of certiorari was granted; the circuit court judge's order was void.

Sullivan v. Norris


02-884


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


2002 Ark. LEXIS 555



November 7, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION. PLEASE REFER TO THE ARKANSAS RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIRCUIT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY, NO. CIV 2002-564-5.



DISPOSITION: MOTION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition in the Circuit Court of Jefferson County, Arkansas, for declaratory judgment alleging that the retroactive application of a sex offender registration statute to his rape conviction violated the constitutional provision against ex post facto laws. The trial court denied the petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a notice of appeal from the trial court's order and attempted to lodge the record with the appellate court without paying a filing fee. When he was notified that he was required to remit a filing fee, he filed a motion asking the appellate court to waive the fee. The appellate court initially noted the inmate clearly failed to state a claim on which the trial court could have granted him the relief sought; thus, pursuant to Ark. R. Civ. Code Ann. § 12-12-901 et seq. was applicable to persons who were found guilty of a sex offense on or after August 1, 1997, or who were serving a sentence of incarceration on August 1, 1997, as a result of an adjudication of guilt for a sex offense. The appellate court concluded the inmate's rape conviction qualified under the registration statute and was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The inmate's motion to waive the filing fee for his notice of appeal was denied.

Lee v. Daniel


01-676


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


350 Ark. 466; 91 S.W.3d 464; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 563



November 7, 2002, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY, ARKANSAS, NO. CIV-98-358; HONORABLE BERLIN JONES, CIRCUIT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee lawyer sued appellant mother in the Jefferson County Circuit Court (Arkansas), seeking recovery under a contingency fee contract. The trial court concluded that there was no justifiable cause for the mother's termination of the contract and that the lawyer had a valid attorney's lien against a proposed settlement with the tortfeasor for injuries to the mother's two minor sons. The mother's appeal was certified to the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that the mother failed to preserve the issue of the constitutionality of Arkansas' attorney's lien statute, Ark. Code Ann. § 16-22-301 et seq., for its review, because she failed to raise her claim until her motion for new trial. Therefore, the supreme court was concerned only with the validity of the contract and the attorney's lien against the proposed settlement to which it gave rise. The mother argued that 13 of the trial court's findings of fact were clearly against the preponderance of the evidence. The supreme court found there was ample evidence from which the trial court could conclude that the mother entered into a valid contract with the lawyer and did not have cause to terminate him. The mother asserted that the trial court abused its discretion in excluding the expert testimony of her witness, a nurse. The nurse conceded that she could not authenticate her medical records. The mother failed to proffer the substance of the nurse's testimony or her opinions as to what possible effects the medication might have had on the mother's state of mind to enter into the contract. Failure to make an offer of proof precluded appellate review of the issue.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's findings of fact and conclusions of law.

M. M. v. State


02-107


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


350 Ark. 328; 88 S.W.3d 406; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 517



October 24, 2002, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Lonoke Circuit Court, Juvenile Division; Philip Whiteaker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile was charged with the rape of a victim under 14, and was adjudicated a delinquent in the Juvenile Division of the Circuit Court of Lonoke County (Arkansas). The juvenile had moved to present testimony bearing on the child's prior sexual conduct. The trial court denied the motion. The juvenile appealed, asserting that the rape shield statute, Ark. Code Ann. § 16-42-101 (Repl. 1999), was inapplicable to a juvenile proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile asserted that even if Ark. Code Ann. § 16-42-101 (Repl. 1999) was constitutional, the statute should not be applicable to juvenile proceedings. The rape shield statute itself set out in clear words that it was to be applied "in any criminal prosecution" involving rape or other sexual offenses. The appellate court held that because a juvenile-delinquency proceeding was not a criminal prosecution, Ark. Code Ann. § 16-42-101 was inapplicable to the juvenile's proceeding. But the appellate court had to decide whether the trial court abused its discretion in excluding the juvenile's proffered testimony on the basis of that testimony's irrelevance under Ark. R. Evid. 401. The appellate court noted that a person who had sexual intercourse or deviate sexual activity with one less than 14 years of age was guilty of the crime, regardless of how old he or she thought the victim was, and regardless of whether there was consent. Because the victim was under the age of 14, the victim's sexual past was completely irrelevant to the question of whether or not the juvenile engaged in sexual activity with the victim. Therefore, the trial court properly excluded the proffered testimony.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court was affirmed.

 

380 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Ward v. Priest


02-954


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


350 Ark. 345; 86 S.W.3d 884; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 526



October 24, 2002, Opinion Delivered



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen petitioned the court maintaining that, pursuant to Ark. Const. amend. VII, references to matters outside the ballot title were insufficient to inform the voters concerning the choice they were to make, the title failed to inform voters about the fiscal consequences of the proposed amendment, and the definitions of "food" and "medicine" were misleading.


OVERVIEW: The citizen's petition dealt with a proposed amendment to the Arkansas Constitution to abolish taxes on food and medicine. Respondent Secretary of State argued that the court did not have jurisdiction until after the secretary had certified an initiative petition pursuant to Ark. Const. amend. VII. The reviewing court found that 1999 Ark. Acts 877, codified at Ark. Code Ann. § 7-9-503(a)(1) (Repl. 2000), provided a procedure whereby a taxpayer could seek an early review of a ballot title's legal sufficiency prior to the gathering of signatures; that is, it was discretionary. Sufficiency of a ballot title was a matter of law to be decided by the court. The definitions of "food" and "medicine" in the ballot title incorporated and established benchmark. It was an impartial description that adequately identified the proposed amendment. A voter would be capable of understanding that any item eligible to be purchased or otherwise available under any state or federal nutrition or health care assistance program would no longer be taxed. The ballot title presented the voter with a fair understanding of the issues presented and the scope and significance of the proposed changes.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

381 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Webb v. Bouton


01-920


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


350 Ark. 254; 85 S.W.3d 885; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 479



October 3, 2002, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SEBASTIAN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CV98-952, HON. JAMES ROBERT MARSCHEWSKI, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sebastian County Circuit Court, Arkansas, granted judgment in favor of appellees, surgeon and clinic, in appellant patient's medical malpractice suit against the surgeon and clinic. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued that the trial court erred in allowing the surgeon to testify as to the standard of care; that the trial court erred when it allowed another doctor to testify; and that the jury's verdict was against the preponderance of the evidence. The appellate court would not address the merits of the patient's argument regarding the alleged conflict between Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-207(3) and Ark. R. Civ. P. 26(b)(1) as it was not raised at the trial level. The appellate court could not determine whether the surgeon and clinic were able to hide their opinions and surprise the patient at trial when the record contained no information to support the argument. The patient did not show how Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-207(3) of the Arkansas Medical Malpractice Act, Ark. Code Ann. § 16-114-207 to -209 (1987), had adversely impacted upon her. The two doctors were not so similar in their credentials and approach to issues that their testimony should be considered cumulative. There was extensive testimony on both sides and substantial evidence for the jury to find in the surgeon's favor. The burden of proof to establish causation was upon the patient, as the plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

382 of 594 DOCUMENTS


City of Siloam Springs v. Benton County


01-869


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


350 Ark. 152; 85 S.W.3d 504; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 470



September 26, 2002, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Benton County v. City of Bentonville, 2008 Ark. LEXIS 312 (Ark., May 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE BENTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, CIV-99-197-1, HON. TOM J. KEITH, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee county filed a declaratory judgment action in the Benton County Circuit Court, Arkansas, alleging that 1963 Ark. Acts 219 was an unconstitutional violation of Ark. Const. amend. 14's prohibition against the passage of any local or special act. The trial court held the act was unconstitutional. Appellant city challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: In its petition, the county argued 1963 Ark. Acts 219 was unconstitutional because it apportioned 90 percent of the road tax funds collected from within the corporate limits of the cities to the cities. The trial court agreed and declared the act unconstitutional. The city appealed, arguing the trial court erred in granting summary judgment without requiring the county to meet its burden of proof that the act was not rationally related to achieving a legitimate objective of state government. The appellate court initially noted merely because a statute ultimately affected less than all of the state's territory did not necessarily render it unconstitutional local or special legislation. The appellate court held an act of the general assembly that applied to only a portion of the state was constitutional if the reason for limiting the act to one area was rationally related to the purposes of that act. The appellate court concluded the county did not meet its burden of proving that the act was not rationally related to achieving a legitimate governmental objective.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded.

 

383 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Gulledge v. Barclay


02-88


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


350 Ark. 98; 84 S.W.3d 850; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 447



September 19, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, SEVENTEENTH DIVISION, NO. IJ2000-6144, HON. MACKIE PIERCE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The General Assembly passed Act 1 of the Second Extraordinary Session of 1999 (Act 1), which the governor then signed. Appellants, acting on their own behalf and on behalf of other taxpayers similarly situated, sued, challenging the constitutionality of Act 1, in the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Seventeenth Division (Arkansas). The Circuit Court upheld the constitutionality of the Act, and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: The general assembly convened an extraordinary session at the governor's call to address the need for a one-half percent sales and use tax increase. There were two issues on appeal: (1) whether the emergency clause of Act 1 was valid under Ark. Const. amend. 7; and (2) whether a bill introduced in a three-day extraordinary session of the general assembly was unconstitutional under Ark. Const. art. 5 § 34. The circuit court found the emergency clause presented numerous facts. Although fair-minded reasonable persons might differ as to their sufficiency and truth, they were sufficient to meet the highly deferential standard under which the judiciary reviewed legislative emergency clauses. The circuit court ruled that Act 1 was not in violation of Ark. Const. art. 5 § 34, as that constitutional provision prohibiting bills from being filed during the last three days of a legislative session did not apply to bills filed during an extraordinary session called by the governor. The question was whether the general assembly stated facts constituting an emergency upon which reasonable minds might disagree.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

384 of 594 DOCUMENTS


S. Farm Bureau Cas. Ins. Co. v. Brinker


01-1435


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


350 Ark. 15; 84 S.W.3d 846; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 434



September 12, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM ST. FRANCIS CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE HARVEY LEE YATES, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of an order of the St. Francis, Arkansas, Circuit Court, which awarded attorney fees and post-judgment interest to appellee victim.


OVERVIEW: The victim had been injured in an accident caused by the negligence of a school district and its employee. The insurer provided underinsured motorist coverage for the victim and the victim joined the insurer as a defendant on that basis. The trial court severed the insurer from the original action and held that the insurer would not be bound by any judgment against the school district or the employee. A jury awarded the victim the full $ 100,000 sought. The victim then filed a demand on the insurer for the $ 75,000 still owed. The insurer refused to pay and the victim appealed. The appellate court reversed the severance order and held that the insurer was bound by the judgment. On remand, the trial court granted the victim attorney fees and post-judgment interest from the date of the original judgment. The appellate court held that the attorney fee award was proper because the victim's claim against the insurer was for the full amount owed. The total amount of the judgment was irrelevant. The interest award was proper because the appellate court's original decision had not reversed the initial award to the victim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The appellate court also granted the victim's motion for attorney fees on appeal.

 

385 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Ballard v. Martin


01-1185


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


349 Ark. 564; 79 S.W.3d 838; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 400



July 5, 2002, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CRAIGHEAD COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CIV 2000-0669, HON. DAVID N. LASER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant objectors challenged a decision of the Craighead County Circuit Court (Arkansas), which approved a class action settlement between appellees, class representatives and several check-cashing companies.


OVERVIEW: The class action was brought against the companies and charged that they engaged in usurious lending practices. A settlement was reached between the class representatives and the companies. After receiving notice of the proposed settlement, the objectors filed motions to intervene in the action, which were granted. They also issued subpoenas for the financial records of the companies, in an attempt to bolster their argument that the settlement reached was not fair or adequate. The trial court approved the settlement and the court affirmed, giving deference to the trial court's decision that the settlement was fair and adequate. The supreme court adopted certain factors in determining whether any settlement was adequate. The court rejected the objectors' claim of collusion. While the settlement was hurriedly entered into, there was no proof that the settlement was not made at arm's length. The fact that the class could have gotten more did not translate into collusion. The class representatives were adequate representatives as required by Ark. R. Civ. P. 23(a)(4), and the notices of the class action, settlement, and fairness hearing comported with due process as required.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's decision that approved the class action settlement.

Jegley v. Picado


01-815


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


349 Ark. 600; 80 S.W.3d 332; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 401



July 5, 2002, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. 01-815, HON. DAVID B. BOGARD, JUDGE, AFFIRMED..



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, acting in his official capacity as prosecuting attorney for the Sixth Judicial District, Arkansas, was sued by appellees, six gay and lesbian Arkansas citizens. Appellant sought review of the order of the Pulaski County Circuit Court, Arkansas, declaring Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-122 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Several gay and lesbian citizens of Arkansas filed a declaratory judgment action seeking to have Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-122 declared unconstitutional insofar as it criminalized specific acts of private, consensual sexual intimacy between persons of the same sex. Complaining citizens admitted they violated the statute in the past and alleged that they intend to engage in conduct prohibited by the statute in the future. As members of the class targeted by the statute, these citizens contended that they were harmed by the law because § 5-14-122 criminalized their private, intimate conduct. The court ruled that Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-122 impermissibly criminalized conduct solely on the basis of the sex of the participants in violation of Arkansas's Equal Rights Amendment, Ark. Const. art. 2, § 18. The statute was overturned.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

387 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Short v. State


CR 01-1269


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


349 Ark. 492; 79 S.W.3d 313; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 383



June 27, 2002, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE POPE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR-2000-433, HON. JOHN S. PATTERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree sexual abuse in violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-108(a)(4) (Repl. 1997) (repealed), in the Pope County Circuit Court (Arkansas). At trial, defendant's motion in limine to allow testimony to prove he reasonably believed the victim was over the age of 14, and his motion for a directed verdict that the State failed to prove the element of mental culpability for the offense was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's appeal raised the issue of whether the State had the burden of proving a culpable mental state in connection with a charge of first-degree sexual abuse involving a victim under the age of 14. Defendant was convicted under former Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-108(a)(4) (Repl. 1997) (repealed) for which the corresponding present offense would be Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-125(a)(3) (Supp. 2001). The appellate court held that the statutory rape provision at the time, Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-103(a)(4) (Repl. 1997) (superseded), and Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-108(a)(4) (Repl. 1997) (repealed), were subject to a specific statute, Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-102(b), that eliminated knowledge, or even a reasonable belief, of the victim's age as a defense. Thus, the trial court did not err in ruling that the State was not required to prove defendant's knowledge of the victim's age in a prosecution for first-degree sexual abuse under Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-108(a)(4) (Repl. 1997) (repealed). Defendant's argument that the victim's statements that occurred on the day of the offense should have been admitted was rejected as encompassed by the rape-shield statute, Ark. Code Ann. § 16-42-101(b) (Repl. 1999).


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Seagrave v. Price


01-1370


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


349 Ark. 433; 79 S.W.3d 339; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 393



June 27, 2002, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF CRAIGHEAD COUNT, ARKANSAS, NO. E-95-1182; HONORABLE HENRY S. WILSON AND DAVID LASER, JUDGES.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother filed a petition in the Craighead County Chancery Court, Arkansas, to terminate defendant father's visitation rights as to their only child. The father responded and filed a counterclaim. In addition, the father's parents, intervenor grandparents, filed a petition for grandparent visitation rights. The trial court denied the mother's petition to cease and restrict visitation and granted the petition for grandparent visitation.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother divorced, and the father was awarded visitation of their young daughter. He continued to have visitation with the girl for three more years. At that time, the father was found guilty of sexual abuse of his daughter. Thereafter, the trial court restricted the father's visitation to those times when his parents were physically present. The grandparents were awarded grandparent visitation rights. On appeal, the mother argued the Grandparental Visitation Rights Act, Ark. Code Ann. § 9-13-103 (Repl. 2002), was facially unconstitutional under the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses, and that the Act was unconstitutional as applied to her; alternatively, she asserted that the trial court failed to comply with the Act in awarding the grandparents visitation. The appeals court initially found that facial invalidation of the Act was inappropriate. It also found the Act did not unconstitutionally discriminate between married and divorced parents. However, because the trial court failed to apply any presumption in favor of the custodial parent's decision regarding visitation, the appeals court held that the Act was unconstitutionally applied in this case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Kemp v. State


CR 00-482


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


348 Ark. 750; 74 S.W.3d 224; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 289



May 16, 2002, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR 93-2903, HON. MARION HUMPHREY, JUDGE.
Kemp v. State, 347 Ark. 52, 60 S.W.3d 404, 2001 Ark. LEXIS 649 (Ark., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death on four counts of capital murder in the Pulaski County Circuit Court (Arkansas). After his direct appeal and resentencing, defendant filed a petition for postconviction relief under Ark. R. Crim. P. 37 which the circuit court denied. That order was appealed to the instant court and remanded to the circuit court, which again denied defendant's petition for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court: (1) rejected defendant's argument that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate the ownership of a weapon found at the crime scene because determining who owned the weapon would not have changed the outcome of the trial, and trial counsel fully developed defendant's self-defense claim that the weapon belonged to one of the victims; (2) and held that there was no rational basis for the trial court to provide a jury instruction for the "imperfect self-defense" under Ark. Code Ann. § 5-2-614 (Repl. 1997), because the evidence revealed that defendant left the crime scene, returned with a weapon, and killed the four victims, therefore, defendant could not rationally argue that he negligently formed the belief that the use of deadly force was necessary to protect himself; (3) trial counsel's failure to move to sever the four murder counts did not support a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel because the motion would not have been successful; and (4) the trial court's use of victim-impact testimony under Ark. Code Ann. 5-4-602(4) (Repl. 1997) was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The lower court's denial of defendant's petition for postconviction relief was affirmed.

Linder v. Linder


01-380


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


348 Ark. 322; 72 S.W.3d 841; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 239



April 25, 2002, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SEBASTIAN COUNTY CHANCERY COURT, NO. E-98-658 (III), HON. JIM SPEARS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, paternal grandparents, sought visitation with defendant mother's child. Visitation was granted by the Sebastian County Chancery Court, Arkansas. The mother, the maternal grandmother, and the mother's sister appealed. The State of Arkansas intervened to defend the constitutionality of the Arkansas Grandparental Visitation Act (GPVA), Ark. Code Ann. § 9-13-103 (Repl. 2002).


OVERVIEW: Prior to the death of the child's father, the paternal grandparents saw the child frequently. After the death of the child's father, the mother was resistant to allowing the paternal grandparent's visitation. The chancery court found that the mother was a fit parent, ordered that the paternal grandparents had visitation rights, and refused to allow the mother to move to another state for a job. The mother fled the jurisdiction for approximately a year, then returned and appealed the chancery court's order based on the constitutionality of the GPVA. The Arkansas Supreme Court found that: (1) the paternal grandparents' motion to dismiss the appeal due to law of the case had no merit because there was no previous judgment on an appeal; (2) res judicata did not apply to bar the appeal of a child visitation order; and (3) the GPVA was unconstitutional as applied because so long as the mother was fit to care for the child, the Fourteenth Amendment right attached, and the State could not interfere without a compelling interest to do so; there had to be some other special factor such as harm to the child or custodial unfitness that justified State interference.


OUTCOME: The paternal grandparents' motion to dismiss the appeal was denied. The judgment of the chancery court was reversed and dismissed.

White v. Priest


02-284


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


348 Ark. 135; 73 S.W.3d 572; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 191



April 10, 2002, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended. Writ of certiorari denied: White v. Priest, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 7628 (U.S. Oct. 15, 2002).



DISPOSITION: Granted in part and dismissed in part; motion to expedite granted; motion suggesting disqualification denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner individual filed a petition naming as respondents all Arkansas Supreme Court Justices, the secretary of state, the attorney general, and the state treasurer, in their official capacities along with other government departments. The individual requested a declaratory judgment concerning the secretary of state's findings that the popular names and ballot titles of his proposed initiatives were fair, accurate, and facially valid.


OVERVIEW: The individual sought a declaratory judgment finding that the ballot titles and popular names of his proposed amendments were sufficient. He had also filed a motion for recusal, wherein he requested the recusal of all supreme court justices. He seemed to suggest that the justices could be liable for illegal exactions in the nature of salaries received that exceeded caps under the amendment he proposed. The appellate court: (1) held the individual's claim for illegal exactions under Ark. Const. art. XVI, § 13, could only be commenced in a trial court and that such a suit could not be commenced in the appellate courts; (2) held that, even if the supreme court had original jurisdiction to initially consider a claim based on illegal exactions, the justices still would be empowered to consider and decide these issues under the rule of necessity; (3) refused to reconsider the individual's previous used car tax amendment that had previously been found insufficient because of its misleading popular name and ballot title; and (4) rejected the individual's remaining claims concerning the attorney general's prior rulings invalidating his previous proposed ballot initiatives.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted review of counts one and two of the individual's petition seeking review to the secretary of state's declaration that the popular name and ballot titles contained in his initiative petitions to cap salaries of state officers and a separate prison system amendment proposal were accurate and facially valid. The remaining counts in the individual's petition were dismissed.

Reinert v. State


CR 01-940


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


348 Ark. 1; 71 S.W.3d 52; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 179



March 21, 2002, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF WASHINGTON COUNTY, ARKANSAS, NO. CR 2001-420; HONORABLE WILLIAM A. STOREY, CIRCUIT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Washington County, Arkansas, for three counts of first-degree violation of a minor, his girlfriend's daughter, and sentenced accordingly. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted after his girlfriend's daughter informed her school guidance counselor that defendant had engaged in sexual intercourse with her three times. On appeal, defendant argued the statute under which he was charged, Ark. Code Ann. § 5-14-120 (1997), was void for vagueness. He further contended if § 5-14-120 was constitutional, the proof was insufficient to convict him. The appellate court initially noted a law was unconstitutionally vague under due process standards if it did not give a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice of what was prohibited. The appellate court held defendant's conduct clearly fell within that proscribed by § 5-14-120 because the evidence at trial indicated he was a guardian of the victim, thus the statute was not void for vagueness. The appellate court concluded the test for determining sufficiency of the evidence was whether substantial evidence, direct or circumstantial, supported the verdict, and found ample evidence supported the convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Garrett v. State


CR 01-923


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


347 Ark. 860; 69 S.W.3d 844; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 144



March 7, 2002, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Lonoke Circuit Court; Lance Lamar Hanshaw, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Lonoke Circuit Court, Arkansas, for driving while intoxicated (DWI), second-offense, and fined $ 400, and ordered to serve seven days in jail. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was previously convicted for DWI. At that time, Ark. Code Ann. § 5-65-111(b)(1) (Repl. 1997) provided a three-year look back period for purposes of sentencing enhancement as a habitual offender. Subsequently, the habitual offender statute was amended to provide for a five-year look back period. Thereafter, defendant was convicted for DWI, second offense, and charged as a habitual offender. On appeal, defendant argued the five-year look-back period was an unconstitutional ex post facto statute. He further asserted the extended look back period violated the Double Jeopardy Clause and did not permit a revival of his first DWI conviction. The appellate court initially noted the amendment to Ark. Code Ann. § 5-65-111 (Supp. 1999) was in effect on the date of defendant's second offense; thus, his sentence was not violative of ex post facto laws. The appellate court held defendant's second argument was not preserved for appellate review because he did not first raise the argument in the trial court. The appellate court concluded the amended statute did not inappropriately revive his prior conviction for purposes of enhancing his sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Williams v. State


No. CR 01-364


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


347 Ark. 728; 67 S.W.3d 548; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 123



February 21, 2002, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at, Appeal dismissed by Williams v. State, 2002 Ark. LEXIS 159 (Ark., Mar. 14, 2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Williams v. Norris, 80 Fed. Appx. 535, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 22956 (8th Cir. Ark., Nov. 10, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Williams v. State, 369 Ark. 104, 251 S.W.3d 290, 2007 Ark. LEXIS 177 (Ark., Mar. 1, 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Williams v. Norris, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 90570 (E.D. Ark., Oct. 31, 2008)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Remanded by Hobbs v. Jones, 2012 Ark. 293, 412 S.W.3d 844, 2012 Ark. LEXIS 309 (Ark., June 22, 2012)
Related proceeding at Lee v. Hutchinson, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 47645 (E.D. Ark., Mar. 30, 2017)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied, Request denied by, Stay denied by Williams v. Kelley, 2017 U.S. App. LEXIS 7508 (8th Cir. Ark., Apr. 27, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE LINCOLN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. LCR-99-147-3, HON. FRED D. DAVIS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Lincoln County Circuit Court (Arkansas) of capital felony murder, on the underlying felonies of first-degree escape and aggravated robbery, and the theft of property. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant escaped prison by hiding in a hog-slop tank that was hauled from the prison. He jumped from the tank and walked to the victim's home where he robbed and killed the victim. Defendant fled from the police in another state in a high-speed auto chase that resulted in defendant's vehicle colliding with another vehicle, killing the driver of that vehicle. On appeal, the supreme court found (1) the trial court improperly submitted the underlying felony of first-degree escape to the jury as defendant had already completed his escape when he killed the first victim; (2) the capital felony murder conviction was proper due to the jury's separate finding of guilt on the underlying felony of aggravated robbery; (3) defendant was properly required to wear prison garb and restraints in the presence of guards during the trial; (4) a juror was acceptable because once her nephew's murder was raised, her responses to questions cured any issue of bias; (5) evidence of the auto chase was admissible; (6) aggravators on multiple deaths and murder to avoid arrest were properly submitted; and (7) the trial court properly substituted an alternate juror without discussing it with the parties.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

395 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Banks v. Evans


01-464


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


347 Ark. 383; 64 S.W.3d 746; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 18



January 17, 2002, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF CRAIGHEAD COUNTY, ARKANSAS, NO. E-97-255, HONORABLE HOWARD TEMPLETON, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court of Craighead County, Arkansas, entered a supplemental decree of divorce in favor of appellee husband, ordering that the marital residence be sold and the proceeds distributed after the sale. Appellant wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife argued that the trial court erred in denying her request for discovery, in finding the premarital agreement to be valid, and in failing to properly distribute the marital property. Both parties expressly waived their rights to a detailed disclosure of the other's financial obligations. The agreement was accompanied by a notarized statement that the wife had read and fully understood the agreement, as well as a notarized statement by her attorney that he had explained the contract to her and advised her of her legal rights and the legal effect of the agreement. A premarital agreement could only be amended or revoked by written agreement signed by both parties, under Ark. Code Ann. § 9-11-405. The decision to postpone discovery until after the court could determine the validity of the prenuptial agreement was intended to save the time and expense of preparing answers to interrogatories and responses to requests for production of documents. Both parties owned their property as a tenancy by the entirety and had an equal right of ownership and possession. The vehicle, boat, lot, and country club membership were owned by the corporation and was not marital property.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

396 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


01-695


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


347 Ark. 409; 64 S.W.3d 728; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 22



January 17, 2002, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE WASHINGTON COUNTY JUVENILE COURT, NO. J 2001-205, HON. STACEY ZIMMERMAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was adjudicated a delinquent in the Washington County Juvenile Court (Arkansas) on the offense of terroristic threatening in the first degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant became angered when a girl in school would not reply to notes he had given her in a class. Defendant then wrote a rap lyric in which he threatened the girl and gave it to her. Defendant alleged his lyric was protected by his right to free speech. At the close of the State's case, the trial court denied defendant's motion for a directed verdict on the ground the State failed to prove the requisite intent under Ark. Code Ann. § 5-13-301 (Repl. 1997) to terrorize or cause extreme fright. On appeal, the supreme court found defendant failed to preserve the sufficiency issue for review because he did not renew his motion at the close of all the evidence. Further, because defendant's rap lyric constituted a true threat to the girl, the rap lyric was not protected by the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

397 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Ross v. State


CR 01-177


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


347 Ark. 334; 64 S.W.3d 272; 2002 Ark. LEXIS 9



January 10, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE PERRY COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR99-23, HON. MARION A. HUMPHREY, JUDGE, HON. J. LEON JOHNSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant horse owner was convicted in the municipal court of a misdemeanor violation of a requirement to have a horse testing positive for infectious anemia to be destroyed, quarantined, or permitted to a research facility. She appealed de novo to the Perry County Circuit Court (Arkansas) and was convicted. Defendant appealed her conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's horse tested positive for equine infectious anemia on the Coggins test for that illness. The issue on appeal was whether Ark. Code Ann. § 2-40-813 was unconstitutionally vague and therefore void, in violation of the due process guarantees of the United States and Arkansas Constitutions, because of the failure to define "research facility" and the failure of the State to provide a mechanism for "permitting" a horse thereto. Defendant asserted that the statute was void for vagueness, both facially and as applied, because it did not give sufficient guidance to persons on how to comply with its terms. The State asserted and the appellate court agreed that defendant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute. Defendant's actions fell squarely within the actions described by the statute in that after her horse tested positive on the Coggins test, it appeared she that failed to quarantine him. Moreover, defendant never attempted to "permit" her horse to a "research facility," which is that part of the statute she contended was vague. As such, defendant had no standing to raise the constitutional argument.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed on appeal.

 

398 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Ark. Contrs. Licensing Bd. v. Pegasus Renovation Co.


No. 01-708


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


347 Ark. 320; 64 S.W.3d 241; 2001 Ark. LEXIS 700



December 20, 2001, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SALINE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CIV 00-626-3, HON. GRISHAM PHILLIPS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Saline County Circuit Court, Arkansas, reversed appellant Arkansas Contractors Licensing Board's decision to revoke appellee renovation company's contractors license for a violation of Ark. Code Ann. § 17-25-308 (Repl. 1995), allowing revocation of a contractors license. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The board argued that the circuit court erred in finding that it had acted in an arbitrary and capricious manner based on the court's reading that "misconduct" had to affect the "physical" "public health and safety" pursuant to Ark. Code Ann. § 17-25-305(a). Ark. Code Ann. § 17-25-308, the statutory provision detailing the requirements for revocation of a contractor's license, laid out the only reasons the board could revoke a contractor's license. The statute did not state that they would be used to determine if misconduct had occurred when considering revocation. Ark. Code Ann. §§ 17-25-305 and 17-25-308 contained different provisions and requirements for different circumstances and could not be applied interchangeably. The company failed to honor three bids, one of which was an actual contract. The letters failed to attempt to work out an alternative option for resolution. The company offered no defense as to why it could not follow through on the bids. The board's decision was supported by a rational basis in that the board was bound to regulate the profession, not only the public at large, but the general contractors who relied on the subcontractors for bids.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

399 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Laime v. State


CR 01-559


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


347 Ark. 142; 60 S.W.3d 464; 2001 Ark. LEXIS 663



December 6, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied May 13, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 3265.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SALINE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR 98-391-1, HON. GRISHAM A. PHILLIPS, JR., JUDGE. Laime v. State, 73 Ark. App. 377, 43 S.W.3d 216, 2001 Ark. App. LEXIS 332 (2001) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants conditionally pleaded guilty to drug possession charges, after the trial court denied their motion to suppress. The Arkansas Court of Appeals reversed the trial court's decision, and the State sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Deciding that a van was hindering traffic, an officer called in its license plate number. He was told the van was not registered. He pulled it to the side of the road. The driver produced a valid registration for the vehicle. Defendants said they were meeting friends at a restaurant, but could not remember the names of the friends or the restaurant. A criminal background check of the driver showed drug charges, which the driver did not reveal, after being questioned. The officer asked permission to search the van, which the driver angrily denied. The officer's drug dog investigated the van, and alerted for the presence of drugs. The van was searched, revealing drugs and paraphernalia. The officer's initial information allowed him to make a valid traffic stop, even though the information was erroneous. By the time that was discovered, the totality of the circumstances, including the driver's criminal history, failure to disclose his drug arrest and charge, refusal to reveal the van's ownership, combative demeanor, and the drugs and paraphernalia gave the officer reasonable suspicion of criminal activity, authorizing further detention of the occupants, and a search of the van.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions were affirmed.

 

400 of 594 DOCUMENTS


Kemp v. State


CR00-482


SUPREME COURT OF ARKANSAS


347 Ark. 52; 60 S.W.3d 404; 2001 Ark. LEXIS 649



November 29, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Kemp v. State, 348 Ark. 750, 74 S.W.3d 224, 2002 Ark. LEXIS 289 (Ark., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE PULASKI COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, NO. CR93-2903, HON. MARION A. HUMPHREY, JUDGE.
Kemp v. State, 335 Ark. 139, 983 S.W.2d 383, 1998 Ark. LEXIS 635 (Ark., 1998)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pulaski County Circuit Court, Arkansas, denied defendant's Ark. R. Crim. P. 37 petition after defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that his counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate the ownership of a gun found at a crime scene, failing to correctly cite a statute when proffering an instruction to the trial court, failing to seek a severance of offenses, and various other grounds. The trial court allowed defendant to orally amend his Ark. R. Crim. P. 37 petition to include the issue of the ownership of the gun, and ruled on the issue from the bench. In its written order, the trial court made a general finding of fact, but did not make a specific finding of fact with respect to the factual issue, nor did it make any specific written conclusion of law with respect to the legal issue, pursuant to Ark. R. Crim. P. 37.5(i). The trial court stated that there was not a rational basis for the giving of two jury instructions, but there were not specific conclusions of law as required. The trial court also failed to provide a specific written conclusion of law concerning the issue of ineffectiveness of defendant's counsel. The trial court's order did not comply with Ark. R. Crim. P. 37.5(i) because it failed to make specific written findings of fact and conclusions of law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.
